# ART PLACEHOLDER 

## Hectic Criminal Escapades in a Retro-Futuristic Dystopia 

_lades ’68_ is a supplement for _Blades in the Dark_ , catapulting the setting forward one hundred years to 968 AC—the Swinging Sixties. A copy of B _Blades in the Dark_ is required to play. 

This supplement is about a group of daring chancers building a criminal enterprise on the streets of a retro-futuristic dystopia. There’s espionage, heists, chases, escapes, dangerous bargains, shoot-outs, deceptions, betrayals, victories, and deaths. 

We play to find out if the fledgling crew can thrive amidst the teeming threats of rival gangs, scheming spy agencies, paranormal entities, the corrupt Bluecoats, and the irresistible pull of the scoundrels’ own vices. 

## **The Basics** 

The game takes place in Doskvol, an important city at the crossroads of the world. It is a city steeped in dark history (see _Blades in the Dark_ ), but if you’re not so familiar with that history, don’t worry—most people on the street don’t know or care that much about history either. The future is now. 

The world is similar to our own in the **1960s** or early 1970s. There are cars, phones, airships, early computers, TV shows, movies, and fast food restaurants. It’s crowded with buildings both old and new, twisting streets and busy new motorways, all criss-crossed with hundreds of canals and bridges. 

The world is also **fantastical** . The sun was destroyed in a cataclysm a thousand years ago, and strange paranormal entities haunt the deathlands between cities. Most cities are protected by a Bubble, a force field that keeps out the horrors of the deathlands, as well as providing artificial daylight to replace the broken sun. 

1 

## **Welcome to the Age of Consensus** 

If you and your players are familiar with _Blades in the Dark_ , you might want to know how we got here. 

After the leviathans went away, there was a dark period of history. The lightning towers began to fail, and frightened people went to war. There was Unity War II, and then Unity War III. Now the Imperium as we once knew it no longer exists—Iruvia and Skovlan are their own world powers, while Severos and the Dagger Isles still struggle for full independence from the other nations. 

As Unity War III came to an end, electroplasmic fusion was invented. Every major city of the Shattered Isles became wrapped in a Bubble, with all the reality-warping danger of the deathlands kept safely out. 

Superstition is a thing of the past—this is the Age of Consensus. This is a time of science, rationality, conformity, consumerism, and peace. 

Or at least, it was. 

The horrors of the past may be buried, but only under a thin layer of soil. Progress is here, but only for some. War may be over, but the shadowy game of espionage has never been more heated. Discontent bubbles under the surface and threatens to erupt at any time, in any place. 

They’ve tried to tell you that the future has arrived and everything is fine now, that it’s not the time to make a fuss. But you know better. You’re a scoundrel, a chancer, a troublemaker. You know the streets and you’re not afraid of danger. The moment is now, everything you’ve dreamed of is within reach. 

## **Bluetime** 

A shining symbol of the promise of the future is the B.L.U.E. Array, an experimental apparatus that “tunes” Doskvol’s Bubble like a plasmovision set, providing several hours of blue skies and genuine daylight every day (along with a few hours of psychedelic colors in the sky, as the device powers up or down). 

This is better than the giant glorified lightbulb that blazes over the Imperial City; this is the real deal, a real blue sky, a real sun. How it works is a matter of some conjecture. Is it focusing the shards of the sun like a magnifying glass, or is it projecting a perfect simulacrum, or is it opening a window to another place, or even another time? 

These are questions for eggheads. What matters is that daylight is back, baby, and cashed-up tourists are flocking to Doskvol to soak up the rays. 

2 

## **Characters** 

There are eight core playbooks to choose from, each representing a different style of criminal operator: 

- **Hulls** are robots powered by a human soul, slowly recovering their memories. 

- **Hounds** are hard-bitten fixers, good at following leads. 

- **Intellectuals** are engineers, scientists, and philosophers. 

- **Operatives** are stealthy espionage professionals. 

- **Paranormalists** are maverick thinkers and occult experts. 

- **Radicals** are agitators, skilled at both persuasion and explosives. 

- **Swingers** are wheelers and dealers. 

- **Veterans** are former soldiers, capable but scarred. 

## **The Crew** 

In addition to creating characters, you’ll also create the crew by choosing which type of criminal enterprise you’re interested in exploring: 

- **Dealers** sell illegal products. 

- **Hit Squads** are killers for hire. 

- **Militants** are revolutionary activists. 

- **Racers** are thrill-seekers and daredevils. 

- **Shadows** specialize in heists and espionage. 

- **Utopians** are an esoteric cult. 

3 

## Using This Book 

You don’t have to read this book from front to back. Each chapter is summarized here—jump to whichever section you’re most excited about. 

## **Characters (page 11) and Crews (page 86)** 

Character creation and the core playbooks, followed by crew creation and the core crews. Start here for a new campaign, but if this is your first time reading the book, you can just skim through. 

## **System Changes (page 150)** 

This chapter outlines the new mechanics of _Blades ’68,_ which differ from core _Blades in the Dark_ . 

## **The Gameplay Cycle (page 162)** 

- **Personal Business (page 164):** Downtime activities and free play. 

- **Planning Meeting (page 180):** The table collaborates to decide on the next score. 

- **The Score (page 188):** Approach, loadout, and engagement roll. 

- **Aftermath (page 190):** Fallout from the score, including payout, Rep, Heat, faction status changes, and harm complications. Ends with an unwind scene. 

## **Special Procedures (page 196)** 

- **The Trouble Engine (p. 197):** The GM rolls for entanglements and other trouble, between sessions. This chapter doesn’t need to be read in-depth until you’re ready to use it. 

- **Wanted Levels and Prison (p. 216):** During the aftermath of a score, the crew might gain Wanted Levels—and a PC might go to prison. This doesn’t need to be read in-depth until such events occur in your game. 

- **Time Skips (p. 228):** Sometimes you’ll interrupt the gameplay cycle with a time skip. This might be to skip over a prison sentence, but can occur for a number of other reasons too. Refer to this section when it occurs. 

- **Raids (page 234):** Sometimes, usually as a result of the Trouble Engine, the PCs find themselves defending against a raid by another faction. 

- **Backing Factions (page 236):** Gaining a backing faction, using their help, rolling Return the Favor, and prestige abilities. 

4 

## **Running the Game (page 242)** 

A guide to the various handouts available, as well as some general GM and player advice. 

- **Cold Opens (p. 256):** Short score openers that you may wish to use when starting a campaign, _in medias res_ . 

- **Ticking Timebombs (p. 272):** Optional background situations that complicate the PCs’ lives over the course of a campaign, providing narrative stakes for their criminal activities. 

## **The Setting (page 300)** 

- **Doskvol ’68 (p. 301):** An overview of the history, technology, geopolitics, culture, and food of Doskvol in the current time period. None of this is required reading—read it if you find it interesting, but otherwise consider it supplementary material that’s just there in case it’s helpful. 

- **The Paranormal (p. 324):** A guide to common attitudes toward the occult, the categories of paranormal entities, Section 6 and the Death Radar, and optional paranormal playbooks. 

- **Faction Rolodex (p. 342):** All the factions of Doskvol, starting with a high-level summary followed by detailed descriptions. Like the setting information, only read this if you find it interesting—otherwise, just dip into specific faction write-ups if they come up in the game and you want some inspiration. 

- **Districts (p. 387):** A guide to the 15 districts of Doskvol, with locations of interest, key NPCs, etc. Not required reading, but may be helpful when the PCs visit a particular district or plan a score there. 

## **Appendix (page 418)** 

- **Score Rolodex (p. 418):** An assortment of random tables for locations and score types, including items of interest, potential obstacles, and sensory impressions to draw from, as well as some potential threats. Useful for both improvising as well as planning a score. 

5 

## Touchstones 

“The 1960s” encompasses a wide variety of genres, moods, and aesthetics. To help you understand what _Blades ’68_ is trying to do, to get inspired before playing, and to pitch it to others, here is a collection of media touchstones. This not an exhaustive list, and you should pull in whatever else inspires you—make ’68 your own.

## Tone and Content 

## **Tone** 

_Blades ’68_ can encompass a wide tonal range, from silly, colorful adventures at one end of the spectrum, to tense, paranoid spy conspiracies at the other extreme. Most games are somewhere in the middle. 

When you sit down to play a new game, it’s worth discussing the desired tone to ensure you’re all on the same page. If anyone has strong feelings for or against either extreme, it’s best to talk about that before you begin. 

## **Making ’68 More Colorful** 

- Bluetime lasts for as long as a regular day in our world, and it’s always a bright blue sky. The world is literally vibrant and colorful. 

- The horrors of the deathlands and the paranormal are mostly forgotten, and/or more ridiculous and campy when they do appear. 

- Anomalous effects like anti-gravity and time-travel are frequent and may be comical. 

## **Making ’68 More Serious** 

- Bluetime is erratic in length, and could be as little as one or two hours at noon. It does provide daylight, but the weather is more often gray and rainy than blue skies. 

- The rest of the time, the world is a dark, dreary place. It rains a lot. 

- The paranormal is dark and unsettling. It has been suppressed, at great effort by the authorities, but it only becomes more threatening when hidden in the shadows. 

- Anomalies are rare, and their effects are unsettling. Those who experience their effects question the very nature of reality, and Section 6 works to erase any mention from the public record, and wipes the memories of witnesses. 

Adjust these dials to suit the tastes of everyone playing. Give yourself permission to adjust these settings as your campaign continues. 

8 

## **Content** 

In our world, the 1960s were a time when many awful prejudices were commonplace, including rampant sexism, racism, ableism, and so on. 

This does not have to be the case in the world of _Blades ’68_ . Use safety and communication tools of your choice (see the next section) to explore which of these prejudices you wish to include and explore, and which you would rather avoid. If in doubt, leave the bigotry off-screen. 

The world of _Blades_ is dark, in more ways than one, and the default assumption is that the following things are true. You can and should change any of this at your own table (especially when aiming for a lighter tone). 

- Inequality and classism are both deeply entrenched. 

- Hulls experience a complete lack of personal autonomy. 

- There are common prejudices against Tycherosi and Skovs. 

- There is a Consensus embraced by the comfortable middle class that emphasizes conformity and consumerism. 

- The Imperium intentionally destabilizes other nations, interferes with their governments, and uses its large military to impose its will and safeguard its access to important resources. 

All these conditions are in the process of being challenged, and are the subject of protests, riots, and general resistance. 

## **Communication Tools** 

As part of agreeing on tone and content, decide which communication tools (or safety tools) you wish to use. Common choices include the X-Card, Lines and Veils, and others. Any of these can be found with a quick internet search. 

You might find the Palette Grid, by Jay Dragon, useful. This tool plots areas of concern on a grid, with one axis for risky/comfortable and one for explore/ ignore. It allows for a more nuanced discussion around what you want to ignore, carefully explore, or fully embrace. 

9 

## ART PLACEHOLDER 

10 

## Character Creation 

## **Choose a Playbook** 

The playbooks are: 

A hard-bitten fixer who’s good at following leads, **Hound** talking to people, and sticking their nose where it doesn’t belong. Play a Hound if you want to get by on instinct and persistence. Hulls are a human soul powering a robot body, **Hull** with no memory of their former life. Play a Hull if you want to slowly discover who you once were. Intellectuals are polymaths; scientists, engineers, **Intellectual** and philosophers. Play an Intellectual if you want to solve problems by inventing clever solutions. Operatives are good at sneaking around and **Operative** breaking into places. Play an Operative if you want to be a shadowy espionage professional. Paranormalists are good at dealing with the **Paranormalist** paranormal. Play a Paranormalist if you want to meddle with the weird and supernatural. Radicals care deeply about a cause, and are good **Radical** at blowing stuff up. Play a Radical if you want to change the world or die trying. Swingers are good at social situations and **Swinger** improvising. Play a Swinger if you want to live fast and have fun. An ex-military veteran from one of the many on- **Veteran** going wars in this “era of peace.” Play a Veteran if you want to be good at violence but weighed down by the scars of your past. 

11 

## **Choose a Heritage** 

Your character’s **heritage** describes where their family line is from. You may be of any heritage of your choice, and then decide if you’re a foreigner who has immigrated to Doskvol or if you’re a local who grew up here. 

When you choose a heritage, circle it on the list on your playbook, then write a detail about your family life on the line above. Examples are listed below each heritage. 

## **Akoros** 

Formerly the heart of the Imperium; now the Imperium consists of little else. The people are a conglomeration of cultures that have grown together in close proximity for centuries, along with many diverse immigrant communities. 

_Government civil servants—Union-strong factory workers in Coalridge— Farmers in Barrowcleft—Clergy within the Church of Ecstasy— Academics working in Charterhall University—A proud line of Rail Jacks, fallen on hard times—Office workers, the model Age of Consensus family_ 

## **The Dagger Isles** 

A tropical archipelago covered in dense jungle growth. The Dagger Isles are a region of small nation-states known as banyans. The Imperium and the USC fight many of their proxy wars via the Dagger Isles, covertly supporting revolutionary and counterrevolutionary groups, and sending in troops to tip the balance when needed. Some of the banyans are little more than puppet regimes as a result, but others remain (as they have always been) independent and self-determining. They fight tooth and nail against this Imperial interference. 

_Bonewalkers, devoted to the intertwining realms of life and death_ — _Lhan Lhaban merchants_ — _Biringan revolutionaries_ — _Refugees_ — — _Melamatine shadow puppeteers Fishing trawler crew— Members of an island commune_ — _Couriers_ 

12 

## **Iruvia** 

A major world power, occupying the desert region to the south. Iruvia was the first nation to secede from the Imperium, and later fought to support the secession of Skovlan. That war ended with the creation of the Null Zone, wiping out both South Point in Akoros and Bright Harbor in Iruvia. Since then, Iruvia has entered an isolationist period, allowing a small amount of trade with the outside world via Mistport and the Dagger Isles. 

_City Guardians—Political exiles—Diplomats—Business magnates— Couriers—Water Bearers—Performers—Restaurant owners—Teachers_ 

## **Severos** 

A land of windswept plains. Severos was the first to join the Imperium, and although it is now an “independent protectorate,” the tendrils of Akoros are deeply embedded. The ruling class send their children to Akorosi schools, and Akorosi corporations extract the profit from the nation’s factories and farms. There is a movement for radical egalitarianism and redistribution of wealth, particularly in the south. 

_Bastion Elders—Irondale factory workers—Railworkers—Butchers—_ — _Tailors—Taxi drivers—Dry cleaners—Severosi government bureaucrats Refugees_ 

## **Tycheros** 

Tycheros is connected to the rest of the Shattered Isles by a Void Gate, a portal-like device that allows rail lines to pass through the resonance field. Tycherosi are rudely called “Visitors,” and sometimes treated like space aliens. Any talk of demon blood is, of course, a relic of the superstitious past. If you choose Tycherosi heritage, also create an alien telltale that marks your character (e.g. green or blue skin, a large cranium, antennae, scales, claws, glowing eyes, webbed feet, gills, metallic skin, etc.). 

_Scientists—Confessors—Paranormal scholars—Steelhands—Diplomats— Political exiles—Bookstore owners—Translators_ 

13 

## **The United Skov Covenant** 

Skovlan finally achieved independence with Unity War III, forming the United Skov Covenant. Local communities elect ruling covens, who send delegates to the High Coven in Lockport. Despite dealing with the legacy of centuries of colonization, as well as the intergenerational physical and mental trauma caused by leviathan blood processing, Skovlan has quickly established itself as a world power. The USC works tirelessly to overtake its nemesis, Akoros. Doskvol has a large population of first-, second-, and third-generation Skovs; they struggle with oppression, distrust, and conflicting loyalties. 

_Midwives—Whispers—Blackvale Coven—Revolutionaries— Exiled Imperial collaborators—Dockhands—Shipbreakers—Miners— Laundry workers—Musicians_ 

## **Choose a Background** 

Your character’s **background** describes what they did _before_ they joined the crew. Choose one of the general background options from the list on your playbook, then write a detail about it that’s specific to your character. For example, you could choose **Labor** and write _Short order cook, recently fired_ . Or you might choose **Professional** and write _Advertising copywriter_ . The following are more examples: 

- **Learned.** A professor or student (from the ivy-clad campus of Doskvol Academy or the incendiary lecture halls of Charterhall University), journalist, priest, librarian, experimental psychologist. 

- **Underworld.** A street kid, gang member, hustler, pickpocket, cultist, dealer, fence. 

- **Performer.** An artist, poet, lounge singer, racer, painter, guitarist, filmmaker, dancer, model, experimental sound collage artist, stage magician, playwright. 

- **Trade.** A sparktech, plumber, autopod mechanic, record shop owner, tattooist, salesperson, street vendor, projectionist. 

- **Professional.** A lawyer, office clerk, accountant, architect, terminal programmer, advertising executive, claims adjuster, civil servant, PR agent. 

- **Aristocrat.** Old money, nobility, dilettante, scion of a fallen house, new money with aspirations, socialite. 

- **Military.** A soldier, officer, mercenary, intelligence operative, strategist, radar operator, medic, R&D scientist, engineer. 

- **Labor.** A factory worker, janitor, dock worker, cab driver, bellhop, waiter, short order cook, farmhand, garbage collector. 

**Some playbooks choose a different aspect of their past instead of a standard background, such as a Veteran’s tours of duty or an Intellectual’s field of study.** See the relevant playbook section for details. 

14 

## **Choose Keys** 

Keys are personality traits that are central to who your character is, both as a person and as a criminal scoundrel, such as _charming_ , _eccentric_ , or _stubborn_ . They help you roleplay your character, and they’re a source of xp. 

You can have up to four keys, but you don’t need all four to start—perhaps start with two or three. You can define more as you work out exactly who this person is in play. 

There are key ideas at the bottom of each playbook sheet; use these, or use ones from another playbook sheet, or make up your own. 

Keys may become deadlocks, and each key lists two potential deadlocks. One is where the key is reversed, and the other is where it’s intensified. For example: 

**Hopeful** _(_[▼] _Cynical_[▲] _Content)_ 

Note that in this example, one of the suggested deadlocks is a positive trait ( _content_ ). Deadlocks hinder your character _as a criminal_ ; sometimes a positive, well-adjusted trait can be the worst kind of hindrance to a life of crime. 

## **Special Resources** 

Every playbook has their own special resource that they can use twice per score to resist consequences or push themselves in particular situations, such as _training_ , _tenacity_ , or _research_ . These are the equivalent of Special Armor in _Blades in the Dark_ . 

Accessing the resource requires the associated special ability, such as the Veteran’s _Military Discipline_ , or the Hound’s _Dogged Persistence_ . If you take the equivalent ability from another playbook as a versatile advance, you may gain multiple special resources. Track them each separately. 

## **Continue Character Creation** 

Follow the rest of the character creation steps from _Blades in the Dark_ (page 54): **add one action dot each for your heritage and background** , select a **special ability** , choose your **friend** and **rival** , pick your **vice** , detail your **look** , and create a **name** . 

15 

## **Vice Purveyors** 

**Faith** (dedication to the church, a new age cult, etc.)

## **Hull Looks** 

Sleek, chrome, racing stripe, polished, chipped paint, pastel paint, geometric, utilitarian, elegant, boxy, bulky, heavy, delicate, high-tech, clunky, wood paneling, friendly, inhuman, bulbous, hard-edged, intimidating, exposed wires, curly cord, antennae, painted unit designation number, blinking light, graffiti, rust 

## **Hull Wearing** 

Nothing, a jumpsuit or high-vis vest, a uniform from your owning faction. _As you remember your former life, do you start to wear human clothing? See the “Wearing” list on the next page._

## **Standard Items** 

**A Blade or Two:** Perhaps you carry a butterfly knife. Or a big military-issue combat knife. Or a heavy butcher’s cleaver. Or a machete. **1 load.** 

**Silenced Shooter:** A semi-automatic handgun with a modest caliber. Quiet as a whisper. **1 load.** 

**Handcannon:** A heavy, large-bore handgun that hits like a sledgehammer. Loud. Slow to reload. **1 load.** 

**Electro-Blade:** A broad, heavy blade with a plasmoleum-powered device built into the hilt. If the sharpened edge doesn’t finish them, the explosive release of electricity will. **2 load.** 

**Pump-Action Scattergun:** A simple but very effective firearm that delivers blasts of shot over short distances. Developed for use in the narrow streets and cramped alleyways of modern cities. **2 load.** 

**Armor:** Layers of impact-resistant fabric combined with areas of rigid plate. Bulky and uncomfortable, but offers unparalleled protection. **3 load.** _**See page 153 for more on how armor works in**_ **Blades ’68** _**.**_ 

**Burglary Gear:** A set of lockpicks. A small pry-bar. A cannister of lubricant to silence squeaky hinges. A spool of high-tensile wire and a set of powerful magnets. A small pouch of fine sand. A glass cutter. **1 load.** 

**Climbing Gear:** A large coil of nylon rope. Grappling hooks. A small pouch of chalk dust. A climbing harness with loops and carabiners. A set of steel pitons and a small mallet. Suction cups. **2 load.** 

**Paranormal Implements:** A resonance gauge for monitoring resonance field activity. An infrared thermometer. An echo frequency scanner. A small mirror. A vial of ultraplasm. A portable echo containment unit. A resonance disruptor. Safety goggles and gloves. **1 load.** 

**Documents:** A folder of paperwork on a variety of topics, including a registry of the nobility, Bluecoat commanders, and other notable citizens. Blank pages, a pen. A number of interesting maps. Some relevant printouts of archival information, prepared before the score. **1 load.** 

**Subterfuge Supplies:** A disguise kit. A selection of blank documents, ready for the forger’s hand. Invisible ink. A forged ID card. Microfilm camera. **1 load.** 

**Demolition Tools:** A heavy drill. A crowbar. Explosive putty and blasting caps. Thermite charges. Vials of acid. A sledgehammer. A blowtorch. **2 load.** 

**Tinkering Tools:** Tools and spare parts for messing with electronics and mechanisms. A wrench, drill, and spanner. Tweezers, pliers, precision screwdrivers. A soldering iron. Oscilloscope, circuit tester, and heat sink. Jumper wires. A magnifying loupe. **1 load.** 

20 

**Arclighter:** A handheld tool that carries a small reserve of plasmoleum. A flick of the thumb produces a small arc of crackling energy, and with a twist of the dial, it turns into a steady beam of light. Used as a flashlight, cigarette lighter, welding torch, or for anything from supercharging firearm rounds, overloading electronic systems, or even jamming into a knife’s hilt to jury-rig a quick electro-blade. **1 load.** 

## **Playbook Cohorts** 

Many playbooks start with their own cohort, such as the Intellectual’s sparkmind assistant, the Hound’s pet, or the Swinger’s autopod. 

Playbook cohorts cannot do secondary scores, but otherwise they can do the things crew cohorts can do—work on long-term projects, take part in group action rolls, and perform tasks by themselves if applicable (with a fortune roll). The fiction comes first, as always. For example, the Swinger’s autopod might be able to work on a long-term project of impressing the local populace, simply by being seen, but it isn’t sentient and couldn’t study documents by itself. 

## _**See page 93 for full cohort rules.**_ 

21 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0033-01.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Consort  INSTINCTS<br>Survey<br>THEIR<br> FOLLOWS<br>HARD-BITTEN FIXER<br>Hound A  WHO<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


The Hound is one of the oldest callings in the Imperium. There’s always been a need for scoundrels who can find what others want to keep hidden, who can find a fix for a bad situation. Whether it’s a washed-up boxer with a missing brother, a two-timing business partner plotting a deadly doublecross, or a stash of diamonds gone missing from a high-stakes heist—it’s a Hound that will follow the trail. 

Hounds already make their living in the seedy underbelly of society, so it’s not unusual that they find themselves in a criminal crew. They know how to take a punch and they’re good at asking questions until they get the right answers—useful skills to any outfit. 

**When you play a Hound, you earn xp when you address a challenge with talking or determination.** Follow your hunches, stick your nose where it doesn’t belong, and don’t be afraid to shake the tree. You never know what will fall out. 

**23** 

## **Loyal, Clever Pet** 

You start with a playbook cohort, a loyal and clever pet. Give them a name, edges, and flaws like any cohort. Your pet functions as an **Expert: Hunter** . As an expert cohort, their Quality is equal to crew Tier +1 when their **type** , or area of expertise (Hunter), applies to the situation at hand. 

_The Hound wants to have their pet (a falcon) fly ahead and search the streets for a fleeing target, from above. The crew is Tier 1 and the pet’s type (Hunter) applies in this context, so they make a 2d fortune roll to see how successful the falcon is._ 

Playbook cohorts can take actions themselves, such as in the previous example. Cohorts can also join in group actions, and they can help during downtime in various ways (see **Cohorts** on page 96 for more detail). Playbook cohorts cannot perform secondary scores. 

What kind of pet does your Hound have? _Perhaps a hound dog, mastiff, lap dog, rat dog, cat, crow, falcon, owl, snake, ferret, eel, monkey, fox, goat, pigeon, pig, rooster, rabbit, large beetle, large moth._

Choose from these keys, or use them as inspiration and pick your own. Each includes two possible deadlocks as examples—one where the key is flipped to its opposite[▼] , and one where it’s intensified[▲] . 

- **Sardonic** ([▼] Grim[▲] Witty) 

- **Cynical** ([▼] Optimistic[▲] Nihilist) 

- **Romantic** ([▼] Cynical[▲] Lovestruck) 

- **Bitter** ([▼] Affable[▲] Vindictive) 

- **Lonely** ([▼] Social[▲] Loner) 

- **Determined** ([▼] Laid-Back[▲] Obsessed) 

- **Suspicious** ([▼] Trusting[▲] Paranoid) 

- **Tired** ([▼] Rejuvenated[▲] Defeated) 

- **Sharp** ([▼] Dulled[▲] Searing)

## **Shady Friends** 

Choose **two close friends** (instead of one as usual), and one rival. 

- **Vanden** , a lazy Bluecoat. _Perhaps a useful source who gives you tip-offs, or a beat officer who’s tired of your shit?_ 

- **Mira** , a nightclub owner. _Perhaps a previous paramour—does a flame still burn, or has it turned to bitterness?_ 

- **Hendrik** , a veterinarian. _Perhaps someone who’ll patch you up without asking too many questions, or a local busybody who disapproves of your lifestyle?_ 

- **Chatterley** , a secret agent. _Perhaps a fellow hound recruited by a spy agency, or a cold manipulator who sees you as a disposable tool?_ 

- **Zam** , a street kid. _Perhaps just a kid who wants to be a hound one day, or a punk who enjoys messing with you?_ 

## **Hound Items** 

- **Fine snub-nosed handcannon:** Maybe you’re no great shot, but this thing packs a hell of a punch and can be concealed in a pocket. **1 load.** 

- **A loyal, clever pet:** Companion might be a better word—a hunter. They never let you down (except when they do). Did you choose them, or did they choose you? _(Cohort, Expert: Hunter)._ 

- **Binoculars:** See distant objects with greater clarity and detail. Amazing. **1 load.** 

- **Hipflask of the good stuff:** Numb pain, clean wounds, or bond with new friends. What’s engraved on the flask? **0 load.** 

- **Pocketful of focus pills:** For when you need steady hands, an alert mind, and laser-like concentration. _Very addictive (this can be resisted)._ **0 load.** 

- **RF radio handset:** A resonance field radio. A small handheld unit tuned to a secure frequency. **0 load.** 

25 

## **Hound Special Abilities** 

## **HOUND’S INSTINCTS** 

When you **push yourself** , you can also do one of the following: _figure out where_ — _to go next, even with zero leads make someone stop and listen to you for a few moments, no matter how unlikely it is._ 

_When you push yourself to activate this ability, you still get one of the normal benefits of pushing yourself (+1d or +1 effect) in addition to the special ability. This kind of ability lets you do something that most characters can’t, but a roll might still be required if there is a threat or obstacle (as usual)._ 

_The first use of this ability gives you a path forward based purely on instinct, no matter how little hard evidence you have to go on. A roll may not even be required._ 

_The second use gives you an opening for a conversational approach no matter what the context is—even in the middle of a life-or-death fight against a sworn enemy, for example._ 

## **LEARN THE HARD WAY** 

Whenever you take harm, clear an amount of Stress equal to the harm level, and it counts as a successful **gather information** roll (with a level of detail equal to the harm level). The GM will tell you what you learn. 

_This ability is based on the harm taken_ _**after** any armor/resistance rolls, not before—it’s based on whatever harm level you write down on your sheet._ 

_Level 3 harm means exceptional details; the information is complete and followup questions may expand into related areas or reveal more than you hoped for. Level 2 harm means good details; clarifying and follow-up questions are possible. Level 1 harm means a cryptic clue; incomplete or partial information._ 

_Unlike a regular gather information roll, you don’t have to ask a specific question (although you might). The GM can simply suggest something that you learn, possibly by pure luck. The information should either help the Hound with the current score, assist in personal business, or open up a new opportunity._ 

_Work together to establish how the information comes out. It could come directly from the source of the harm, but it might also just be luck. For example, it could be something said by your assailant as they throw a punch, but it could also be that you notice a clue underneath the sofa while you lying bleeding on the ground._ 

_If the GM is stumped for information to give, consider the Faction Rolodex (page 342)—a faction’s secrets, quirks, projects, enemies, and allies are all useful types of intel._ 

26 

## **JUST A SCRATCH** 

Harm doesn’t slow you down during a score, and never factors into effect (level 4 harm is still fatal, and you still roll for harm complications). You gain **potency** when you **Consort** with someone who has caused you to mark harm. 

_Make sure you still record harm for the purposes of harm complications and recovery. You should still portray the injuries in your descriptions—this ability doesn’t erase them, but represents your Hound gritting their teeth and pushing through no matter what. Nothing slows them down._ 

## **FIXER** 

During downtime, you get **+1 result level** when you **Acquire Asset** or **Reduce Heat** . When incarcerated, take +1d to all real time prison rolls, or take +2d to a prison time skip roll. 

_Your array of underworld connections can be leveraged to loan assets, pressure a vendor to give you a better deal, intimidate witnesses, etc. Note that prison can be handled in two ways, in real time or with a time skip—see page 218 for more details._ 

## **IN TOO DEEP** 

Once per score, you can **Consort** with an NPC to form an intimate bond. If you have such a bond with someone involved in a score, you get + **1d** and **potency** to any actions dealing with them. 

_This ability only works with Consort, not Sway—it’s about forming a genuine connection, not manipulating people. It’s up to you to roleplay these connections. This ability can be a powerful advantage if used against hostile people, enemy factions, or anyone in your way. The only downside is that it creates a complex web of emotional investments_ — _but is that really a downside?_ 

## **ECHO PET** 

Your pet is imbued with anomalous resonance. It gains **potency** when tracking or fighting the paranormal, and gains a paranormal ability: _time-glitching, mind-link,_ or _mirror-field_ . Take this ability again to choose an additional paranormal ability for your pet. 

_This ability gives your pet potency when against paranormal targets, and a paranormal ability of your choice. Time-glitching means the pet can jump timelines, suddenly appearing in a difference place entirely as though they teleported a short distance, or allowing them to move extremely quickly. Mind-link allows the pet and owner to share their senses and thoughts telepathically. Mirror-field lets the pet blend into their surroundings perfectly, rendering them nearly invisible as light bends around their form._ 

27 

## **DOGGED PERSISTENCE** 

Twice per score, you may use your **tenacity** to resist a consequence of exhaustion or mental harm (fear, confusion, losing track of someone) or to **push yourself** for influencing someone or searching for clues. 

_When you use this ability, tick one of the tenacity boxes on your sheet. If you resist a consequence of the appropriate type, you might avoid it completely, or you might reduce it by one (such as harm, or a clock ticking), as per resistance as usual. If you use this ability to push yourself, you get one of the benefits (+1d, +1 effect) but you don’t take 2 Stress. Your tenacity uses are restored at the beginning of downtime._ 

## **Hound Questions** 

After crew creation and character creation, your group can run through background questions together. Take turns introducing your characters, and then take turns asking the group one of the following questions (your choice), or make up your own question. 

Anyone can answer, and together you can flesh out some of the details. 

- Which of you is an old friend? 

- Which of you carried me home, unconscious? 

- Which of you once came to me as a client, with a case? 

- Which of you does my pet like more than it likes me? 

- Which of you shares my taste in music? 

- Which of you poured out your sorrows to me at the bar last week? 

Then go around again—ask another question from the list, or pass. When everyone has passed, move on to crew questions. 

28 

29 

## Hull 

## **Skirmish Attune** 

## **THE SOUL OF A CONDEMNED CRIMINAL TRAPPED IN A ROBOT BODY** 

You are the product of the experimental new “Lusk Reform Technique.” This procedure takes hardened criminals and turns them into “the Reformed”; vacant-eyed, compliant members of society. A byproduct is that the criminal’s resonance echo, their psychic imprint, is used to power a hull that can work off the criminal’s debt to society. 

You are one such hull, but there is something wrong with you. You are defective, faulty, recidivist. You were meant to be a robotic automaton that works tirelessly for the betterment of society, but you’ve fallen back into your old criminal lifestyle. 

You’re starting to remember. 

**When you play a Hull, you earn xp when you obey orders, or address a challenge with cold simplicity.** 

30 

31 

## **Hull Character Creation** 

You start with no memory of your former human life. Your human feelings, interests, and connections are almost entirely gone. 

**1.** You start with no background or heritage, so assign four action dots wherever you want. Unlike most playbooks, Hulls start play with six action dots instead of seven. 

**2.** You start with the Hull trait _Automaton_ (see the next page). Pick one more trait to start with. Note that Hull traits cannot be taken as versatile advances by other playbooks. 

**3.** You do not start with either friends or rivals. You have one contact, who is your controller from your owning faction. Your controller is responsible for giving you orders and setting you to work. 

**4.** You do not indulge vice, so skip this step. See _Drain_ and _Fuel_ , on the next page. 

**5.** You start with no keys, so make sure you hit your xp triggers ( _you obeyed orders or addressed a challenge with cold simplicity_ ) to keep up with the other PCs. 

**6.** Record your hull designation, alias (what the crew calls you), look, and wearing (if anything). See page 18 for hull-specific examples of each of these. 

## **Owning Faction** 

You lead a double life. Some of the time, you do the work of a laboring automaton for an owning faction. The rest of the time, you live a free life, pursuing your own goals and remembering who you once were. 

Choose an owning faction, or the GM can suggest one. Most hulls made this way end up working for the government or the city, but many are also purchased by corporations, and some end up in criminal hands. Some examples of owning factions and their typical program duties: 

- **Bluecoats.** Street patrols, traffic monitoring. 

- **City Council.** Street cleaning, garbage detail, roadworks, sewer detail. 

- **Ministry of Stability.** Nutriwafer delivery, crowd control, rail security, Gaddoc Station duties. 

- **Corporation.** Cleaning windows, moving cargo, data entry, office security. 

- **Criminal gang.** Smash and grabs, stealing autopods, intimidating rivals. 

Your owners see you as a piece of hardware, no different than a delivery truck, bulldozer, or telephone. They have no reason to suspect that when they shut off the lights and leave their hulls powered down in a concrete lot, you power back up, hop the fence, and meet up with your friends and criminal associates. 

32 

— _How do you hide your double life from your owning faction are you just one more machine overlooked in the multitude, or do you have some personal arrangement with your controller?_ 

_What makes them overlook your wear and tear after a score_ — _is it normal for your category of hull, or do you have a particularly absent-minded controller, or do you have some way of hiding it?_ 

## **Automaton** 

You have human-like strength and senses, by default. Your frame has built-in **armor** (this doesn’t count for your load). If you total your armor during a score, it gets replaced during any Recover (Hull Repair) downtime activity (the same downtime activity can also add ticks to your repair clock if needed). 

You may be repaired if damaged or even destroyed (level 4 harm). Choose two frame features to start with. 

## **Drain** 

Instead of Stress, you now take **Drain** . You have 10 Drain boxes. Whenever you would take Stress, take Drain instead. 

## **Fuel** 

Your frame runs on electroplasmic power. Recharge your capacitors by connecting to an industrial-grade generator (this takes one **downtime activity** ). When you do this, clear **5 Drain** . 

## **On Program** 

During the personal business phase, spend a **downtime action** going **ON PROGRAM** . In this state, you do the work assigned by your controller. The GM will tell you what you did. This might represent one shift of work, or a montage of multiple days of work. This work should start as meaningless drudgery, but you might discover that your work for your owning faction becomes more complicated and compromised as time goes on. 

Each personal business phase that you skip going On Program, tick the “Suspicion” clock. When full, your owning faction will take steps against you, including cutting you off from their industrial-grade generator. They may raid your base to try and reclaim you. 

Will you find some other way to recharge? Will you remember who you were? Can you get free from your owning faction one day? 

Note that going On Program is essentially a wasted downtime action, since it doesn’t include any other benefits (except maybe an insight into the actions and motivations of the controlling faction). 

Usually, the “Suspicion” clock does not tick backward, but your GM could allow it to tick backward _sometimes_ to give the Hull more leeway in how they 

33 

use their downtime actions. The GM should also consider how harsh the consequence is for a full “Suspicion” clock—a minor consequence (like losing access to the generator for one downtime) or a major consequence (like the controlling faction locks up the Hull character). Lighter consequences give the Hull more leeway to skip going On Program. Have this conversation between GM and the Hull’s player to ensure the character still gets to enjoy downtime. 

Hulls also have their own **harm complications** on page 192. 

## **Memory Clocks** 

Whenever you would mark xp (from end-of-session triggers, desperate actions, zero-dot actions, or hitting a key), you can tick a memory clock instead. Each memory clock is eight segments. 

**Memory pacing:** If you’re running a shorter campaign, let the Hull’s player fill in two ticks on every memory clock, making them 6-segment clocks instead of 8. This will let them unlock all their memories faster. For a really short campaign, ignore the clocks and simply have the Hull unlock one memory at the end of every score (if you use this variant, the Hull doesn’t gain special abilities from these memories). 

When a clock is full, fill in the memory according to the prompt. 

You also remember all of the following: 

- One **key** of your choice. 

- A **contact—** either a former friend from another player’s playbook, or a powerful and dangerous rival. 

- A **special ability** . Choose another playbook and roll 1d8. Use your result to count down the list of abilities from the top, and take that one. If it involves special items, you get those too. _How did you acquire them?_ If the ability feels wrong, select from the ones above and below it, or just choose any ability instead of rolling randomly. Random selection helps it feel like the Hull is discovering who they were, rather than selecting who they were, but it’s not mandatory. 

When all four memories are complete, replace your first xp trigger with this one: _You worked to free yourself from your owning faction and controller, or you addressed a challenge with your humanity._ 

34 

## **Contacts** 

- **Your controller.** _Someone from your owning faction who manages your work while On Program._ 

## **Frame Features** 

You begin with two frame features of your choice. 

- **Advanced Visual Sensors:** Your eyes can switch to various visual modes, including night vision, heat vision, ultra-zoom, and resonance vision (the ability to see resonance entities). 

- **Lifelike Appearance:** Utilizing the latest super-realistic latex, you are masterfully crafted to pass for a living being. You may be detected if closely scrutinized; there are certain tests that can uncover even the most lifelike hull. 

- **Hidden Compartment:** Your frame has a secret compartment that escapes even the most thorough search. Lead-lined to prevent X-ray scanning. 

- **Smokescreen Emitter:** An emergency system that can exude a dark, acrid cloud of smoke—enough to fill a large room. 

- **Surveillance Hardware:** The latest espionage equipment, including an ultra-sensitive microphone that can hear at long range or through walls, a tape-feed to record this audio, as well as a resonance field radio tuned to a secure frequency. 

- **Jet Propulsion:** Your frame includes jet boosters that provide a limited form of flight (either slow or temporary). 

35 

## **Hull Traits** 

## **A ROOM OF YOUR OWN** 

You have your own secret little den. You can now put stacks into bank. You have a pet. You can spend a downtime action to look after the pet (describe the lengths you go to), and mark **3 xp** in a **memory clock** of your choice. 

_Hulls cannot put stacks into bank unless they have this trait. Note this also means that if the crew advances from xp and everyone makes bank, the Hull can only benefit if they have this trait._ 

## **POWERHOUSE** 

Take **1 Drain** to perform a feat of extreme strength or speed (run faster than an autopod, rend metal with your hands, etc.). _This factors into effect._ 

_Hulls have human-like abilities by default. Take this trait if you want to act like a superpowered robot: running, jumping, lifting, and punching like a powerful machine._ 

## **RETRACTABLE ARSENAL** 

Your items are built into your frame and may recess beneath panels out of sight. Your frame can now carry + **2 load** . 

_The first part of this trait lets you carry items and weapons without being noticed (take the hidden compartment frame feature for complete and impenetrable secrecy). The second part gives you increased load._ 

## **ENERGY BEAM** 

You may release some of your energy as an electric shock around you or as a directed beam. You may also use this ability to create a lightning barrier to repel or trap a resonance entity. Take **1 Drain** for each level of **magnitude** . 

_See page 331 for magnitude examples. As a shortcut, take 1 Drain per Tier difference. If you’re a Tier 0 Hull and want to trap a Tier 4 resonance entity, this might take 4 Drain. If the Hull were instead part of a Tier 2 crew, it would only take 2 Drain. This ability always costs a minimum of 1 Drain._ 

## **INTERFACE** 

You may **Attune** to the local electroplasmic power field to control it or something connected to it (including another hull). 

## **FRAME UPGRADE** 

Choose two additional frame features. 

_You can take this trait twice._ 

36 

## **Hull Questions** 

After crew creation and character creation, your group can run through background questions together. Take turns introducing your characters, and then take turns asking the group one of the following questions (your choice), or make up your own question. 

Anyone can answer, and together you can flesh out some of the details. 

- Which of you found me when I was malfunctioning and took me in? 

- Which of you finds me useful, but like how a forklift is useful? 

- Which of you finds me easy to talk to? 

- Which of you has a bad history with my owning faction? 

- Which of you still doesn’t trust me? 

- Which of you has shown me what’s good in life? 

Then go around again—ask another question from the list, or pass. When everyone has passed, move on to crew questions. 

37 

Intellectual **Tinker Study** 

**A BRILLIANT ENGINEER, SCIENTIST, AND PHILOSOPHER** 

The world is at a turning point, and Intellectuals play a pivotal role in shaping whatever comes next. They are cultural critics, academic theorists, scholars, inventors, and polymaths. The most famous Intellectuals are celebrated in society, interviewed on talkshows, and profiled in glossy magazines. Some Intellectuals find a place in the underworld, too—what better place from which to observe and influence the political and social upheaval of our times. 

Whether you’re a hands-on technical egghead or a theorizing philosopher, any criminal crew will benefit from a good keen mind. **When you play an Intellectual, you earn xp when you address a challenge with technical skill or cleverness.** Doskvol is a city of the future, full of sparkcraft technology, automaton hulls, electronic systems, and mechanical hardware for you to bend to your purposes. 

38 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0049-00.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Characters<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


**39** 

## **Fields of Study** 

Instead of writing down a background, decide what fields of study your Intellectual has experience in. This is not about defining your future, but explains how you became the Intellectual you are today. Choose from the following list, or make up your own. Are you self-taught, or did you attend university, or were you educated by tutors in the fashion of the nobility? 

- **History:** Understanding the past provides context for the present and future. _Sociology, art history, military history, Imperial history, precataclysm theory._ 

- **Biology:** What could be more fundamental than understanding the complexities and mechanics of living organisms? _Anatomy, luminant botany, deathlands zoology, evolution, void marine biology, paleontology._ 

- **Philosophy:** Pondering the big questions about existence, knowledge, morality, and truth. _Epistemology, ethics, literary theory, aesthetics, logic, language, political philosophy._ 

- **Sparkcraft:** Applying practical scientific and mathematical principles to the development of new inventions. _Mechanics, electroplasmics, chemical engineering, aeronautics, terminal programming, sparkmind development, hull engineering._ 

- **Paranormal:** Exploring phenomena that are beyond normal scientific understanding, including supernatural occurrences and fringe science. _Metaphysics, parapsychology, spectrology, resonance studies, remote viewing._ 

- **Political Science:** The study of governance and power. _Statecraft, international relations, espionage, propaganda, revolutionary theory, counterinsurgency strategy, bureaucratic analysis._ 

- **School of Hard Knocks:** Perhaps you sharpened your mind through the tough experiences and hardships of the streets. _Practical psychology, resilience, improvisation, critical thinking, interpersonal skills, entrepreneurship, determination, underworld sociology, persuasion._ 

40 

## **Sparkmind Assistant** 

You start with a playbook cohort, your own sparkmind assistant. Give them a name, edges, and flaws like any cohort. Choose a **type** and **housing** . As an expert cohort, their Quality is equal to crew Tier +1 when their type applies to the situation at hand. 

The size of their housing determines how powerful they are, which in turn might influence position or effect when they attempt certain actions. A large housing lets the sparkmind attempt more ambitious calculations and actions, but they are immobile. 

Playbook cohorts can take actions themselves, and they can also join in group actions, and they can help during downtime in various ways (see **Cohorts** on page 96 for more detail). Playbook cohorts cannot perform secondary scores. 

## **Type** 

- **Research:** Gathering information. 

- **Analysis:** Studying and invention. 

- **Ingress:** System hacking. 

## **Housing** 

- **Small:** A wristwatch, a metal orb, a tiny hull, etc. Less powerful but highly portable. 

- **Large:** A room-sized computer. More powerful, but immobile. 

How did you come by this sparkmind assistant; did you build it, steal it, rescue it, or find it by chance? How long ago? 

41 

## **Intellectual Keys** 

Choose from these keys or use them as inspiration and pick your own. Each includes two possible deadlocks as examples—one where the key is flipped to its opposite[▼] , and one where it’s intensified[▲] . 

- **Arrogant** ([▼] Humbled[▲] Self-Obsessed) 

- **Sophisticated** ([▼] Modest[▲] Pretentious) 

- **Insecure** ([▼] Confident[▲] Anxious) 

- **Enigmatic** ([▼] Open[▲] Reclusive) 

- **Lonely** ([▼] Social[▲] Loner) 

- **Determined** ([▼] Laid-Back[▲] Obsessed) 

- **Enthusiastic** ([▼] Apathetic[▲] Reckless)

- **Cold** ([▼] Brutal[▲] Friendly)

- **Rational** ([▼] Irregular[▲] Uncaring)

## **Brilliant Friends** 

- **Faden** , an innovative doctor. _Perhaps an esteemed equal with some unusual ideas, or a dangerous fraud?_ 

- **Penny** , a debauched theorist. _Perhaps a stimulating conversational partner, or a former colleague lost to hedonism?_ 

- **Jarris** , an escaped test subject. _Perhaps a victim of science who you help when you can, or one of your own vengeful test subjects?_ 

- **Ackhurst** , a professor (fired). _Perhaps an old friend or mentor who crossed the wrong people, or your longtime academic rival?_ 

- **OLEK** , a rogue sparkmind. _Who created them, and how did they escape? Where are they now?_ 

42 

## **Intellectual Items** 

- **Fine tinkering tools:** Tools and spare parts for messing with electronics and mechanisms. A wrench, drill, and spanner. Tweezers, pliers, precision screwdrivers. A soldering iron. Oscilloscope, circuit tester, and heat sink. Jumper wires. Magnifying loupe. **1 load.** 

- **Experimental laser cannon:** A plasmoleum-fueled device that generates a continuous beam of electroplasmic radiation. A dangerous and potentially unstable weapon that will incinerate pretty much anything it’s pointed at. **2 load.** 

- **Sparkmind assistant:** Sparkminds are a form of artificial intelligence, utilizing a matrix of circuits and chips to harness the immense intellect of a high-Tier resonance entity. Where did you get yours? Did you invent it, steal it, or something else? ( _Cohort, Expert: Research, Analysis, or Ingress_ ). 

- **Gadgets:** You can create gadgets in a flashback and track their load here. If they’re very simple, just the flashback may be enough. More ambitious gadgets might require you spend a downtime action inventing them (additional downtime actions cost 1 stack). **1+ load.** 

- **Pocketful of focus pills:** For when you need steady hands, an alert mind, and laser-like concentration. _Very addictive (this can be resisted)._ **0 load.** 

- **RF radio handset:** A resonance field radio. A small handheld unit tuned to a secure frequency. **0 load.** 

## **Intellectual Special Abilities** 

## **UNALLOYED GENIUS** 

When you **craft an invention** , take + **1** result level to your roll (a 1-3 becomes a 4/5, etc.). Invention clocks start with one segment already filled. 

_See page 166 to learn more about crafting an invention._ 

## **MENTALIST** 

You can deduce trivial details about anyone. **Study** them to reveal their current intentions as well as a deep desire they’re keeping secret or didn’t even know they had; gain + **1d** and **potency** when acting on this information. 

_Note that this ability is not paranormal; it uses cold reading, psychology, and a deep understanding of human behavior._ 

_What does your mentalism look like? What theatrics or misdirection are involved?_ 

43 

## **HIGH-FUNCTIONING INSOMNIAC** 

During **downtime** , you get **two ticks** to distribute among any long-term project clocks that involve research, investigation, or crafting. 

## **TRY NOT TO BREAK IT THIS TIME** 

Any flashbacks to give another crew member just the right gadget before the score cost 0 Stress. Gain one free **downtime action** to craft such a gadget in a flashback. 

_The gadget can either be counted against the recipient’s load or the Intellectual’s, your choice. Most gadgets are 1-load._ 

_If it’s a very simple gadget, just the flashback may be enough. More ambitious gadgets might require you spend a downtime action inventing them; see page 166 for details._ 

_The_ _**jury-rig** option is a good choice for these gadgets—it lets you create the invention with one roll (no clock needed). Make a Tinker roll, and the result indicates the Quality of the gadget (1-3: Inferior (Tier -1), 4/5: Standard (Tier), 6: Fine (Tier+1), critical: Exceptional (Tier +2). A jury-rigged gadget only lasts one score._ 

## **RESEARCHER** 

Twice per score, you may use your **research** to resist a consequence of fatigue, weakness, or resonance effects, or to push yourself when working with technical skill or handling resonance objects. 

_When you use this ability, tick one of the research boxes on your sheet. If you resist a consequence of the appropriate type, you might avoid it completely, or you might reduce it by one (such as harm, or a clock ticking), as per resistance as usual. If you use this ability to push yourself, you get one of the benefits (+1d, +1 effect) but you don’t take 2 Stress. Your research uses are restored at the beginning of downtime._ 

## **ANATOMIST** 

You can **Tinker** the human body to treat wounds or stabilize the dying. You may **Study** a sickness or corpse. Everyone in your crew gets + **1d** to their healing treatment rolls. 

_Any chancer can try some first aid, but this ability represents specialist expertise—forensics, surgery, pharmacology, and advanced knowledge of anatomy._ 

44 

## **ENCYCLOPEDIC KNOWLEDGE** 

When you **push yourself** , you can also do one of the following: _instantly find a_ — _weak point or exploitable pattern in an obstacle dazzle an audience with your intellect, leaving them confused and distracted._ 

_When you push yourself to activate this ability, you still get one of the normal benefits of pushing yourself (+1d or +1 effect) in addition to the special ability. This kind of ability lets you do something that most characters can’t, but a roll might still be required if there is a threat or obstacle (as usual)._ 

_A weak point or exploitable pattern improves position and/or effect. This might be a literal gap in their armor, a flaw in a machine’s design, a gap in a guard patrol, or a moment in a target’s daily routine that leaves them exposed (such as when they step outside to the balcony for a cigarette, alone)._ 

_Dazzling an audience might mean one target, or a small group. This might leave them vulnerable to suggestion, or it might make a good distraction from other events. This stacks with the Mentalist ability, if you have previously deduced their deepest desires._ 

## **ADVANCED SPARKMIND** 

Choose an additional **type** , or add an **edge** , or remove a **flaw** . 

_This ability can be taken twice._ 

## **Intellectual Questions** 

After crew creation and character creation, your group can run through background questions together. Take turns introducing your characters, and then take turns asking the group one of the following questions (your choice), or make up your own question. 

Anyone can answer, and together you can flesh out some of the details. 

- Which of you finds me pretentious? 

- Which of you is learning something from me? 

- Which of you likes to wind me up? 

- Which of you also loves my favorite restaurant? 

- Which of you is friends with my sparkmind assistant? 

- Which of you shared a deep conversation with me the other night? 

Then go around again—ask another question from the list, or pass. When everyone has passed, move on to crew questions. 

45

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
 CLANDESTINE<br>AND<br>PROFESSIONAL<br>STEALTHY<br>A  ESPIONAGE<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


Doskvol plays a pivotal role in the cold war. With its large population of second- and third-generation Skovs, and its position directly across the void sea from the USC capital of Lockport, Doskvol is the symbolic wall between Skovlan and Akoros. It is a hotbed of espionage activity, used as a base of operations and staging ground by multiple spy agencies, including Skov, Imperial, and Iruvian intelligence. 

Operatives are the agents and assassins who do this dirty work. Many work for one spy agency or another, but some fall into the underworld. Their knowledge of spycraft and their expertise in infiltration and deception make them uniquely suited to many criminal endeavors. 

**When you play an Operative, you earn xp when you address a challenge with stealth or subterfuge.** Sneak in, get the job done, and exit cleanly. You’re a professional; you can handle any complications. 

**46** 

47 

## **Backing Faction** 

Other playbooks have to unlock a backing faction by completing a long-term project, but as an Operative, you start with one already. This is likely one of the spy agencies, but could be any faction of your choice. _Did they train you, recruit you, or are you a disposable asset? Do you willingly maintain a connection to them, or is it impossible for you to cut ties?_ 

- **Blackthorn Park (Tier 3)** : The foreign intelligence service of the United Skov Covenant. They’ve been punching above their weight, achieving some big wins despite having fewer resources than the Palace. 

- **The Palace (Tier 5)** : The Imperial Intelligence Agency, or I.I.A. Spends as much time neutralizing internal threats to its own power as it does clashing with Blackthorn Park. 

- **Section 6 (Tier 5)** : Responsible for enforcing Reality Constancy Law (investigating anomalies and unlicensed paranormal experimentation). 

- **Anixis Field Unit (Tier 2)** : Newly independent in the wake of Unity War III, Iruvia has entered an isolationist period. Their intelligence agency (Anixis) maintains a small field unit in Doskvol to monitor the other spy agencies and advance Iruvian interests where possible. 

- **The Strelai (Tier 4)** : Counter-paranormal secret agents with mysterious motives and affiliation. 

- **The Burn Corps (Tier 2):** The radical militant arm of Burning Orange, the Severosi social activism collective. The Burn Corps is dedicated to armed self-defence, particularly against Bluecoat brutality. 

You can call on your faction for help—either during crew business or personal business. Your faction can: 

- **Assist** on your action roll, as if they were a teammate (+1d). 

- **Increase effect** on your action roll, as though you pushed yourself. 

- Loan you **equipment** of their Tier level in Quality. 

- Share relevant intel with you; make a **gather information** roll with dice equal to their Tier. 

- Give you a **1 stack reward** when handing over information of interest to them. 

- **Resist or dismiss unwanted consequences** , if it’s within their powers. 

- **Intervene with another faction** on your behalf, if it’s within their powers. 

After your faction helps you, they might ask for something in return—including a **personal mission** . If you complete that personal mission, you gain access to the faction’s **prestige ability** . 

See the **Backing Faction** section on page 236 for full details. 

48

- **Disciplined** ([▼] Loose[▲] Uptight)

- **Haunted** ([▼] Self-Assured[▲] Tormented)

- **Fearless** ([▼] Nervous[▲] Turbulent)

- **Calculating** ([▼] Apathetic[▲] Paranoid)

## **Covert Friends** 

- **Harani Ankhayat** , a diplomat. _Perhaps a reliable go-between contact, or perhaps a former contact who double-crossed you?_ 

- **Tailor** , a handler. _Perhaps your own handler, or perhaps they work for the other side?_ 

- **Karla** , a field agent. _Perhaps a trusted colleague, or a rival threatened by your success?_ 

- **Percy** , a cat-burglar. _Perhaps an old friend and confidant, or perhaps a troublemaker who enjoys interfering in your operations?_ 

- **Bowman** , an undersecretary. _Perhaps a good source of information, or perhaps an overly curious bureaucrat who’s noticed irregularities in your paperwork?_ 

49 

## **Operative Items** 

- **Truth serum syringe:** Delivers one dose of a truth serum. The victim becomes delirious and suggestible for up to an hour, open to answering all sorts of questions. **0 load.** 

- **Fine sniper rifle:** A high-powered sniper rifle complete with silencer. Deadly at long range, unwieldy in close quarters. **2 load.** 

- **Tiny tracking device:** A small tracking device (adhesive and/or magnetic) and a handheld gadget that shows the device’s current location. Works reliably up to a distance of two city districts away. **0 load.** 

- **Fine silenced shooter:** A finely made semi-automatic handgun with a modest caliber. Quiet as a whisper. **1 load.** 

- **Fine disguise:** A state-of-the-art disguise of one specific person. Includes clothing as well as a super-realistic latex mask and wig. Could fool their own family, assuming you’re roughly the same height and build. **1 load.** 

- **RF radio handset:** A resonance field radio. A small handheld unit tuned to a secure frequency. **0 load.** 

## **Operative Special Abilities** 

## **CLEAN** 

Twice per score, you may use your **precision** to resist a consequence from detection or security measures, or to **push yourself** for a feat of athletics or stealth. 

_When you use this ability, tick one of the precision boxes on your sheet. If you resist a consequence of the appropriate type, you might avoid it completely, or you might reduce it by one (such as harm, or a clock ticking), as per resistance as usual. If you use this ability to push yourself, you get one of the benefits (+1d, +1 effect) but you don’t take 2 Stress. Your precision uses are restored at the beginning of downtime._ 

## **DOUBLE AGENT** 

You gain a second **backing faction** of your choice immediately. You get **+2d** when working on long-term projects to influence either of your backing factions. _How long have you been secretly building this relationship? Does your first backing faction know about it?_ 

_Remember that backing factions don’t have to have a positive faction status with your crew. You should definitely consider taking the backing of enemy factions—infiltrate them to learn their secrets, and manipulate them from the inside. Does this new faction know they are backing you, or are you operating under a disguised identity?_ 

50 

_Whenever you attempt to guide a backing faction via long-term project, take +2d._ 

_You can request help from both backing factions; one instance of each type of help per faction (assist, resist, etc.). If you take help from both factions, make two Return the Favor rolls._ 

## **DEAD DROP** 

You have access to a bound resonance entity that will leave up to **2 load** of items anywhere you need them. The flashback to requesting the item(s) is free, and they’re left anywhere you choose. You can also flashback to an Acquire Asset roll for the items as a free downtime activity. 

_These items could be standard playbook items. They could be equipment left on the other side of a security checkpoint, or under a table, or even inside a vault (explosives left inside a target’s desk, for example)._ 

_You can also use a free Acquire Asset downtime activity if you want nonstandard item(s)—a stab-proof vest, gas mask, underwater breather, hangglider, etc._ 

_The items count against your own load limit. This ability can be used twice per score if each item is 1 load (2 load total is the max). Both flashbacks are free, but you only get one free Acquire Asset downtime activity._ 

_Who leaves the items? Are they an echo, or a non-human resonance entity? Why do they work for you?_ 

## **ECHO WALKER** 

Pay 2 Stress to step into the resonance field and disappear. Reappear at a moment of your choice, wherever you want (you have to be able to move there physically). When you reappear, you are _so cold_ (level 1 harm, can be resisted). 

_When you pay 2 Stress for this ability, you disappear. You must have the freedom to physically step into the resonance field, so this ability cannot be used to dodge bullets or escape restraints (it’s more like walking through a door)._ 

_You can use this ability to bypass all sorts of obstacles, with very little chance of detection._ 

_The other way to use this ability is to step into the resonance field and then keep your character in a quantum state, where they are nowhere and so could be anywhere. When the GM reveals an assassin holding a gun to a hostage’s head, the Echo Walker could appear right behind the assassin, unseen. When the diplomat comes out on the balcony to wave to the crowd, the Echo Walker could appear in the hotel room behind them to rifle_ 

51 

_through their desk. As long as it’s plausible they could have moved there physically (they can’t appear in a locked vault), they can appear whenever and wherever they want, at any dramatic moment._ 

_Armor does not stop the level 1 harm, but it can be resisted as normal._ 

## **WETWORK** 

When you **push yourself** , you can also do one of the following: _make an_ — _improbable shot at extreme distance or with extreme speed perform a feat of athletics that verges on the superhuman._ 

_When you push yourself to activate this ability, you still get one of the normal benefits of pushing yourself (+1d or +1 effect) in addition to the special ability. This kind of ability lets you do something that most characters can’t, but a roll might still be required if there is a threat or obstacle (as usual)._ 

_For the first use, the range is relative to the firearm; “extreme distance” will be different for a handcannon vs. a sniper rifle. Either way, this ability extends the range considerably. It also lets you take the shot extremely quickly._ 

_For the second use, you might climb a sheer surface that lacks good handholds, tumble safely out of a three-story fall, leap a shocking distance, etc._ 

## **CIPHER** 

You have a deep cover identity. When you use it, you get + **1d** to rolls to confuse or deflect suspicion. When you reveal your true identity, the resulting surprise gives you the initiative in the situation (as well as **+1d** and **potency** ). If your cover identity is blown, create a new one with a 4-segment long-term project. 

_This ability is very powerful for infiltration, as well as to get out of trouble if a covert operation goes haywire. Don’t forget your fine disguise item (including realistic latex mask and wig), which boosts the effect of your covert deception methods._ 

## **SLEEPER AGENTS** 

Once per score, pay **2 Stress** and nominate a minor NPC. They’ve been working for you this whole time. 

_The GM has final say on who counts as “a minor NPC,” but they are encouraged to be generous in their interpretation. As a guideline: any NPCs who haven’t been given a name, or who are likely to appear in this score only, or who aren’t a reoccurring antagonist or faction leader. If in doubt, it works. This could also include hulls (they are NPCs)._ 

_Note that while the NPC works for you (and/or your backing faction), they aren’t mind-controlled and will definitely want to stay alive, and might potentially want to keep their cover if possible._ 

52 

## **CONTROL** 

Choose one of your action ratings. When you lead a **group action** using that action, you can suffer only 1 Stress at most regardless of the number of failed rolls, and you may count multiple 6s from different rolls as a critical. 

_This special ability is good for covering for your team. If they’re all terrible at your favored action, you don’t have to worry about suffering a lot of Stress when you lead their group action. It also lets you turn a group action into a critical more often._ 

## **Operative Questions** 

After crew creation and character creation, your group can run through background questions together. Take turns introducing your characters, and then take turns asking the group one of the following questions (your choice), or make up your own question. 

Anyone can answer, and together you can flesh out some of the details. 

- Which of you doesn’t trust me? 

- Which of you has my affiliated faction asked me to monitor? 

- Which of you will always have my back? 

- Which of you has had secret contact with a faction that rivals my affiliated faction? 

- Which of you tested the truth serum together with me, that one night? 

- Which of you asked me to train you? 

Then go around again—ask another question from the list, or pass. When everyone has passed, move on to crew questions. 

53 

## Paranormalist 

**54** 

The world is undeniably an uncanny place, with alternate dimensions smashed together by a realitybreaking cataclysm. Other scientists might be afraid to venture outside the safe waters of conventional science, but the Paranormalist dives into that void sea with curiosity and passion. Only once you abandon the fear of skepticism and ridicule can you start to uncover the vast and mysterious truths beyond the veil. 

**When you play a Paranormalist, you earn xp when you address a challenge with knowledge or paranormal power.** Seek out the strange and supernatural and bend it to your will. Be fearlessly curious. Experiment and innovate. Others may laugh, but you know that untold power lies within reach for those with the right tools and an open mind. 

**55** 

## **Loyal Resonance Entity** 

You start with a playbook cohort, a loyal resonance entity. Give them a name, edges, and flaws like any cohort. The resonance entity functions as an **Expert: Paranormal Assistant** . As an expert cohort, their Quality is equal to crew Tier +1 when their **type** , or area of expertise (Paranormal Assistant), applies to the situation at hand. It’s up to the table to agree on what that means, but you could broadly say it covers research, equipment handling, field support, safety, fetching things, and maybe being the occasional distraction. It would not cover fighting or other bold, aggressive actions. 

Playbook cohorts can take actions themselves, and they can also join in group actions, and they can help during downtime in various ways (see **Cohorts** on page 96 for more detail). Playbook cohorts cannot perform secondary scores. 

Resonance entities exist in the resonance field, but may manifest in the physical world as a concentration of electroplasmic matter. In this state, they may weakly interact with the physical world, and vice versa. They’re vulnerable to paranormal powers and electroplasmic effects. 

What kind of resonance entity is it? 

_**Resonance Echoes:** Former lover, old enemy, fallen mentor, parent or ancestor, accidental victim, antiquated stranger, polite butler, whispering wraith, just a rude dude._ 

_**Non-Human Entities:** Slime entity, mirror shards, cloud of dark smoke, insect swarm, floating orb, hypnotic lights, weird goblin._ 

What’s your history with this entity? How cordial is your relationship? 

56 

## **Paranormalist Keys** 

Choose from these keys, or use them as inspiration and pick your own. Each includes two possible deadlocks as examples—one where the key is flipped to its opposite[▼] , and one where it’s intensified[▲] . 

- **Flamboyant** ([▼] Demure[▲] Self-Obsessed) 

- **Enigmatic** ([▼] Open[▲] Reclusive) 

- **Haunted** ([▼] Self-Assured[▲] Tormented) 

- **Bold** ([▼] Nervous[▲] Reckless) 

- **Charismatic** ([▼] Quiet[▲] Manipulative) 

- **Comical** ([▼] Serious[▲] Unhinged)

- **Eccentric** ([▼] Ordinary[▲] Erratic) 

- **Passionate** ([▼] Apathetic[▲] Furious) 

- **Fearless** ([▼] Nervous[▲] Turbulent) 

- **Idealistic** ([▼] Cynical[▲] Zealous) 

- **Shy** ([▼] Brash[▲] Withdrawn) 

- **Open-Minded** ([▼] Rigid[▲] Reckless) 

- **Spiritual** ([▼] Cynical[▲] Obsessed)
