## **Strange Friends** 

- **Goodridge** , an archivist. _Perhaps a useful friend with similar interests in the strange and paranormal, or perhaps a skeptic who considers you a dangerous fraud?_ 

- **Scurlock** , a recluse. _Perhaps your partner in a dark endeavor, or perhaps a dangerous person you double-crossed?_ 

- **Padeen** , a Strelai operative. _Perhaps a mystic willing to share knowledge, or perhaps a skilled professional who considers you a danger to yourself and others?_ 

- **Warley** , a mind traveler. _Perhaps a good source for secrets and forbidden knowledge, or perhaps an unstable entity with a loose grip on reality?_ 

- **Chime** , an old whisper. _Perhaps a mentor, or perhaps a deadly rival?_ 

57 

## **Paranormalist Items** 

- **Fine resonance gauge:** A handheld device that measures resonance in its vicinity. Can be used to detect paranormal activity and locate resonance entities. **1 load.** 

- **Resonance accelerator pack:** A handheld particle-thrower connected to a backpack-sized resonance accelerator. Blasts a stream of highly focused, polarized electroplasmic energy. Suitable for grappling with a resonance entity and dragging it into a containment unit. **2 load.** 

- **Fine echo containment unit:** A device used to hold a single resonance entity for containment and safe transport. Designed for Class I–IV Resonance Entities. Not advised for Class V or above. **1 load.** 

- **Psychic amplification device:** An experimental piece of equipment that focuses the wearer’s paranormal abilities. Also affords some measure of protection against paranormal assault. What does yours look like; is it a helmet, a circlet, a glove or gauntlet, or something else? Did you invent it yourself, or acquire it some other way? **0 load.** 

- **Loyal resonance entity:** How did you come by this entity, and why do they help you? Are they the echo of a human or... something else? _(Cohort, Expert: Paranormal Assistant)._ 

- **RF radio handset:** A resonance field radio. A small handheld unit tuned to a secure frequency. **0 load.** 

## **Paranormalist Special Abilities** 

## **THIRD EYE OPENED** 

You’re always aware of resonance entities in your vicinity. You can **Attune** to the resonance field to force a nearby entity to appear and obey a command you give it. 

_The GM will tell you if you sense any resonance entities nearby. If you don’t, you can gather information (maybe Attune, Survey, or Study) to attempt to locate one._ 

_By default, a resonance echo wants to satisfy its need for life essence and to exact vengeance. When you command it, you can give it a general or specific instruction, but the more general it is (like “Protect me”), the more the entity will interpret it according to its own desires. Your control over the entity lasts until the command is fulfilled, or until a day has passed, whichever comes first._ 

58 

## **PRECOGNITION** 

Two times per score, you can **assist** a teammate without paying Stress. Tell us how you prepared for this in advance. 

_You can narrate an event in the past that helps your teammate now, or you might explain how you expected this situation and planned a helpful contingency that you reveal now._ 

_This precognition is more a vague sense than perfect foresight—you don’t know everything that’s going to happen, but perhaps, for example, you had a sense that a particular teammate would be faced with a particular sort of lock, and gave them warning to prepare for it._ 

## **PSYCHOKINESIS** 

When you push yourself, you can also do one of the following: _levitate for a short time_ — _violently push or pull objects through the air._ 

_When you push yourself to activate this ability, you still get one of the normal benefits of pushing yourself (+1d or +1 effect) in addition to the special ability. This kind of ability lets you do something that most characters can’t, but a roll might still be required if there is a threat or obstacle (as usual)._ 

## **EXTRASENSORY PERCEPTION** 

Twice per score, you may use your **sixth sense** to resist a paranormal consequence, or to push yourself when you deal with paranormal forces. 

_When you use this ability, tick one of the sixth sense boxes on your sheet. If you resist a consequence of the appropriate type, you might avoid it completely, or you might reduce it by one (such as harm, or a clock ticking), as per resistance as usual. If you use this ability to push yourself, you get one of the benefits (+1d, +1 effect) but you don’t take 2 Stress. Your sixth sense uses are restored at the beginning of downtime._ 

## **FORBIDDEN SCIENCE** 

You can use a downtime action to perform a **paranormal experiment** to manifest a supernatural effect or being. Gain **one free downtime action** to perform such experiments. 

_Without this special ability, the study and practice of paranormal experiments leaves you utterly exposed to reality-warping powers, with a high risk of catastrophe._ 

_Will you devise a method to find anomalies? To combat paranormal entities? To travel into the resonance field? To strengthen (or weaken) the B.L.U.E. Array? To escape notice of the Reality Wardens? To travel through time?_ 

_For more detail on paranormal experiments, see page 167._ 

59 

## **ECHO PROJECTION** 

Pay **2 Stress** to become a radiant being of crackling energy. While in this mode, you count as wearing armor, your physical attacks gain **potency** , and you can push yourself to shoot arcs of electroplasmic lightning. The projection drops at the end of the scene (or pay 2 Stress to continue for another scene). When you drop the projection, take the level 2 harm _Drained_ and the GM will tick a clock of their choice (you may resist these consequences). If you take this ability a second time, the GM will not tick a clock. 

_When you pay 2 Stress for this ability, you physically transform and project an aura of pure resonance energy. What does this look like?_ 

_You count as wearing armor, reducing all incoming physical harm by one level automatically. You can total the armor, but this will drop the projection._ 

_Your physical attacks (with close combat weapons or your bare hands) gain potency. When you push yourself, you can also unleash a blast of lightning; the GM will describe its effect level and significant collateral damage. If you unleash it in combat against an enemy who’s threatening you, you’ll still make an action roll in the fight (usually with Attune)._ 

_The length of a scene is up to the table to decide, but typically it’s when you’ve dealt with the current obstacle (for example, the fight is over), the location changes (you finally emerge from the sewers into the mansion above), or a significant amount of time passes._ 

## **MEDIUM** 

You can communicate with all paranormal entities, even those not present in the physical realm. Take + **1d** and **potency** when you do. 

_While some resonance echoes still act and speak much as they did while living, many fall to a feral state, incapable of coherent speech. Some might be entirely invisible and unheard, existing as a poltergeist. Other entities include non-human aberrations and powerful metadimensional entities, which may or may not choose to use human speech._ 

_You can communicate with all of the above (are there special preparations or rituals involved?), and are particularly good at it._ 

## **PARAPSYCHOLOGY** 

You’re immune to the terror that paranormal entities inflict on sight. Take + **1d** to resistance rolls with Resolve. Take + **1d** when you gather info about the paranormal. 

60 

## **Paranormalist Questions** 

After crew creation and character creation, your group can run through background questions together. Take turns introducing your characters, and then take turns asking the group one of the following questions (your choice), or make up your own question. 

Anyone can answer, and together you can flesh out some of the details. 

- Which of you has helped me with a paranormal experiment? 

- Which of you is skeptical of the paranormal? 

- Which of you has led me to an interesting insight? 

- Which of you have I seen in a terrible vision of the future? 

- Which of you asked me to read your fortune? 

- Which of you tripped on mushrooms with me? 

Then go around again—ask another question from the list, or pass. When everyone has passed, move on to crew questions.

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Sway<br>Wreck Command<br>EVERY SENSE<br>IN<br>AGITATOR—<br>Radical AN  INCENDIARY<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


There is no question that this is a time of great change—social, political, and material. The comfortable Consensus is being pushed and challenged, and it is the Radical who pushes hardest. 

Radicals are dedicated to overthrowing existing power structures, and the underworld is the perfect place to do it from. You know that this war must be fought on multiple fronts—you must spread the truth, and you must fight the man by any means necessary. 

**When you play a Radical, you earn xp when you address a challenge with persuasion or mayhem.** Sway people to your cause and talk your way past problems. When that doesn’t work, blow something up. 

62 

**63** 

## **Radicalized By** 

Instead of writing down a background, decide what radicalized you. Choose from the following list, or make up your own. This makes your grievance and associated ideology specific, not just vague and generic activism. _Were you radicalized by your own upbringing, or experiences later in life, or by radical literature, or an influential activist?_ 

- **Bluecoats** 

- **Labor conditions** 

- **Bigotry** 

- **Inequality** 

- **Horrors of war** 

- **Discrimination** 

## **Radical Keys** 

Choose from these keys, or use them as inspiration and pick your own. Each includes two possible deadlocks as examples—one where the key is flipped to its opposite[▼] , and one where it’s intensified[▲] . 

- **Idealistic** ([▼] Skeptical[▲] Zealous) 

- **Determined** ([▼] Laid-Back[▲] Obsessed) 

- **Protective** ([▼] Careless[▲] Vengeful) 

- **Romantic** ([▼] Cynical[▲] In Love) 

- **Suspicious** ([▼] Trusting[▲] Paranoid) 

- **Violent** ([▼] Merciful[▲] Vicious) 

- **Stubborn** ([▼] Flexible[▲] Pigheaded) 

- **Reckless** ([▼] Careful[▲] Chaotic) 

- **Kind** ([▼] Harsh[▲] Selfless)

- **Commanding** ([▼] Deferential[▲] Controlling ) 

- **Passionate** ([▼] Apathetic[▲] Furious) 

- **Defiant** ([▼] Compliant[▲] Wild) 

- **Charismatic** ([▼] Cold[▲] Manipulative) 

- **Fearless** ([▼] Nervous[▲] Turbulent) 

See page 154 for more about keys and deadlocks. 

64 

## **Zealous Friends** 

- **Vuko** , a union Rep. _Perhaps a fellow traveler, or a fervent believer in a rival ideology?_ 

- **Delyan** , a fireworks technician. _Perhaps a friendly source of explosives, or perhaps an honest worker who suspects you’re stealing their stock?_ 

- **Russo** , a maverick artist. _Perhaps a mentor who inspires your writing, or an old friend who considers you a hypocrite?_ 

- **Plundell** , a surgeon (and terrible poet). _Perhaps they help patch you up in exchange for notes on their poetry, or perhaps they consider themselves an artistic rival?_ 

- **Stoker** , a fearless journalist. _Perhaps they’re sympathetic to your cause, or perhaps they consider you a menace to public safety?_ 

## **Radical Items** 

- **Provocative manifesto:** A short punchy document declaring the views, motives, and intentions of a political movement. Has the potential to incite a crowd, or to enrage the authorities. **0 load.** 

- **Nondescript change of clothes:** An outfit of perfectly ordinary cut, for blending in with the crowd of whatever district you’re in. **1 load.** 

- **Bandolier:** A strap worn across the body, fitted with specially padded pouches to hold three explosives or bombs. When you employ an item from the bandolier, choose one from the list (or one of your own custom-made explosives). _During downtime, you automatically refill your bandoliers, so long as you have reasonable access to your supplier. Who are they?_ **1 load.** 

- **Pocketful of go-go pills:** Xantara Pharm’s finest uppers, for when you need pure, explosive energy. _You’ll run your mouth (what do you say that will get you in trouble?), and take the passing harm “jittery” when they wear off (these consequences can be resisted)._ **0 load.** 

- **RF radio handset:** A resonance field radio. A small handheld unit tuned to a secure frequency. **0 load.** 

65 

## **Explosives** 

The radical has access to a range of explosives that they can pull from their bandolier. These all count as **fine** items, with a Quality equal to **crew Tier +1** , and are generally **scale 1** (enough to effect a small gang, 3–6 people). Using multiple bandolier slots on one action may increase the scale. 

_It may seem overpowered that the Radical has such a wide range of utility bombs from the start, but if the crew is Tier 0, it means that these bombs are homemade, unreliable, and possibly undercooked (just like all the crew’s weapons and equipment at Tier 0). They won’t be very effective against much higher-Tier obstacles._ 

_Remember to follow the fiction, though—if it seems like a grenade in the right place at the right time would finish the job, then let that hold true regardless of Quality or Tier._ 

Note that if any explosives are used on a score, it adds **+1 Heat** during the aftermath. 

## **Radical Special Abilities** 

## **TRUE BELIEVER** 

Twice per score, you may use your **conviction** to resist a consequence of law-breaking (being arrested or hassled by Bluecoats, etc.) or to push yourself when fighting for your ideology. 

_When you use this ability, tick one of the conviction boxes on your sheet. If you resist a consequence of the appropriate type, you might avoid it completely, or you might reduce it by one (such as harm, or a clock ticking), as per resistance as usual. If you use this ability to push yourself, you get one of the benefits (+1d, +1 effect) but you don’t take 2 Stress. Your conviction uses are restored at the beginning of downtime._ 

## **DIRECT ACTION** 

When you make a desperate roll with either Wreck or Command, you gain both **potency** and **scale** . Remember that you can trade position for effect to make almost any action desperate, if you dare. 

_Potency and scale both factor into effect, so this ability will make both your words and your bombs extremely effective when you’re in a desperate position._ 

– _By default, bandolier explosives effect a small gang, 3 6 people. Increasing the scale would mean more like 12_ – _20 people._ 

66 

_It’s harder to quantify the scale of a Command, but start from what seems reasonable for the average chancer without this ability (shouting at a large crowd from a soapbox, or putting pressure on one person) and increase it one step (shouting at a huge crowd from a soapbox, or pressuring five people at once)._ 

_When you trade position for effect, think about what being in a desperate position looks like. With explosives, it might mean being particular reckless with timers, fuses, and quantities. With rhetoric, it might mean being louder, more recklessly provocative, or exposing your true identity._ 

## **ECHO CHAMBER** 

The resonance echoes of the downtrodden are drawn to you, and when you open yourself to them, your poetry reverberates with their power. Whenever you loudly recite poetry, a crowd gathers to listen (if possible). When you use poetry as a means to an end, take + **1d** and gain **potency** dealing with the paranormal. 

_The first part of this ability lets you gather a crowd in any almost any situation, which can be very useful for a Radical (see the Polemicist ability on the next page, for example, or Direct Action)._ 

_The second part means that when poetry is the tool you use to take action, you take +1d_ _**and** gain potency if dealing with paranormal entities. This can be used in creative ways—perhaps you graffiti poetry on a wall as a distraction, or deliver a subversive message that confuses a small-minded authoritarian, or have a personal poem delivered to the nightclub’s bouncer in a flashback (so they like you before you even arrive)._ 

_Whenever you use this ability, work with the GM to decide which echo (ghost) works through you. Is it a new one, or one you’ve dealt with before? Who were they in life? How long ago did they live? What do they want; what message do they hope to deliver through your poetry?_ 

67 

## **FELLOW TRAVELERS** 

In any scene with more than one NPC, ask the GM which of them are sympathetic to your cause. It’s always at least one, but often a few, many, or sometimes all of them. 

_When you ask “Who in this group is sympathetic to my cause?,” the GM can never answer “nobody”; there will always be at least one sympathizer in any group. Being sympathetic to your cause does not mean they work for you, will take your orders, or will automatically be your friend (although it might mean that). It does always mean you have a strong angle for further persuasion._ 

## **POLEMICIST** 

When you **push** yourself, you can also do one of the following: _whip a crowd_ — _into a righteous fury shame a powerful figure into silence or retreat._ 

_When you push yourself to activate this ability, you still get one of the normal benefits of pushing yourself (+1d or +1 effect) in addition to the special ability. This kind of ability lets you do something that most characters can’t, but a roll might still be required if there is a threat or obstacle (as usual)._ 

_The first use incites a crowd of any size, provided they can hear your voice. The second use forces the target to back down (at least for now), either into silence or outright retreat, no matter how high Tier or powerful they are._ 

## **PRAXIS** 

If you loudly and visibly destroy a symbolic target during a score, gain + **2 result levels** to any **long-term project** rolls related to your revolutionary work during the following personal business phase. 

_+2 result level is very powerful—a 1-3 becomes a 6 (three ticks), and a 4/5 or 6 becomes a critical (five ticks). This applies to all relevant long-term project rolls in that personal business phase, so make the most of it. A critical is still the maximum result possible._ 

## **PAMPHLETEER** 

You can publish revolutionary literature as a **4-segment long-term project** . Name each work. Once complete, a published work can tick another longterm project clock related to the revolution, once per downtime (maximum of four such works may be in effective circulation). If you die or get imprisoned, each work adds **two ticks** . 

_If you are imprisoned, the additional ticks only apply for the length of your incarceration. Once you’re released, it goes back to one tick per work._ 

68 

_The long-term project clock to finish a work of revolutionary literature is a valid choice for the Praxis ability—working on your literature would net the +2 result level, if the other conditions have been met._ 

_Completed literature cannot add ticks to further literature clocks—one work cannot write another._ 

_If GM and player agree, some works might become redundant and no longer function (such as if you publicly discredit yourself, the issue becomes moot, etc.)._ 

## **TOTAL DEDICATION** 

When you roll a desperate action, you get + **1d** to your roll if you also take **-1d** to any resistance rolls against consequences from your action. 

_This special ability is a bit of a gamble. The bonus die helps you, but if you suffer consequences, they’ll be more costly to resist. This ability stacks with Direct Action—if you have both abilities, a desperate action with rhetoric or explosives would net increased scale, potency, and +1d, with -1d to resist consequences. Anything for the revolution._ 

## **Radical Questions** 

After crew creation and character creation, your group can run through background questions together. Take turns introducing your characters, and then take turns asking the group one of the following questions (your choice), or make up your own question. 

Anyone can answer, and together you can flesh out some of the details. 

- Which of you is dismissive of my convictions? 

- Which of you fears what I’ll do one day? 

- Which of you enjoys debating my ideas? 

- Which of you quietly shares my convictions? 

- Which of you helps me restock my explosives? 

- Which of you asked for my feedback on a poem you wrote? 

Then go around again—ask another question from the list, or pass. When everyone has passed, move on to crew questions.

## **Fine Two-Seat Autopod** 

You start with a playbook cohort, your own two-seat autopod. Give it a name, edges, and flaws like any cohort. Choose a **type** . As an expert cohort, their Quality is equal to crew Tier +1 when their type applies to the situation at hand. 

Playbook cohorts can take actions themselves, and they can also join in group actions, and they can help during downtime in various ways (see **Cohorts** on page 96 for more detail). Playbook cohorts cannot perform secondary scores. 

## **Type** 

- **Racing:** This autopod is built for pure speed. 

- **Impressing:** The detailing is particularly stunning, and can help you Sway or Consort when you show it off. 

- **Surprising:** This autopod has built-in gadgets like an oil slick device, hidden guns, an ejector seat, a smoke emitter. 

How did you come by this autopod; did you buy it, build it, steal it, inherit it? 

## **Swinger Keys** 

Choose from these keys, or use them as inspiration and pick your own. Each includes two possible deadlocks as examples—one where the key is flipped to its opposite[▼] , and one where it’s intensified[▲] .

## **Fun Friends**

## **Swinger Items** 

- **Fine clothes & jewelry:** A fabulous outfit with a flattering cut, in the latest style. Sure to impress. If you’re carrying this item as a second outfit to change into, it counts as 2 load. **0 load.** 

- **Fine two-seat autopod:** The latest model. Is it built for racing, impressing, or surprising your enemies? ( _Cohort, Expert: Based on type_ ). 

- **An invitation to the party:** Everybody knows it’s not a party if you’re not invited. **0 load.** 

- **Fine concealed shooter:** A semi-automatic handgun with a modest caliber. It’s very difficult to detect on your person, even if you’re searched. **1 load.** 

- **Pocketful of sleeping pills:** If someone takes a few of these pills, they’ll quickly fall unconscious for at least an hour. The victim’s sleep isn’t paranormal, but it is deep—they can only be roused with some effort. **0 load.** 

- **RF radio handset:** A resonance field radio. A small handheld unit tuned to a secure frequency. **0 load.** 

73 

## **Swinger Special Abilities** 

## **HERE GOES NOTHING** 

Take **2 Stress** to roll your **Sway** or **Consort** rating while performing a different action. Use a free flashback to reveal who you convinced to teach you this particular technique or approach. 

_If you want to attempt lots of different sorts of actions and still have a good dice pool to roll, this is the special ability for you. The idea is that you use your Sway or Consort in a flashback to convince a friend, acquaintance, or even a stranger you just met to teach you some specific skill they have. While the action is rolled in the flashback, the consequences happen in the present. How well did you learn what they had to show you? How applicable was it to the situation you’re in? The dice decide._ 

_Maybe the Hound gave you some tips on following a target. Or your friend taught you a speed-reading research technique. Or your mechanic taught you how to patch up your autopod. Or a neighborhood kid showed you how to sneak. Or the bouncer at the nightclub to showed you some self-defense moves. Or a rockstar showed you how to wreck a room. Or that loner at the bar showed you how to talk to resonance entities._ 

## **YEAH, BABY** 

When you agree to an NPC’s proposal, even though it complicates the crew’s goals, everyone else on the crew marks **1 xp** while you clear **3 Stress** . 

_Perhaps talk to the rest of the table before you take this ability, and check they’re ok with you causing trouble (most players are—and they do get xp when you do). If you’re not receiving as many tempting proposals from NPCs as you would like, feel free to suggest your own (for example: “maybe the crime lord invites me on a private tour of her art gallery at this point; just me, and her, and her most lethal goons?”)_ 

## **GROOVE MACHINE** 

You always know where the nearest music is playing and when you start dancing, others feel compelled to join. When you take action while moving it on the dance floor, take **+1d** and **potency** . 

_The first part of this ability gives you permission to make a dance floor happen almost anywhere it’s even remotely plausible, without waiting for the GM to introduce one._ 

_This second part of this ability means that any action you take while dancing on the dance floor is super effective—not just dancing, but also persuading, picking a pocket, planting a wire, even engaging in a shoot-out. You name it._ 

74 

## **IMPROVISER** 

When you **push yourself** , you can also do one of the following: _claim to be_ — _anyone and others will consider the possibility, no matter how outlandish plunge blindly in an unexpected direction and find a new path._ 

_When you push yourself to activate this ability, you still get one of the normal benefits of pushing yourself (+1d or +1 effect) in addition to the special ability. This kind of ability lets you do something that most characters can’t, but a roll might still be required if there is a threat or obstacle (as usual)._ 

_The first use lets you put on a ruse in any situation and you always get a chance to see if it works, no matter how implausible. The second use means you can act first and think later, and it still stands a good chance of succeeding; jump through a window, drive off the bridge, dive down the laundry chute._ 

## **ALWAYS HUSTLING** 

Every personal business phase, mark **+1 bank** , and you may give yourself or another crew member + **1 downtime action** . What’s your side hustle? 

_If you forget to use this ability during downtime, you can still activate it during the score and flashback to the previous downtime when the extra activity happened._ 

## **PARTY ANIMAL** 

When you Indulge Vice, you can invite an ally to join you. They do not need to spend their own downtime action, and lose the same Stress that you do. One time during the next score, they can **assist** you once for free. 

_When you indulge vice together, the Swinger rolls as normal. Their result applies to both characters; if they rolled a 4, both characters clear 4 Stress. Either or both characters can overindulge as normal. What do you talk about as you indulge vice together?_ 

## **ECHO TWIN** 

There’s an alternate version of you in the resonance field, ghostly and glitched out. Take 2 Stress to summon them for a few moments, plus 1 Stress for each additional feature: _they last for a scene rather than a few minutes_ — _they_ — _appear completely stable and solid they obey your instructions to the letter._ 

_The summoned twin is a doppelganger, with the same abilities and equipment as you. When they take action, you might make a fortune roll with your own applicable action rating as a guide (if you want your twin to wrestle with someone, you might use your own Skirmish rating as a fortune roll to see how they do)._ 

75 

_They do not suffer Stress or harm, in mechanical terms, so it’s up to the GM to decide appropriate consequences. They can be injured, or destroyed (sending them back to the resonance field)._ 

_If you spend additional Stress, you can extend the summons for additional benefits, which may increase their effect (depending on the circumstances) as usual._ 

_Where do they go when they return to the resonance field? Is it always the same individual, or a different entity each time? Do they yearn to live in the physical realm? Do they like you, or resent you?_ 

## **SMOOTH** 

Twice per score, you may use your **mojo** to resist a consequence of suspicion or social faux pas, or to push yourself when talking your way out of a tight spot or driving under pressure. 

_When you use this ability, tick one of the mojo boxes on your sheet. If you resist a consequence of the appropriate type, you might avoid it completely, or you might reduce it by one (such as harm, or a clock ticking), as per resistance as usual. If you use this ability to push yourself, you get one of the benefits (+1d, +1 effect) but you don’t take 2 Stress. Your mojo uses are restored at the beginning of downtime._ 

## **Swinger Questions** 

After crew creation and character creation, your group can run through background questions together. Take turns introducing your characters, and then take turns asking the group one of the following questions (your choice), or make up your own question. 

Anyone can answer, and together you can flesh out some of the details. 

- Which of you went to that big party with me the other night? 

- Which of you saved my life when I did something stupid? 

- Which of you thinks I’m not a serious person? 

- Which of you is my competition on the dance floor? 

- Which of you comes to me for fashion advice? 

- Which of you trusts me as a true professional? 

Then go around again—ask another question from the list, or pass. When everyone has passed, move on to crew questions.

![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0089-01.png)



![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0089-02.png)


The Age of Consensus is a time of peace— that’s what we’re told, anyway. As a Veteran, you know there’s a reason why youths are conscripted en masse and shipped out, why untold millions are poured into military technology, why there’s a sprawling military base on the edge of Doskvol. Akoros may not officially be at war but it is still an Imperial machine, and the military is its iron fist. The nation is forever engaged in peacekeeping, temporary interventions, kinetic actions, strategic strikes, protective measures—war by any other name. 

Whether you volunteered or got drafted, you did your time on the frontlines. You learned discipline, and you learned how to do violence. You got chewed up, and the military spat you out. Now you’re back on the streets with little to show for your time but deep scars and lethal abilities. 

**When you play a Veteran, you earn xp when you address a challenge with violence or discipline.** 

**79** 

Unlike other playbooks, you also start with one special ability already (Military Discipline), and get to choose another, and you have one more action dot than other characters. On the flipside, you start with one **deadlocked key** already (choose both the key and its deadlocked state). 

**Damage:** Note down the damage you received during your time in service, that you still suffer from. _Burns or shrapnel injuries, a missing eye or limb, tinnitus, nightmares, traumatic flashbacks, the shakes._ 

**Something That Helps:** Note down what helps you cope with your damage. _A wheelchair, a prosthetic, medication, acupuncture, a cane or crutch, a service animal._ 

## **Tours of Duty** 

Instead of writing down a background, decide what tours of duty your Veteran has completed. Choose from the following list, or make up your own. 

**The Irondale Action** : Two years ago. Revolutionaries seized the Severosi city of Irondale, and Akoros landed troops to quash the movement. Bitter urban warfare, from city block to city block. 

**The Sevrin Invasion:** Ten years ago. The precursor to the Irondale Action, when the same radical group started their own separatist city in the deathlands, in an old fortification outside Sevrin. Akoros sent in troops to “stop the spread of this hateful ideology.” 

**Unity War III:** Twenty years ago. The last true war, and the end of the Imperium as it was. A generation-defining, world-spanning conflict. Ended with the accidental creation of the Null Zone, wiping out both South Point in Akoros and Bright Harbor in Iruvia. 

**Dagger Isles Peacekeeping:** Ongoing. The Dagger Isles are a collection of small countries, and both the Imperium and the United Skov Covenant use these nations as proxies in their own cold war. Akorosi troops are constantly rotating in and out of the Dagger Isles, supporting this revolution or fighting that one, and have done so since Unity War III ended. Student protests often feature placards demanding troops out of the Dagger Isles. 

80 

## **Veteran Keys** 

Choose from these keys, or use them as inspiration and pick your own. Each includes two possible deadlocks as examples—one where the key is flipped to its opposite[▼] , and one where it’s intensified[▲] . 

- **Protective** ([▼] Careless[▲] Vengeful) 

- **Hopeful** ([▼] Cynical[▲] Content) 

- **Erratic** ([▼] Calm[▲] Chaotic) 

- **Commanding** ([▼] Deferential[▲] Controlling) 

- **Lonely** ([▼] Social[▲] Loner) 

- **Distant** ([▼] Warm[▲] Cold) 

- **Violent** ([▼] Merciful[▲] Vicious) 

- **Reckless** ([▼] Careful[▲] Sloppy) 

- **Methodical** ([▼] Loose[▲] Uptight) 

- **Comical** ([▼] Serious[▲] Unhinged) 

- **Suspicious** ([▼] Trusting[▲] Paranoid) 

- **Tired** ([▼] Rejuvenated[▲] Defeated) 

- **Arrogant** ([▼] Humbled[▲] Self-Obsessed) 

- **Bold** ([▼] Nervous[▲] Reckless) 

- **Kind** ([▼] Harsh[▲] Selfless) 

- **Haunted** ([▼] Self-Assured[▲] Tormented ) 

See page 154 for more about keys and deadlocks. 

## **Difficult Friends** 

**Brackley** , a deserter. _Perhaps an old buddy from your unit, or someone who saw you do terrible things?_ 

**Fellows** , an army officer. _Perhaps an old friend who rose through the ranks, or your awful commanding officer?_ 

**Tiptree** , a hitwoman. _Perhaps a fellow veteran fallen into the same line of work, or someone who competes for the same violent work as you?_ 

**Professor** , a rough sleeper. _Perhaps you were also a rough sleeper for a time and they looked out for you, or perhaps they’re the only person who knows a dark secret about you?_ 

**Grunt** , a back-alley doctor. _Perhaps a medic you know from the front, or someone who’s had to clean up the mess after you go to work?_ 

81 

## **Veteran Items** 

**Submachine Coilgun (SMC):** A military-grade firearm noted for its compact size and rapid-fire capability. **1 load.** 

**Heavy Assault Coilgun (HAC50):** A military-grade assault rifle with detachable magazine. Loud and devastating. **2 load.** 

**Heat blade:** The latest in military technology, an advanced electro-blade that superheats to red-hot intensity. Can cut through steel. Well balanced and deadly. **1 load.** 

**A few grenades:** They go boom. **1 load.** 

_Military-grade weapons and explosives, such as the Veteran’s items, garner +1 Heat (total, not per item) during the aftermath of the score. They are highly restricted._ 

**Pocketful of go-go pills:** Xantara Pharm’s finest uppers, for when you need pure, explosive energy. _You’ll run your mouth (what do you say that will get you in trouble?), and take the passing harm “jittery” when they wear off (these consequences can be resisted)._ **0 load.** 

**RF radio handset:** A resonance field radio. A small handheld unit tuned to a secure frequency. **0 load.** 

## **Veteran Special Abilities** 

## **MILITARY DISCIPLINE** 

Twice per score, you may use your **training** to resist harm from an attack in combat or to **push yourself** during a fight. 

_When you use this ability, tick one of the training boxes on your sheet. If you resist harm, that means the level of harm you’re facing right now is reduced by one. If you use this ability to push yourself, you get one of the benefits (+1d, +1 effect) but you don’t take 2 Stress. Your training uses are restored at the beginning of downtime._ 

## **GOT YOUR BACK** 

When you **protect** a teammate, clear **1 Stress** and take + **1d** to any resistance rolls. 

_The protect teamwork maneuver lets you face a consequence for a teammate. When you do so, clear 1 Stress. If you choose to resist that consequence, this ability also gives you +1d to all resistance rolls related to it._ 

82 

## **ECHO FIGHTER** 

Thanks to special training, you may engage enemies in combat with nothing but your mind. You gain **potency** in combat vs. the paranormal. You can attempt to read people’s next intentions. 

_Psychically assaulting someone from a distance with this ability typically involves a_ _**Command** action._ 

_What does this psychic combat technique look like for you? Do you just stare at your opponent really hard (perhaps you practiced on goats), or hold your fingers to your temples, or do you project ghostly fists of resonance energy? Whatever the technique, while it has the advantage of being potent against the paranormal, it’s also useful against regular opponents._ 

_Reading someone’s next intentions generally requires a roll; Attune or Study are usually applicable choices._ 

## **LEADERSHIP** 

When you **Command** a **cohort** in combat, they continue to fight when they would otherwise **break** (they’re not taken out when they suffer level 3 harm). They gain **increased effect** and **1 armor** . 

_This ability makes your cohorts more effective in battle and also allows them to resist harm by using armor. While you lead your cohorts, they won’t stop fighting until they take fatal harm (level 4) or you order them to cease. What’s your style of leadership?_ 

## **WALKING ARSENAL** 

Your load limit is always 2 higher than normal (5 for a Quiet approach, 8 for Loud). Pull out another 1-load gun at any time, no matter how many you’ve already used. Each additional gun of its type (after the first) is 0 load. 

_Since your exact gear is determined on the fly during an operation, having more load gives you more options to get creative during a score. Since you can always pull another gun out, don’t be shy about asking for relevant Devil’s Bargains—having a gun jam, being disarmed, emptying your clip and tossing the gun, etc. That’s what this ability is for._ 

_Note that this ability doesn’t allow infinite free guns for the whole crew; any gun you hand off to another character counts toward their load limit, even though it doesn’t count toward yours._ 

83 

## **WAR MACHINE** 

When you **push yourself** , you can also do one of the following: _sweep and_ — _secure a large area single-handedly and without pausing engage an improbable number of enemies in a ballet of violence._ 

_When you push yourself to activate this ability, you still get one of the normal benefits of pushing yourself (+1d or +1 effect) in addition to the special ability. This kind of ability lets you do something that most characters can’t, but a roll might still be required if there is a threat or obstacle, as usual._ 

_To sweep and secure a large area means you make it safe for you and your allies, at least for now; you force hostiles to retreat, moving forward and securing the area with relentless precision. If you engage an improbable number of enemies, you don’t suffer reduced effect due to scale (“improbable” is the operative word—perhaps up to 10 hostiles, depending on context)._ 

## **GET BACK IN THERE** 

You were subject to experimental procedures designed to increase the shelf-life of front-line soldiers. Permanently fill in one of your healing clock segments. Take + **1d** to healing treatment rolls. 

_Your healing clock becomes a 3-clock, and you get a bonus die when you recover. What was the nature of the experiments done to you? What telltale marks did they leave on your body?_ 

## **CREATIVE COMMUNITY** 

You gain a second vice: learning a new creative hobby. What is it? When you indulge this vice by going to class, add + **2** to the result, and then create a new **friend** or **rival** (classmate or teacher), or develop your relationship with an existing one. These people have no criminal utility, but they might give you a ride or let you lay low at their place in a pinch. When you overindulge, one of these friends is put in danger. 

_What is your amateur hobby? Perhaps acting, poetry, singing, pottery, flower arranging, or painting figurines? The bonus from this ability is a flat addition—if your highest die from indulging vice is a 4, you clear 6 Stress (4 + 2). This ability allows you to clear up to 8 Stress._ 

_This ability should give your character a second life separate to their life of violence and crime. Take a few moments each time you indulge this vice to figure out who some of your fellow hobbyists are; they should be regular people. How does your relationship to these people change and evolve? How does this effect the Veteran? Do they dream of “going pro” and leaving their life of crime behind?_ 

84 

_The likelihood of overindulging is higher than normal. When you do, a friend is put into danger instead of choosing an overindulgence as usual. This danger should start light (resolved with free play only, no rolls) and gradually become more serious the more times you overindulge._ 

_The overindulgence might start to require an action roll, then it might tick a clock, and when the clock is filled, it might eventually require a long-term project or even a score to resolve._ 

## **Veteran Questions** 

After crew creation and character creation, your group can run through background questions together. Take turns introducing your characters, and then take turns asking the group one of the following questions (your choice), or make up your own question. 

Anyone can answer, and together you can flesh out some of the details. 

- Which of you was unable to pull the trigger, so I did it for you? 

- Which of you have I promised to protect? 

- Which of you is my drinking buddy? 

- Which of you pities me? 

- Which of you helps me with my disability, my damage? 

- Which of you have I confided my recurring nightmare to? 

Then go around again—ask another question from the list, or pass. When everyone has passed, move on to crew questions. 

85 

## ART PLACEHOLDER 

86 

## Crew Creation 

Your crew type determines the scores that you’ll focus on, as well as a selection of special abilities and claims that support that kind of action. The crew type isn’t meant to be completely restrictive—a crew of Racers might sometimes engage in heists (like Shadows) or sell contraband (like Dealers)— but the core activity of the crew type is the most frequent way they earn stacks and xp for advancement. 

## **Choose a Crew Type** 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0097-04.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Dealers Pushers who acquire and sell illegal product: drugs,<br>literature, paranormal experience, or any other<br>contraband.<br>Hit Squad Professional killers for hire. Some have a code, others<br>just take the job. Accidents, disappearances, murders,<br>and ransom operations.<br>Militants Revolutionary activists who know the only way to<br>create real change is to break the system.<br>Assassinations, demonstrations, sabotage, and battle.<br>Racers Thrill-seekers and daredevils who execute smuggling<br>operations, hijackings, hot pursuits, and compete in<br>dangerous races.<br>Shadows Infiltration experts who specialize in elaborate heists<br>and high-stakes espionage.<br>Utopians An esoteric cult working toward a utopian dream. They<br>may start with good intentions, but they’re on a dark<br>road to damnation.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


87 

Grab the crew sheet for your chosen type (and the generic base sheet used by all crew types) and record the following choices in crew creation as you go. Your crew begins with **2 stacks** in its coffers (the remains of the PCs’ savings). You are **Tier 0** , with **strong hold** and **0 Rep** . 

## **Choose an Initial Reputation** 

Your crew has just formed and acquired a base of operations. Given this group of characters and their previous escapades, what initial **reputation** would you have among the factions of the underworld? Choose one from the following list, or create your own. You earn xp when you bolster your crew’s reputation, so think of this as another cue to indicate what sorts of action you want in the game. 

- Ambitious 

- Flashy 

- Daring 

- Honorable 

- Ruthless 

- Professional 

- Calculating 

- Freewheeling 

- Subtle 

- Eccentric 

- Loyal 

- Deceptive 

- Stubborn 

- Menacing 

- Strategic 

- Relentless 

- Tenacious 

- Groovy 

Also talk about the crew’s **base** . This could grow into something grand in time, but starting at Tier 0, it’s a fixer-upper with potential. 

- An abandoned **department store** . 

- An underground **bunker complex** . 

- A gloomy **warehouse** on the docks. 

- The floors above (or below) a **smoky lounge bar** or **bouncing nightclub** . 

- A **decrepit mansion** . Who inherited it? 

- A **junkyard** and **auto shop** . 

Choose the district in which your base is found. Are you based in some derelict area of a wealthy district, or is your base one of many other run-down buildings in a destitute area? A good district choice is Crowfoot—known for its street gangs and open criminal activity, but also swinging music, fashion, and nightclubs. 

88 

## **Base Flair** 

Choose two pieces of flair that you’ve added to the base. They have no direct mechanical effect, but might play a part in fictional context (especially for unwind scenes). Whenever you go up in Tier, choose another piece of flair for the base. 

- Bar 

- Conversation pit with shag carpet 

- Discothèque 

- Sauna 

- Professional kitchen 

- Dining room 

- Library 

- Cinema 

- Swimming pool 

- Aquarium 

- Conference room 

- Wine cellar 

- Plant conservatory 

   - Trophy room (glass cases with spotlighting) 

   - Communication hub (telephones, radios, plasmovision sets) 

   - Meditation room 

   - Game room 

   - Art studio 

   - Music room 

   - Tea parlor 

   - Ball court 

   - Front business (laundrette, autopod-wash, real estate office, art gallery, taxi service, restaurant, etc.) 

- Stellar observatory 

## **Define Your Hunting Grounds, Meet Your Ward Boss** 

Your crew is brand-new, but you have chosen some small part of a district as your **hunting grounds** . This is the area that you usually target for your scores, and you know it well. Your hunting grounds don’t have to be in the same district as your base. The area is small, only three or four city blocks—but it’s still claimed by somebody. The GM will tell you which faction is your local **ward boss** , then you decide how to deal with them: 

- Give them **1 stack** in exchange for giving you room to work. 

- Pay the faction **2 stacks** as a show of respect and gain +1 status with them. 

- Keep your money and take - **1 status** with that faction. 

When you prepare to execute an operation of your preferred type on your hunting grounds, you get **+1d** to any gather information rolls and a **free additional downtime activity** to contribute to that operation. 

Secondary scores in your hunting grounds gain +1d. 

When you acquire turf, decide which district it’s in and how large it is. You also choose a new preferred operation type. 

89 

## **Tithes** 

After every score, **pay stacks equal to your crew Tier +1** as a tithe to your ward boss. If you choose not to pay, add one tick to their 4-segment **anger** clock. Every time it fills up, lose 1 faction status with them, and there may be other reprisals. 

## **Becoming the Ward Boss** 

At a certain point, you may wish to supplant your ward boss. This requires going to war and forcing them to surrender. It may have other requirements such as a long-term project. 

Once you’re the ward boss, you no longer have to pay a tithe. In fact, the crew gains **1 stack** every downtime in tithes from smaller crews. Helping your vassal crews grow in Tier, either through scores or long-term projects, might increase the stacks you gain in tithes. They might also drag you into their own conflicts. And always watch your back—they have their eye on your crown. 

## **Choose a Special Ability** 

Take a look at the special abilities for your crew and choose one. It’s important to pick a special ability that everyone is excited about. You can get more special abilities in the future by earning xp. 

## **Assign Crew Upgrades** 

Each crew type has two pre-selected upgrades that suit that crew (like Resolve training and a gang of muscle for the Militants crew). 

You get to add two additional upgrades to your new crew (so you’ll have a total of four upgrades when you start). You can choose from the specific upgrades available to your crew type or the general upgrades on the crew sheet. 

When you assign your two upgrades, the GM will tell you about two factions that are impacted by your choices: 

- One faction helped you get an upgrade. They like you, and you get **+1 status** with them. At your option, spend **1 stack** to repay their kindness, and take **+2 status** with them instead. 

- One faction was screwed over when you got an upgrade. They don’t like you, and you get **-2 status** with them. At your option, spend **1 stack** to mollify them, and take **-1 status** with them instead. 

90 

## **Choose a Favorite Contact** 

Take a look at your list of potential contacts on the crew sheet. Choose one contact who is a close friend, long-time ally, or partner in crime. The GM will tell you about two factions that are impacted by your choice: 

- One faction is also friendly with this contact, and you get **+1 status** with them. 

- One faction is unfriendly with this contact, and you get **-1 status** with them. 

At your option, these factions are even more concerned with this contact and so you take **+2** and **-2 status** instead. 

## **Crew Upgrade Details** 

- **Boat:** You have a boat, a dock on a waterway, and a small shack to store boating supplies. A second upgrade improves the boat with armor and more cargo capacity. 

- **Cohort:** A cohort is a gang or a single expert NPC who works for your crew. For all the details on cohorts, see the following page. 

- **Lounge and Quarters:** Your lair includes a shared lounge as well as living quarters for the crew. Add another piece of flair to the base. **Whenever the crew unwinds (at the end of crew business), clear all passing harm.** Without this upgrade, each PC sleeps elsewhere, and is vulnerable when they do so. 

- **Mastery:** Your crew has access to master-level training. You may advance your PCs’ action ratings to 4 (until you unlock this upgrade, PC action ratings are capped at 3). This costs four upgrade boxes to unlock. 

- **Quality:** Each upgrade improves the Quality rating of all the PCs’ items of that type, beyond the Quality established by the crew’s Tier and fine items. You can improve the Quality of Documents, Gear (covers Burglary Gear and Climbing Gear), Paranormal Implements, Subterfuge Supplies, Tools (covers Demolitions Tools and Tinkering Tools), and Weapons. 

- **Secret Base:** Your base has a secret location and is disguised to hide it from view. Maybe it’s a new base, or maybe you find a way to hide your current base. If you’re **raided** , it can’t be at your base until they work out where it is (if they try to raid you outside your base, you take **+2d** to your engagement roll). If your base is discovered, use two downtime activities and pay stacks equal to your Tier to hide it once again. 

91 

- **Security Systems:** Your lair has cameras, alarms, and traps to thwart intruders. If you’re **raided** , add **+1d to the engagement roll** and you have always have access to a minimum of **4 load** . A second upgrade improves the defenses to include measures that work against paranormal intrusion, and you add **+2d** total to raid engagement rolls. 

- **Training:** If you have a Training upgrade, you earn 2 xp (instead of 1) when you train a given xp track during downtime ( **Insight** , **Prowess** , **Resolve** , or **playbook** ). This upgrade essentially helps you advance more quickly. 

- **Van:** You have a transport autopod, big enough for the whole crew and their gear. A second upgrade improves the van with armor and a more powerful engine. 

- **Vault:** Your base has a secure vault, increasing your storage capacity for **stacks** to 8. A second upgrade increases your capacity to 16. A separate part of your vault can be used as a holding cell. 

- **Workshop:** Your base has a workshop with tools for tinkering and invention, some sparktech equipment like a tape recorder and basic computer, as well as a collection of books, documents, and maps. You may accomplish longterm projects with these assets without leaving your base. When you work on an **invention long-term project** with the workshop, **increase the result level of the roll by one** . You can spend stacks to increase the result further as usual. 

Looking for crew xp and advancement? See _Blades in the Dark_ , page 49. For Rep, hold, and increasing Tier, see _Blades in the Dark_ , page 44. 

92 

## Cohorts 

A cohort is a **gang** or an **expert** who works for your crew. To recruit a new cohort, spend two upgrades and create them using the following process. 

## **Creating a Gang** 

Choose a **gang type** from the following list: 

- **Eggheads:** Scholars, scientists, and tinkerers. 

- **Hustlers:** Con artists, undercover agents, and socialites. 

- **Runners:** Drivers, scouts, and couriers. 

- **Infiltrators:** Spies, sneaks, and thieves. 

- **Muscle:** Heavies, brawlers, and thugs. 

A gang has **scale** and **Quality** equal to your current crew Tier. It increases in scale and Quality when your crew moves up in Tier. 

Some crew upgrades will add the “Elite” feature to a gang, which gives them +1d when they roll for a given type. _So, if you’re Tier 1 and have a gang of Elite Muscle (+1d), they would roll 2d when they try to kill a target._ 

## **Creating an Expert** 

Record the expert’s **type** (their specific area of expertise). 

**Example Experts:** _Doctor, Investigator, Occultist, Hitman, Spy, Demolitionist, Surveillance Specialist, Counterfeiter, Chemist, Psychologist, Sparktech, Socialite, Musician, Escape Artist, Stunt Driver, Weaponsmith, Con Artist, PR Expert, Art Forger, Chef, Martial Artist, Fashion Designer, Locksmith, Pharmacist, Psychic Medium, Documentarian, Airship Pilot, Lawyer, Big Pet, Resonance Entity._ 

An expert has **Quality** equal to your current crew Tier +1. Their scale is always 0 (one person). Your experts increase in Quality when your crew moves up in Tier. 

93 

## **Edges & Flaws** 

When you create a cohort, give them one or two edges and an equal number of flaws. 

## **Edges** 

- **Fearsome:** The cohort is terrifying in aspect and reputation. 

- **Independent:** The cohort can be trusted to make good decisions and act on their own initiative in the absence of direct orders. 

- **Loyal:** The cohort can’t be bribed or turned against you. 

- **Resourceful:** The cohort thinks outside the box, and they’re good at improvised solutions. 

- **Tenacious:** The cohort won’t be deterred from a task. 

- **Vigilant:** The cohort is always alert and ready. 

## **Flaws** 

- **Principled** : The cohort has an ethic or values that it won’t betray. 

- **Ruthless:** The cohort is excessively violent and cruel. 

- **Clumsy:** The cohort is prone to accidents and mistakes. 

- **Hedonistic:** The cohort is often drunk, high, or otherwise intoxicated. 

- **Panicky:** The cohort is prone to fear and anxiety. 

- **Superstitious:** The cohort is overly fearful of bad omens, curses, and paranormal threats. 

## **Modifying a Cohort** 

You can add an **additional type** to a gang or expert by spending two crew upgrades. When a cohort performs actions for which its types apply, it uses its full Quality rating. Otherwise, its Quality is 0. A given cohort can have up to two types. 

## **Using a Cohort** 

When you send a cohort to achieve a goal, roll their **Quality** to see how it goes. Or, a PC can oversee the maneuver by leading a **group action** . The Quality of any opposition relative to the cohort’s Quality affects the position and effect of the action. 

94 

## **Cohort Harm & Healing** 

Cohorts suffer harm similarly to PCs. A cohort can suffer four levels of harm: 

1. **Weakened.** The cohort has reduced effect. 

2. **Impaired.** The cohort operates with reduced Quality (-1d). 

3. **Broken.** The cohort can’t do anything until they recover. 

4. **Dead.** The cohort is destroyed. 

If a cohort is destroyed, it may be replaced. Spend **stacks** equal to your Tier +2 to restore it, plus a downtime activity to recruit new gang members or hire a new expert. 

95 

## Cohort Actions 

Cohorts can help out, both during personal business and crew business. 

## **Personal Business** 

Each cohort gets one downtime action per personal business phase. They cannot pay for more. Choose one: 

- **Assist:** Assist a PC with their downtime activity, if they have relevant skills (Acquire Asset, Long-Term Project, or Reduce Heat). The PC gets **bonus dice** equal to the cohort’s Quality (minimum +1d). _For example, your gang of runners assist on your Long-Term Project activity by driving you around; you choose an action to roll as normal, and add their Quality as bonus dice._ 

- **Long-Term Project:** If they have the relevant skills, a cohort can work on a long-term project by themselves. Roll their Quality. 

- **Reduce Heat:** Roll their Quality. 

- **Recover:** The cohort recovers two levels of harm. 

## **Crew Business** 

Cohorts also take part in crew business. After the planning meeting, choose one of the following for each cohort: 

**Primary score** . The cohort is around to help out during your main score, as needed. You can have them perform tasks during the score, making a fortune roll with their Quality to see how they do. They can also join group actions, again using their Quality (if their type is applicable). 

**Secondary score** . Pick one of the opportunities you didn’t take during the planning meeting, and a cohort can attempt it. Only one secondary score can be attempted, regardless of how many cohorts you have. Playbook cohorts cannot take on secondary scores. 

The cohort will expect a **cut** if the score is successful—a payment of stacks equal to their **Quality +1** . If you can’t or won’t pay their cut, give the cohort the flaw _Mutinous_ until the situation is resolved to their satisfaction. 

Remember that when a cohort’s type applies, you can use its full Quality rating, but otherwise its Quality is 0. The cohort’s type should be compared against the nature of the score, and if it doesn’t apply, then the cohort’s Quality will be 0. 

96 

_The Crowfoot Chancers have Elite Infiltrators with a Quality of 4. They send them on a secondary score. Since the score involves breaking into a building, the Infiltrators get to roll their Quality._ 

_The cohort’s cut will be 5 stacks, but the score pays 8 so the crew will still makes a profit of 3 stacks._ 

Roll the cohort’s Quality to determine how the secondary score went. If the score is a preferred operation in the crew’s hunting grounds, add +1d. 

The score is a **failure** , and the cohort marks **harm** equal to **1-3** half the payout of the score, rounded down (e.g. _for a score with a 7 stack payout, they take 3 harm)_ . Consider other repercussions like Heat, negative faction status, and/or clock ticks, depending on the scope of the score and the Tier of the target relative to the crew’s Tier. The score is **successful** , but the cohort marks **1 harm** , and **4/5** the crew takes **3 Heat** . The crew gains **1 Rep** . The cohort gets paid their cut. The score is **successful** , and the cohort returns unharmed. **6** The crew takes **2 Heat** . The crew gains **2 Rep** . The cohort gets paid their cut. The score is **successful** , with zero Heat, and the cohort **Critical** achieves something extra—they stole some extra loot (bonus stacks), or they got in good with another faction (positive faction status), etc. The crew gains **2 Rep** . The cohort gets paid their cut. 

97 

## **Crew Type ONE of SIX** DEALERS 

**PUSHERS WHO ACQUIRE AND SELL ILLEGAL PRODUCT** 

**When you play Dealers, you earn xp when you execute a successful bulk acquisition, bulk sale, social intrigue, or show of force operation.** Instead of hunting grounds, you have a sales territory where you sell your product. 

98 

## **Starting Upgrades** 

- **Lair: Secure** 

- **Cohort: Gang (Hustlers)** 

## **The Product** 

Choose the category of product that you deal in, and consider the details. Do you deal in one specific item, or a broad range? Maybe this will change as your crew develops and expands. 

## **Narcotics** 

- **Echo weed.** A plant native to the resonance field that can be smoked for a mild high. Calming, with very minor hallucinatory effects. 

- **White lotus.** Black lotus can be refined into the soft crystals known as white lotus. When injected or smoked, it produces euphoric relaxation. Dangerously addictive. 

- **Blood powder.** Bloodneedle was a fairly obscure drug, but this refined version is rapidly gaining popularity. A red powder, typically snorted, that gives a temporary burst of fevered mania and rampant energy. 

- **Trance powder.** A glittering blue powder that induces a pleasant hypnotic trance when inhaled. Old-fashioned, but with a resurgence in popularity amongst alternative truth-seekers. 

- **Rainbow mushrooms.** Before the invention of bluetime, Doskvol was a city that ran on mushrooms, with rich and poor alike cultivating them for food. As such, psychedelic mushrooms have been well-understood for centuries, 

99 

although always frowned upon by the authorities. In the last decade, there has been a renewed interest in these psychoactive psychedelics, particularly by those seeking to expand their consciousness. 

- **Lysid.** Compound 25, Dream Dots, Void Acid. A recently invented synthetic chemical that induces total embodiment in the resonance field. Initially studied by the Ministry of Discovery as a tool for unlocking latent paranormal powers, lysid is now used much more widely in the pursuit of psychedelic enlightenment, and by those just looking for a good time. 

## **Blackmarket goods** 

- **Pirated records.** Music has never been bigger, raking in cash from the young and trendy. But records are expensive, and some releases are hard to get a hold of. Pirates with a good ear for the next big thing can make a killing. 

- **Art and antiques.** The art world is also exploding, and the most popular pieces fetch eye-watering sums. The perfect target for some not-quitelegal disruption. 

- **Fresh food.** Although Bowmore Fields produces more fresh food than ever before, the lion’s share still goes to the wealthy. The poorest of Doskvol are forced to subsist on nutriwafer, a dry daily mouthful of nutrients. There’s a big market for good, fresh food supplied by those willing to break the law. 

- **Luxuries.** Blackmarket staples like perfume, watches, whiskey, and handbags, avoiding the usual taxes and fees. 

- **Stolen autopods.** Highly coveted, but very expensive when acquired through legitimate channels. 

## **Restricted or prohibited items** 

- **Banned books, films, music.** Between the Church, the Ministry of Stability, and Section 6, many harmless cultural products fall victim to the censor’s scrutiny. 

- **Paranormal books or artifacts.** Even more highly controlled are books and artifacts related to the occult and arcane. 

- **Dangerous deathlands wildlife.** Deathlands fauna is strictly forbidden inside the Bubble, but that doesn’t stop the rich and famous from wanting their own exotic pets. 

- **Alluvium.** The very substance of the resonance field—quantum instability in physical form. A critical component in most paranormal experiments. Rare, unstable, and highly illegal. 

- **Weapons and military equipment.** The ’60s are a powderkeg waiting to blow, and many factions are willing to pay a premium to be properly armed. 

None of these are better or more profitable than the others, so pick whichever fits the vibe you’re going for. You can also make up your own unique product. 

100 

## **Preferred Operations** 

Unlike other crews, Dealers start with a single turf claim instead of hunting grounds. Decide which district your starting turf is in. The district might be informed by the product you sling, and the kind of clientele you sell to. _Perhaps you hawk counterfeit art to the rich and powerful in Brightstone, or maybe you sling echo weed and mushrooms to students and faculty at Charterhall University._ 

What kind of locations do you target? _Street corners, alleyways, nightclubs, warehouses, seedy hotels, underground bars, casinos, private residences, empty lots, bookstores, libraries, antique shops, pawn shops, record stores._ 

Finally, choose a preferred operation type. You can choose a new favored operation each time you acquire more turf. 

- **Show of Force.** Make an example of an enemy to dominate territory. 

- **Social Intrigue.** Jockey for influence and power in Doskvol’s web of factions. 

- **Bulk Acquisition.** Acquire a large amount of new product with one score. Product units should form the majority (if not all) of the payout. 

- **Bulk Sale.** Sell a large amount of product units with one score. This should involve trading units from the crew’s stash exchanged at a healthy rate (negotiated with the GM), in addition to a regular payout. 

## **Contacts** 

- **Sevoy** , a magistrate. _Perhaps a powerful figure with a taste for your particular product?_ 

- **Vera** , an airship pilot. _Perhaps a smuggler who sees your potential?_ 

- **Blodgett** , a Bluecoat. _Perhaps an informant within the law?_ 

- **Sloan** , a gang boss. _Perhaps a business partner who can provide muscle?_ 

- **Marlyn** , a party animal. _Perhaps someone who can get you an invite to places you shouldn’t be?_ 

- **Crimson** , a fixer. _Perhaps a connect between the best suppliers, smugglers, and buyers?_ 

## **Dealer Upgrades** 

- **Dealer Rigging:** One carried item is concealed and has no load. This does not work for armor. _For example, you could carry a load of drugs or a weapon, perfectly concealed, for zero load._ 

- **Elite Muscle:** All your cohorts with the Muscle type get +1d to Quality rolls for Muscle-related actions. 

101 

- **Elite Hustlers:** All your cohorts with the Hustlers type get +1d to Quality rolls for Hustler-related actions. 

- **Intriguing:** Each PC gets +1 key/deadlock box, meaning they can each take another key (which can become another deadlock). This costs three upgrades to unlock, not just one. _This may bring a PC with four deadlocks back into play if you wish._ 

## **Dealer Claims** 

Unlike other crews, Dealer claims are about assembling your product-dealing infrastructure. By working on supply, demand, distribution, and competitive advantages, Dealers can start making a large amount of stacks over and above the payout from individual scores. 

To begin with, your crew can use their starting sales territory to **move 1 unit** of product for **1 stack** during downtime (take **1 Heat** when you do). You’ll have to acquire the units of product with a score. 

## **SUPPLY** 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0112-07.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
LOCAL  LOCAL<br>SMUGGLER MANUFACTURER AIRSHIP<br>SUPPLIER SUPPLIER<br>DEMAND<br>LUXUR Y  KEY<br>LOCAL FIENDS CITY-WIDE VIP CLIENTS<br>VENUE INFLUENCER<br>COMPETITIVE ADVANTAGES<br>MONEY  TOP SECRET  MONEY<br>BRANDI NG MONO POLY<br>LAUNDERING INTEL LAUNDERING<br>DISTRIBUTION<br>TURF TURF TURF TURF TURF<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


To expand this operation, you must unlock **claims** . Dealers have four claim tracks—supply, demand, competitive advantages, and distribution. Progress along each track by unlocking claims from left to right. The second Demand claim can only be unlocked _after_ either the second Supply or Competitive Advantage is unlocked. 

- **Supply** claims allow you to **gain** more units every downtime. 

- **Demand** claims mean that you make **more stacks** when you move product. 

- **Competitive advantages** can help manage Heat, and lead to other big advantages. 

- **Distribution** claims allow you to **move more** product units. 

102 

## **SUPPLY CLAIMS** 

**Local Supplier:** Once per personal business phase, take **1 Heat** to gain **1 unit** . 

**Smuggler:** Once per personal business phase, take **1 Heat** to gain **2 units** . 

**Manufacturer:** Once per personal business phase, take **1 Heat** to gain **2 units** . 

**Airship:** Once per personal business phase, take **1 Heat** to gain **3 units** . 

_If you have access to all five Supply claims, you could take 5 Heat to gain 9 units. Alternatively, you could choose to just use the airship and the manufacturer, taking 2 Heat to gain 5 units._ 

## **DEMAND CLAIMS** 

**Local Fiends:** All turf generates **+1 stack** when moving units. _Who are these local customers? Who do they currently buy from?_ 

**City-Wide:** All turf generates **+1 stack** when moving units. _How will you generate city-wide demand?_ 

**Luxury Venue:** You get **+1d** to Consort and Sway on-site, and take **+2 stacks** payout for social intrigue scores. 

**Key Influencer:** All turf generates **+1 stack** when moving units. 

**VIP Clients:** All turf generates **+1 stack** when moving units. 

## **COMPETITIVE ADVANTAGES** 

**Branding:** You get **+1d** to the engagement roll for social plans, and take **+2 stacks** payout for bulk sale or bulk acquisition. _What’s unique about your product, and how are you going to get the word out there?_ 

**Money Laundering:** Take **-3 Heat** from gaining/moving units, every personal business phase. This only offsets any Heat from dealing activities, and cannot result in negative total Heat. 

**Top Secret Intel:** Unlocking this claim means you get **+2d** to the **engagement roll** for the **Monopoly one-off opportunity** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Monopoly:** This claim is a one-off opportunity against a **Tier 5 target** , and if successful, all **Turf** can move **2 units** per personal business phase for the same Heat. For example, by default, each Turf can move 1 unit for 1 stack, at the cost of 1 Heat—if you gain a monopoly, each Turf can move 2 units for 2 stacks, at the cost of 1 Heat (Demand claims would further increase the payout). This is a huge advantage, and quite possibly the end of the campaign. _The Tier 5 target might be made up of multiple smaller factions— gaining a monopoly means taking out or absorbing every competitor, after all._ 

## **DISTRIBUTION** 

**Turf: 1 unit** can be moved for **1 stack** during the personal business phase (take **1 Heat** when you do). 

If a claim is lost, all claims that are only accessible via that claim are unavailable until the link is restored. _If you lose your smuggler, you lose access to your manufacturer and airship until you get the smuggler back._ 

103 

## **MONEY MONEY MONEY** 

Dealers can become incredibly wealthy, eventually hauling in 10+ stacks every personal business phase. While this might seem “broken,” remember: 

- **The crew has to unlock the claims first.** It will take several claims before the dealing machinery becomes especially profitable, and this could take most of the campaign. Crews don’t usually gain a claim every score. 

- **Success attracts attention.** Clever Dealers will find ways to run circles around the inept local Bluecoats, but Heat isn’t the only way to gain Wanted Levels. The crew might attract the attention of an Inspector’s Mandate (see page 190), and they will certainly become the target of larger factions who want those healthy profits for themselves. 

- **They’re allowed to win.** If the crew makes smart choices, evades the law, and builds a dealing machine that makes them rich and powerful, that’s perfectly acceptable. Maybe they get to retire to a life of luxury, and you can start a new campaign. 

If a crew’s dealing activities become so profitable they no longer see the point in doing scores, other factions may start coming for their profits—meaning a cycle of raids (rather than scores), punctuated by personal business. 

## **Dealer Special Abilities** 

## **FIRST RATE** 

Your merchandise is exquisite. Gain potency when you **Sway** or **Consort** with those hooked on your product. When you deal with a crew or faction, the GM will tell you who among them is already hooked (one, a few, many, or all). 

_Note that the GM cannot answer “none,” so this ability means that whenever you deal with a crew or faction, there’s always at least one individual hooked on your product (whether that’s art, music, drugs, or whatever)._ 

## **ON RETAINER** 

You have an expert lawyer representing your crew. Their **Quality** is equal to **crew Tier + 2** . When you take the Reduce Heat downtime action, you can have your lawyer roll their Quality instead. When you take the rap, your Wanted Level counts as one lower for the purposes of sentencing. 

## **CAT AND MOUSE** 

The GM will tell you about any special Mandates investigating your crew, and put their clocks on the table from now on. You get + **2d** to the engagement roll against any raids (Mandates or otherwise). 

_Having these clocks on the table means you can start trying to counteract them, perhaps through your own long-term projects or scores._ 

104 

## **FIRST ONE’S FREE** 

You can give away your product to build Rep during downtime. **1 Rep** costs **1 unit** . 

## **FIELD TESTING** 

You can prepare a special cut of your product for use during a score. Choose an effect: _healing, exhilarating_ , _calming_ , or e _nlightening._ Each costs 1 unit of product, takes 1 load, and is consumed after one use. 

- **Healing** product clears all level 1 harm. 

- **Exhilarating** product clears 1 Stress. 

- **Calming** product, if enjoyed or consumed by a target, means that social actions (such as Consort or Sway) gain potency against them. 

- **Enlightening** product increases the result level on one gather information roll. 

_What does this special preparation involve? Is there a paranormal aspect? What does it mean for your particular product, whether that’s music, art, food, alluvium, or drugs?_ 

## **PAYMENT IN KIND** 

You can use units to purchase crew upgrades. **1 crew upgrade** costs **5 units** (so a new cohort would cost 10 units). 

## **BENEFACTOR** 

When you take this ability, the crew immediately receives **4 stacks** . Whenever you advance your **Tier** , it costs **half the stacks** it normally would. 

_Who’s backing you? Why do they help you?_ 

## **Dealer Questions** 

After character questions, your group can run through crew questions together. Each PC picks one from the following list that applies to you (or make up your own) and supply a few details about how you came to that role. You don’t have to go too in-depth—this is just to give a general sense of the shape of the crew as you begin. 

- Which of you has experience dealing? 

- Which of you has the best connections? 

- Which of you handles the books? 

- Which of you knows the streets best? 

- Which of you is most involved in preparing the product? 

- Which of you first suggested forming a crew? 

105 

## **Dealer Opportunities** 

During the planning meeting (page 180), each player (as well as the GM) will present an opportunity for a possible score that the crew might take. If anyone feels stuck, look at the following list and consider a Show of Force, Social Intrigue, Bulk Acquisition, or Bulk Sale approach for any of them. 

- **`1`** The newspaper headlines are all about a big contraband sting. The seized product is just sitting there in the local Bluecoat precinct station—it would be a shame for it to go to waste. 

- **`2`** An influential celebrity is hosting the biggest party of ’68. The perfect place to buy, sell, or otherwise build your Rep. 

- **`3`** Dealers of a competing product have set up shop in the same district. 

- **`4`** An infamous smuggler turned up dead in a canal. Their stash house is rumored to be hidden in the tunnels beneath Doskvol. Plenty of product sitting there for whoever gets to it first... 

- **`5`** A bigger outfit is consolidating power. They approach the crew to work for them—or else become enemies. 

- **`6`** A large criminal faction has had a falling out with one of their regular suppliers, and they’re shopping for new business partners. 

- **`1`** An airship crashed in the deathlands, and rumor is it was carrying a lot of contraband product. 

- **`2`** A washed-up musician is looking to reinvent herself—and wants a product no one’s seen before. 

- **`3`** You hear a famous intellectual dabbles in your kind of product. They’re a paranoid recluse, but if you could just have a moment of their time... 

- **`4`** A high-end restaurant is dealing product through an exclusive secret venue hidden in the basement. 

- **`5`** You get a tip-off about an irregularity in the rail schedule out of Gaddoc Station. Someone’s running an unlogged train. What could be on board? 

- **`6`** A resonance echo is haunting a local apartment block, and it wants only one thing—your product. 

106

**Crew Type TWO of SIX CONTRACT KILLERS— DISCREETAND SKILLED ASSASSINS** HIT SQUAD 

**When you play a Hit Squad, you earn xp when you execute a successful accident, disappearance, murder, or ransom operation** . _Are you professionals with a code you work to, or is anyone fair game?_ Between the Death Radar, Section 6, and paranormal instability, Doskvol is a dangerous place to be an assassin.

## **Starting Upgrades** 

- **Training: Prowess** 

- **Cohort: Gang (Muscle)** 

## **Hunting Grounds** 

Choose a favored operation type: 

- **Accident.** A killing with no telltale signs of murder. 

- **Disappearance.** The victim vanishes without a trace—does the client want them alive, or dead? 

- **Murder.** An obvious killing that sends a message. 

- **Ransom.** A kidnapping and demand for payment for their return. 

## **Contacts** 

- **Vestine Keel** , a crime boss. _Perhaps she helped your crew get started?_ 

- **Beesby** , a deal broker. _Perhaps they act as a liaison with your clients?_ 

- **Tilton** , a vengeful aristocrat. _Perhaps a potential patron for your crew?_ 

- **Mowsley** , a cult leader. _Perhaps willing to pay handsomely for someone else to do his dirty work?_ 

- **Hush** , a Reality Warden. _Perhaps a double agent informant for you?_ 

- **Yugo Xantara** , a powerful CEO. _Perhaps a connection to other wealthy clients?_
