## **Hit Squad Upgrades** 

- **Assassin Rigging:** You get 2 free load worth of weapon or gear items. _For example, you could carry a silenced shooter (a weapon) and burglary tools (gear) for zero load._ 

- **Elite Infiltrators:** All your cohorts with the Infiltrators type get +1d to Quality rolls for Infiltrator-related actions. 

- **Elite Muscle:** All your cohorts with the Muscle type get +1d to Quality rolls for Muscle-related actions. 

- **Deep:** Each PC gets +1 key/deadlock box, meaning they can each take another key (which can become another deadlock). This costs three upgrades to unlock, not just one. _This may bring a PC with four deadlocks back into play if you wish._ 

## **Hit Squad Claims**

This crew has five special claims on the claim map, including two **one-off opportunities** . For one-off opportunities, the “claim” is itself a lucrative score (with bonus rewards). If they have the connection on the claim map, the crew can attempt the one-off score at any time of their choosing. The opportunity doesn’t expire. 

110 

**City Records:** You get **+1d** to the **engagement roll** for **stealth** approaches. _You can use blueprints and other documents to determine a good approach for infiltrations._ 

**Clock the Routine:** Unlocking this claim means that during the **Legendary Target one-off opportunity** , the crew gets **three free flashbacks** . If these flashbacks involve a downtime activity, that extra activity is also free. The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Cover Identities:** You get **+1d** to the **engagement roll** for **deception** and **social** approaches. _False identities help confuse the opposition._ 

**Cover Operation:** You get **-2 Heat** per score. _The cover of a legitimate operation helps deflect some of the Heat from law enforcement._ 

**Detailed Map:** Unlocking this claim means you get **+2d** to the **engagement roll** for the **Legendary Target one-off opportunity** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Dispensary:** You get **+1d** to **healing treatment rolls** . _Easy access to all the best drugs and medicines._ 

**Dive Bar:** You get **+2 stacks** in payout for scores that involve low-class clients. _This dive bar gives you access to notable underworld figures._ 

**Double Contract:** Unlocking this claim means that the **Legendary Target oneoff opportunity** now includes a second hit, adding **+10 stacks** to its **payout** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. _Who’s the second target?_ 

learning about this special contract. _Which faction is protecting them?_ 

**Friendly Ink Rake:** You get **+1 Rep** per score. _A journalist at one of the tabloids glorifies your exploits, bolstering your reputation._ 

**Gambling Hall:** Any time during personal business, roll dice equal to your Tier. You earn **stacks** equal to the highest result, minus your **Heat** . 

**Hagfish Farm:** When you use the **Reduce Heat** downtime activity after a score that involves killing, you get **+1d** to the roll. _Quiet, convenient disposal of any bodies you left on the job._ 

**Informants** : You get **+1d** to gather information for a score. _Your eyes and ears on the streets are always on the lookout for new targets._ 

**Legendary Target:** This claim is a oneoff special score against a **Tier 5 target** , which yields **15 Rep** and **10 stacks** as payout. This is a very dangerous opportunity with a high payout. It’s probably the end of a season, or even the campaign. _What’s the obstacle to unlocking this opportunity—earning the right to attempt the contract from a special client, or learning of the target’s existence or whereabouts?_ 

**Protection Racket:** Any time during personal business, roll dice equal to your Tier. You earn **stacks** equal to the highest result, minus your **Heat** . 

**Shady Hotel:** Your Infiltrator cohorts get **+1 scale** . _Suitable accommodation means more gang members._ 

**VIP Lounge:** You get **+2 stacks** in payout for scores that involve highclass clients. _This lounge gives you access to wealthy clients._

111 

## **Hit Squad Special Abilities** 

## **TAKE THE SHOT** 

When any PC takes the decisive action to eliminate a key target, they get **+1d** . 

_The key words here are_ _**decisive action** and_ _**key target** . Both must apply. Examples might include taking a sniper shot at the mark, dropping poison into the target’s drink, cutting the brakes on their autopod, tricking them into walking out on to a sabotaged balcony, dropping a chandelier, tinkering with the sauna controls to set the temperature to “lethal,” etc._ 

## **UNDER THE RADAR** 

When you kill someone during a score, you can take 2 Stress so it doesn’t count toward Heat afterwards. How does your crew avoid the Death Radar? 

_When your crew kills someone, it doesn’t trigger the Death Radar at Section 6 Central, and no klaxon sounds. Is this because of some gadget or invention, or a paranormal ritual, or a contact on the inside at Section 6?_ 

## **CHAMELEONS** 

Take + **1d** to the **engagement** roll for **stealth** or **deception** approaches. When you subdue someone and don their outfit, the disguise has increased **effect** . 

_The second part of this ability only applies to disguises acquired during the score—you must subdue a target like a guard or servant, and steal their uniform. You gain increased effect when you do._ 

## **COLD STORAGE** 

Every crew member can always find a convenient place to hide a body near to hand. Take 1 Stress to hide the body in the resonance field instead (it will rematerialize after a few hours). 

_Convenient hiding places might include a dumpster, locker, closet, laundry hamper, sewer grate, folded up in a folding bed, the trunk of an autopod, under a tarp, in a wine barrel, down an elevator shaft, in a portable toilet, etc._ 

_How do you hide bodies in the resonance field? Is it a strange invention that every crew member carries, or some paranormal ritual?_ 

## **BENEFACTOR** 

When you take this ability, the crew immediately receives **4 stacks** . Whenever you advance your **Tier** , it costs **half the stacks** it normally would. 

_Who’s backing you? Why do they help you?_ 

112 

## **LOOPERS** 

Your crew is caught in an anomaly, and regularly experiences time loops where events are replayed. Usually you don’t retain memory between loops, but you can jump loops with some effort. Take 4 Stress after any action roll to **roll it again, and take the best result between the two rolls** _._ The second roll uses the exact same number of dice (pushes, assists, etc.). You can choose to do this after the GM has announced the consequences, but not after any resistance rolls. 

_Imagine the score playing out in splitscreen, like sliding doors. Which version of events will we follow as one becomes the main narrative?_ 

_Activating this ability costs a lot of Stress, but there are times when you will scrape together every bonus die and assist you can and still manage to roll poorly. Being able to roll the whole dice pool again to see if you can do better can be a lifesaver._ 

_What’s the origin of this ability? Was it the unintentional side effect of something the crew was exposed to, or the result of an ingenious invention or paranormal ritual? It may even be the result of something that happens in the future, which the crew is not aware of yet._ 

## **PROFESSIONALS** 

When you keep an operation quiet or make it look like an accident, you get half the Rep value of the target (round up) instead of zero. When you end **downtime** with zero Heat, take **+1 Rep** . 

_There are many clients who value quiet operations. This ability rewards you for keeping a low profile._ 

## **Hit Squad Questions** 

After character questions, your group can run through crew questions together. Each PC picks one from the following list that applies to you (or make up your own) and gives a few details about how you came to that role. You don’t have to go too in-depth—this is just to give a general sense of the shape of the crew as you begin. 

- Which of you first suggested forming a crew? 

- Which of you has a grand vision for the crew’s future? 

- Which of you enjoys this a little too much? 

- Which of you still feels uneasy about it? 

- Which of you has the most to lose if we get caught? 

- Which of you knows the streets best? 

113 

## **Hit Squad Opportunities** 

During the planning meeting (page 180), each player (as well as the GM) will present an opportunity for a possible score that the crew might take. If anyone feels stuck, look at the following list and consider an Accident, Disappearance, Murder, or Ransom approach for any of them. 

- **`1`** A bored and petty aristocrat wants to teach their rival a lesson. 

- **`2`** A bankrupt aristocrat offers the last of their wealth in return for revenge on a powerful lender, who repossessed their autopod and foreclosed on their mansion. 

- **`3`** An arms dealer is going to defect to the USC. Before they flee Doskvol, they’re attending one more high society event. Deal with the situation. 

- **`4`** Target a cult leader during their large annual gathering. 

- **`5`** A high-stakes gambler scored big against a powerful faction, and they want payback. 

- **`6`** A foreign spy will be conducting a handoff with a mole at a wax museum.

## **Crew Type THREE of SIX** MILITANTS 

**ACTIVISTS PUSHING FOR REVOLUTIONARY CHANGE** 

**When you play Militants, you earn xp when you execute a successful assassination, demonstration, sabotage, or battle operation.** This is a time of radical political and social upheaval—as Militants, you’re on the frontlines of the struggle. 

116 

## **Starting Upgrades** 

- **Training: Resolve** 

- **Cohort: Gang (Muscle)** 

## **The Cause** 

Instead of hunting grounds, choose two _Enemies of the Cause_ . You get +1d to gather information rolls and a free downtime activity for preferred operations against Enemies of the Cause. 

It may help to start by defining your cause, at least loosely. _Is your cause civil rights, anti-imperialism, anti-war, anti-hull, freedom from Bluecoats brutality, economic justice, workers’ rights, or something else?_ 

**Enemies of the Cause** might be: 

- **Strangford-Michter Financial.** A powerful investment firm with a habit of backing illegal ventures off the books. Has stakes in a large number of criminal groups and shady scientific projects. 

- **Imperial Military.** Garrisons are posted at Gaddoc Monorail Station, aboard the naval destroyer _Nightcastle_ , and at the Premier’s stronghold (about 1,000 troops in total). The military also runs a training camp east of Doskvol for fresh conscripts, along with a prison for draft dodgers and deserters. 

- **Section 6.** A powerful and shadowy government agency responsible for enforcing Reality Constancy Law (investigating anomalies and unlicensed paranormal experimentation). 

- **The Palace.** The Imperial Intelligence Agency, or I.I.A. 

117 

- **Ministry of Stability.** The governmental body that oversees border security, transportation, and the disbursement of food and other vital resources. Their pursuit of national stability also involves a program of surveillance and control. 

- **The Church.** They honor the life of the body and deem the transcendent, spiritual, or otherworldly to be heretical. Ruthless enforcers of conformity. 

- **Bluecoats.** The City Watch of Duskwall, tasked with upholding the law. Decades of PR have rebranded them as your friendly local constables, but they are still just as corrupt, violent, and cruel as ever. 

- **Lusk Reform Clinic.** Pioneers of the Lusk Reform Technique; they turn the most violent criminal into one of the Reformed (vacant-eyed hollows) and also produce a brand-new hull to serve the city. 

- **The Foundation.** A powerful consortium of property developers, architects, and builders. 

- **Xantara Pharm.** A profiteering pharmaceutical company. 

## **Preferred Operations** 

- **Assassination.** An obvious killing of a key NPC from an Enemy of the Cause faction. 

- **Demonstration.** A public act of defiance with symbolic meaning. Protests, occupying buildings, art projects, defacing a meaningful target. 

- **Sabotage.** Hurt an Enemy of the Cause by destroying some key piece of infrastructure. 

- **Battle.** Confront an Enemy of the Cause with direct armed resistance. Riots, clashing with law enforcement, fighting to control a key neighborhood or apartment, directly assaulting an HQ. 

## **Contacts** 

- **Davran** , a foreign diplomat. _Perhaps a potential patron for your crew?_ 

- **Hickling** , a union organizer. _Perhaps a fellow traveler, with their ear to the ground?_ 

- **Eaves** , a Palace handler. _Perhaps they’re willing to put their substantial intelligence resources behind you, if your revolutionary targets align with their own shady goals?_ 

- **Kannick** , a Blackthorn Park handler. _Perhaps an espionage player who sees you as an important pawn on the board?_ 

- **Sovata** , a student leader. _Perhaps someone with sympathetic politics who’s able to swing grassroots support behind you?_ 

- **Kastor** , a weapons dealer. _Perhaps a source for armaments and explosives?_ 

118 

## **Militant Upgrades** 

- **Militant Rigging:** You get 2 free load worth of weapon or armor items. _For example, you could be wearing armor for only 1 load, instead of 3._ 

- **Elite Runners:** All your cohorts with the Runner type get +1d to Quality rolls for Runner-related actions. 

- **Elite Muscle:** All your cohorts with the Muscle type get +1d to Quality rolls for Muscle-related actions. 

- **Complicated:** Each PC gets +1 key/deadlock box, meaning they can each take another key (which can become another deadlock). This costs three upgrades to unlock, not just one. _This may bring a PC with four deadlocks back into play if you wish._ 

## **Militant Claims** 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0129-07.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
SECRET   POPULAR  CRITICAL<br>EXPROPRIATION HOSTEL<br>CACHES SUPPORT STRIKE<br>CATALYST  TURF KEY   TURF “INTERVIEW<br>ACTION CONSPIRATOR ROOM”<br>GRASSROOT<br>INFORMANTS DONATIONS DISPENSARY SOCIAL CLUBS<br>SUPPORT<br>COVERT  BASE<br>TURF TURF MEETING HALL<br>FUNDING<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


This crew has five special claims on the claim map, including two **one-off opportunities** . The “claim” is itself a lucrative score (with bonus rewards). If they have the connection on the claim map, the crew can attempt the one-off score at any time of their choosing. It doesn’t expire. 

119 

**Catalyst Action:** This claim is a oneoff score against a Tier 4 target, and if successful, it creates a **new Tier 2 faction** that starts with **+2 status** with the crew. Having access to this claim means you have everything primed, ready to light the fuse. _What kind of faction will it create—a small cell that branches off your own crew, or a broad popular movement, or something in between? Which faction has to be hit to create the catalyst?_ 

**Critical Strike:** This claim is a one-off opportunity against a **Tier 5 target** , and if successful, that target faction **drops two Tiers immediately** . This is a very dangerous score with a highimpact result. It’s probably the end of a season, or even the campaign. _What’s the obstacle to unlocking this opportunity—learning some secret weakness of the target faction, or setting up a trap, or making sure there will be appropriate publicity?_ 

**Cover Identities:** You get **+1d** to the **engagement roll** for **deception** and **social** approaches. _False identities help confuse the opposition._ 

**Covert Funding:** You get **+2 stacks** payout scores that involve **sabotage** or **assassination** . _Who’s secretly funding your fight against the Enemies of the Cause? Why?_ 

**Dispensary:** You get **+1d** to **healing treatment rolls.** _Easy access to all the best drugs and medicines._ 

**Donations:** You get **+2 stacks** payout for scores that involve **battle** or **demonstration** . _Who’s donating money toward your fight against the Enemies of the Cause?_ 

**Expropriation:** Unlocking this claim means that the **Critical Strike one-off opportunity** now includes **+10 stacks** in its **payout** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. _What obstacle stands in the way of these resources?_ 

**Grassroot Support:** Unlocking this claim means that if you complete the **Catalyst Action one-off opportunity** , the resultant new faction starts with **+3 status** with your crew. The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Hostel:** Your Muscle cohorts get **+1 scale** . _Suitable accommodation means more gang members._ 

**Informants:** You get **+1d** to gather information for a score. _Your eyes and ears on the streets are always on the lookout for new targets._ 

**“Interview Room”: +1d** to **Command** and **Sway** on-site. 

**Key Conspirator:** Unlocking this claim means you get **+2d** to the **engagement roll** for the **Critical Strike one-off opportunity** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Meeting Hall: +1d** to **Consort** and **Sway** on-site. 

**Popular Support** : You get **+1d** to the **engagement roll** for **stealth** approaches. _Everyday people will help cover for you._ 

**Secret Caches:** You get **+1d** to **Acquire Asset rolls** . _You have secret stockpiles of various resources, which can be useful on their own, or used for barter when you need it._ 

**Social Clubs:** Any time during personal business, roll dice equal to your Tier. You earn **stacks** equal to the highest result, minus your **Heat** . 

120 

## **Militant Special Abilities** 

## **SYMPATHIZERS** 

The common citizenry of your home ground, and any turf you hold, are sympathetic to you and your cause. You can consider them allies (status +3). When asked, they will: give you shelter or a place to hide, redirect Bluecoats or other enemies, or give you other aid if they can. 

## **MUTUAL AID** 

You can lend support to one allied faction, and their Tier counts as one higher as long as you do. Your crew gets one free downtime action to work on one of that faction’s long-term project clocks, if you wish. You can switch support once per downtime. 

## **GUERRILLAS** 

When the target of a score is two or more Tier higher than you, take no penalty to the **engagement** roll, and gain **+2 Rep** after the score (whether you were successful or not). 

_Usually if the target of a score is higher Tier, the engagement roll suffers a -1 penalty. With this ability, there is no penalty (if the target is two or more Tier higher)._ 

## **ON THE SIDE OF THE OPPRESSED** 

You loudly and openly oppose the Bluecoats and their authoritarianism. You may count each Wanted Level as if it were turf. 

_The maximum Wanted Level is 4. Regardless of how much turf you hold (from this ability or otherwise), the minimum Rep cost to advance your Tier is always 6._ 

## **ABSOLUTE COMMITMENT** 

You have all sworn solemn vows of service to the cause. You get **+1d** to **resistance** rolls. 

_This ability only applies to PCs in the crew. It doesn’t confer any special resistance to your cohorts._ 

_If another crew type takes this ability as a versatile advance, they should decide what solemn vows they have sworn, and to what cause._ 

## **BENEFACTOR** 

When you take this ability, the crew immediately receives **4 stacks** . Whenever you advance your **Tier** , it costs **half the stacks** it normally would. 

_Who’s backing you? Why do they help you?_ 

121 

## **REVOLUTIONARIES** 

When you’re at war (-3 faction status), your crew does not suffer -1 hold and PCs still get two downtime activities, instead of just one. 

_If another crew type takes this ability as a versatile advance, they should decide what their revolutionary cause is._ 

## **Militant Questions** 

After character questions, your group can run through crew questions together. Each PC picks one from the following list that applies to you (or make up your own) and gives a few details about how you came to that role. You don’t have to go too in-depth—this is just to give a general sense of the shape of the crew as you begin. 

- Which of you first suggested forming a crew? 

- Which of you is the most devout believer in the cause? 

- Which of you is the most cynical? 

- Which of you has the most personal grudge against an Enemy of the Cause? 

- Which of you knows the streets best? 

- Which of you has the most to lose if we go to Ironhook? 

122 

## **Militant Opportunities** 

During the planning meeting (page 180), each player (as well as the GM) will present an opportunity for a possible score that the crew might take. If anyone feels stuck, look at the following list and consider an Assassination, Demonstration, Sabotage, or Battle approach for any of them. 

**How do Militants get paid?** The payout might be **seized directly from the target** during the score. **Local supporters** (victims, families, grassroots groups) might pool their savings to support the crew. A **rival faction of the target** may pay the militant crew, using them as a catspaw (particularly common for espionage factions, but could also be one corporation paying the crew to target another corporation, etc.). **Sympathetic insiders** (officials and bureaucrats) might funnel money to the crew, off the books, to do what they cannot. 

- **`1`** Undermine a political rally or parade staged by an Enemy of the Cause. 

- **`2`** Target a power transfer station, rail line, communications tower, or factory that supports an Enemy of the Cause. 

- **`3`** Remove or publicly shame a prominent politician, officer, financier, or other collaborator of an Enemy of the Cause. 

- **`4`** Tear down or deface a monument, statue, or other symbol of an Enemy of the Cause. 

- **`5`** Aid a strike, riot, rebellion, or walkout by providing leadership, arms, or a distraction. 

- **`6`** Expose a secret operation, program, or project that an Enemy of the Cause wants kept quiet. 

- **`1`** Seize or destroy a convoy, weapons cache, payroll, or equipment meant for an Enemy of the Cause. 

- **`2`** Reclaim a neighborhood. Free a street or apartment block currently patrolled or occupied by an Enemy of the Cause. 

- **`3`** Target propaganda infrastructure. An advertising agency, plasmovision studio, radio broadcaster, or other mouthpiece of an Enemy of the Cause. 

- **`4`** Free a political prisoner. 

- **`5`** Retaliation. Make an example of those responsible for a recent crackdown, atrocity, or other example of authoritarian brutality. 

- **`6`** Defend a neighborhood, spokesperson, or community group that is being threatened. 

123 

**Crew Type FOUR of SIX** 

## **THRILL-SEEKERS, SMUGGLERS, DAREDEVILS, AND FAMILY** RACERS 

**When you play Racers, you earn xp when you execute a successful smuggling, hijacking, racing, or hot pursuit operation.** _Are you racers first and criminals second, or the other way around? Do you have a code?_ 

124 

## **Starting Upgrades** 

- **Vehicles:** Every PC starts with their own autopod, autocycle, or boat. A second upgrade improves the vehicles with armor and carrying capacity. 

- **Lair: Workshop** 

## **Local Circuit** 

Instead of hunting grounds, your crew has a **local circuit** . Choose a preferred operation type. When you gain turf, you expand your circuit and unlock new preferred operations. 

- **Smuggling.** The covert transportation of illicit goods (or people) into or out of restricted areas. 

- **Hijacking.** Intercept and seize a vehicle or convoy and deliver it safely to a target location. 

- **Racing.** Either illegal street racing, or within a sanctioned autodrome. Cash prizes are involved, but there may be other shady goals for particular clients, such as fixing the race or taking out a particular target. 

- **Smash-and-Grab.** Hit fast and hard, grab the target, and follow it with a high-speed getaway. 

## **Contacts** 

- **Karson** , a bookmaker. _Perhaps a good source for the latest news about illegal street races?_ 

- **Rinse** , a drug dealer. _Perhaps a potential client for hijacking operations?_ 

- **Ivory** , an arms dealer. _Perhaps a potential client for smuggling operations, or a source for acquiring weapons and explosives?_ 

- **Baine** , a Palace spy. _Perhaps a source for high-stakes operations, such as hot pursuit?_ 

- **Buddy** , a mechanic. _Perhaps a reliable place to get your autopods fixed up?_ 

- **Vreen** , owns the autodrome. _Perhaps a good source for tip-offs about upcoming races?_ 

## **Racer Upgrades** 

- **Racer Rigging:** Two of your carried items are perfectly concealed. _You could carry 1 load of contraband and a handcannon, perfectly concealed, even against a pat down._ 

- **Airship:** Add _mobility_ to your base. You can move it to a new location as a downtime activity—this thwarts any potential raid of your base that would have otherwise occurred. 

- **Elite Runners:** All your cohorts with the Runners type get +1d to Quality rolls for Runner-related actions. 

- **Complicated:** Each PC gets +1 key/deadlock box, meaning they can each take another key (which can become another deadlock). This costs three upgrades to unlock, not just one. _This may bring a PC with four deadlocks back into play if you wish._ 

- **Heavy Vehicles:** A semi-truck, bulldozer, tractor, barge, bus, drilling rig, limousine, or armored car. A second upgrade adds another heavy vehicle. 

## **Racer Claims** 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0136-12.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
WEIRD   WEIRD OLD  DEATHLANDS<br>SECRET HIT GAMBLING DEN<br>OLD GATE MAPS RACE<br>SECRET<br>TURF TURF CHOP SHOP WAREHOUSE<br>ROUTES<br>TURF<br>BIG STREET  COVER<br>LOUNGE BAR TURF INFORMANTS<br>RACE OPERATION<br>BASE<br>TURF LOYAL FENCE CONVOY BETS PLACED<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


126 

This crew has five special claims on the claim map, including two **one-off opportunities** . The “claim” is itself a lucrative score (with bonus rewards). If they have the connection on the claim map, the crew can attempt the one-off score at any time of their choosing. It doesn’t expire. 

**Bets Placed:** Unlocking this claim means that the **Big Street Race** now includes **+5 stacks** in its **payout** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. _Who do you have to convince to make the bet for you? How do they ask you to prove yourselves?_ 

**Big Street Race:** This claim is a one-off special score against **Tier 3 opponents** , with a **15 stack prize** . _What’s required to get an invite to the race—gaining the notice of a particular faction, or achieving certain victories?_ 

**Chop Shop:** Any time during personal business, roll dice equal to your Tier. You earn **stacks** equal to the highest result, minus your **Heat** . 

**Convoy:** Your cohorts have their own vehicles. _Each cohort has a common vehicle, with Quality equal to your Tier._ 

**Cover Operation:** You take **-2** Heat per score. _What’s your cover? Who did you seize it from?_ 

## **Deathlands Race:** This claim is a 

one-off special score against **Tier 4 opponents** , which yields **10 Rep** and **15 stacks** as a prize. _This is a very dangerous opportunity with a high payout. It’s probably the end of a season, or even the campaign._ 

**Lounge Bar: +1d** to **Consort** and **Sway** on-site. 

**Loyal Fence:** You get **+2 stacks** payout for **smuggling** or **hijacking** scores. 

**Secret Hit:** Unlocking this claim means that the **Deathlands Race** now includes **+10 stacks** in its **payout** (if you take out a particular target during the race). The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Secret Routes:** You get **+1d** to the **engagement roll** for **speed** approaches. 

**Warehouse:** You get **+1d** to **Acquire Asset rolls** . _You have a stockpile of various resources, which can be useful on their own, or used for barter when you need it._ 

**Weird Old Gate:** Safe passage out of the Bubble. _Usually travel in and out of the Bubble is strictly controlled by the Ministry of Stability. This gate provides a safe and secret path, just for you_ . 

**Weird Old Maps:** Unlocking this claim means you get **+2d** to the **engagement roll** for the **Deathlands Race** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Gambling Den:** Any time during personal business, roll dice equal to your Tier. You earn **stacks** equal to the highest result, minus your **Heat** . 

**Informants:** You get **+1d** to gather information for a score. _Your eyes and ears on the streets are always on the lookout for new targets._ 

127 

## **Racer Special Abilities** 

The crew starts with Stunt Riders, and can choose one more. 

## **STUNT RIDERS** 

The first time one of the crew’s **signature stunts** is performed during a score, take **+2d** and **increased effect** . **Choose one to start with.** The crew masters an additional signature stunt each time you take this ability. You can do any of these stunts even if they’re not a signature, but don’t get bonus dice etc. 

**Smuggler’s Turn:** A controlled skid and turn before speeding off in the opposite direction. 

**Reverse 180:** Spinning 180 degrees and continuing in the same direction, but facing backward. 

**Shell Game:** Launching decoy vehicles (may need to acquire an asset) to confuse and surprise. 

**Outside Ride:** Riding the roof, side, or hood of a moving vehicle, and leaping from vehicle to vehicle. 

**Big Air:** Launching a vehicle into the air across a surprising distance with any improvised ramp. 

**Ramming Speed:** Putting your foot down and meeting obstacles head-on. 

## **CUSTOM RIDE** 

Create one of your vehicles as a **cohort** (use the vehicle edges and flaws in the following list). Its Quality is equal to your Tier +1. The vehicle can use **teamwork** actions (using Quality for rolls). A vehicle can’t lead a group action, but may participate. A vehicle can help during downtime like other cohorts, but cannot go on secondary scores. 

## **Vehicle Edges** 

**Nimble:** The vehicle handles easily. Consider this an assist (+1d) for tricky maneuvers. 

**Simple:** The vehicle is easy to repair. Remove all its harm during downtime. **Sturdy:** The vehicle keeps operating even when broken. 

## **Vehicle Flaws** 

**Guzzler:** The vehicle costs 1 stack per downtime to keep in operation. 

**Distinct:** The vehicle has memorable features. Take +1 Heat when you use it on a score. 

**Finicky:** When operated without the one person who understands it, the vehicle has -1 Quality. 

_The Blackline Syndicate, a Tier 1 crew of racers, have a vehicle cohort (a sweet van called the Black Echo). Aniya is driving the Black Echo in a race. She could rely purely on the van’s Quality, making a 2d fortune roll (Tier +1) to see if it can take the lead by itself. Instead she decides to lead a group action, with her driving skill and the van itself both contributing. She rolls Finesse and pushes herself for a total of 3d. The van roll its Quality (2d). Aniya’s highest result is a 1, while the van’s highest result is a 5. Aniya takes 1 Stress for the 1-3 result, but the 4/5 result stands. The Black Echo takes the lead, but there will be a consequence that could apply to either Aniya, her van, or both._ 

128 

## **ESCAPE VELOCITY** 

One of the crew’s vehicles is fitted with a device that activates at a specific speed. This requires filling an **8-segment acceleration clock** during the score. When the clock is filled and the vehicle hits the target speed, choose an effect: _break the laws of gravity—create a tear in reality—travel into the resonance field—travel backward or forward through time._ 

_If the vehicle comes to a stop, reset the acceleration clock to zero._ 

## **THE FAMILY TAKES A CUT** 

Before payout for a smuggling or hijacking score, the crew can skim the goods for **+4 stacks** _._ The GM will tick a clock. 

_The GM can tick any clock of their choice—a good default is “somebody notices you’re skimming the goods.” The idea is that any repercussions are not immediate, and won’t kick in until the clock is filled. Also, you can work against that clock during downtime with your own long-term projects, etc._ 

## **BRING THEM IN** 

As long as you’re not currently fighting them (e.g. you’re at war), you can turn even the most bitter of enemies into family. This requires a long-term project— **6 segments** to turn them into a crew contact, **10 segments** to turn them into a **cohort** or **PC** (your choice). If they become a PC, create them as normal, with bonus action dots and abilities each equal to their Tier, and any deadlocks at the GM’s discretion. Their faction’s relationship to your crew does not change. 

## **SPEED DEMONS** 

When you go into conflict aboard a vehicle, you gain increased effect for vehicle damage and speed. If the vehicle has armor, you can use it for your own protection. 

## **Racer Questions** 

After character questions, your group can run through crew questions together. Each PC picks one from the following list that applies to you (or make up your own) and gives a few details about how you came to that role. You don’t have to go too in-depth—this is just to give a general sense of the shape of the crew as you begin. 

- Which of you first suggested forming a crew? 

- Which of you has been racing the longest? 

- Which of you has experience smuggling? 

- Which of you drives like you have a death wish? 

- Which of you knows the streets best? 

- Which of you has the most to lose if we get caught? 

129 

## **Ways to Run a Race** 

If the players decide to be a crew of Racers, the GM will want to think about how to run races. There is no one correct way; try something in one score and see how it feels, then tweak it for next time. 

## **Follow the Fiction** 

You could follow the race in the fiction, keeping track of the relative position of the various competitors either in your head, with pen and paper, with tokens, or with miniature cars. 

Successful action rolls will help PCs pull ahead, while consequences might push them back and see them overtaken. You could use a simple clock (for example, an 8-clock) to represent how long the race is, ticking it with every action roll. When the clock is complete, whoever is in the lead wins. 

Can one of the PCs make sure they’re in the front of the pack at the right time? 

## **Racing Clocks** 

You could use racing clocks (see _Blades in the Dark_ , page 16). Put down two opposed clocks—one for a PC winning the race, and one for someone else winning. 

Successes put ticks on the “Win the Race” clock (with the number of ticks depending on effect, as usual). Consequences put ticks on the clock for “Someone Else Wins.” Can the PCs finish their “Win the Race” clock before someone else wins? 

Start simple with an 8-clock for both. With their various advantages, abilities, and resisting consequences, the PCs should win pretty easily. 

Next time, you could try an 8-clock for the PCs and a 6-clock for the opposition. Keep making the PC clock bigger and the opposition clock smaller for more challenging races. Also remember that against higher-Tier opponents, the PCs will have less effect (meaning fewer clock ticks on a success). 

130 

## **Racer Opportunities** 

During the planning meeting (page 180), each player (as well as the GM) will present an opportunity for a possible score that the crew might take. If anyone feels stuck, look at the following list and consider a Smuggling, Hijacking, Racing, or Hot Pursuit approach for any of them. 

- **`1`** Rumor is that anyone who wins big at the autodrome gets approached about race-fixing. A client wants you to win big and tell them who approaches you. 

- **`2`** A joyrider stole a luxury autopod belonging to a very wealthy, powerful individual. They want it back. 

- **`3`** The Deep Run, a street race that goes into the depths of Coalridge Deep Excavation and back out. Strange shit happens down there, but the prize money is real. 

- **`4`** A defecting military officer needs urgent passage out of the city. 

- **`5`** A paranormal crystal (a prison for a powerful entity) is scheduled to be transported out of the city and into a containment facility in the deathlands. A weird old recluse desperately wants that crystal for himself. 

- **`6`** The Highwire, a deadly street race that takes place entirely across the rooftops of Doskvol. 

- **`1`** A corporate R&D lab is offering a cash bounty to anyone who can beat their experimental new autopod in a race. 

- **`2`** The Voidwater Burn, a street race along bridges, barges, and many miles of canals. 

- **`3`** A rival outfit is transporting contraband through the deathlands in a customized tanker. They say it’s invulnerable; prove them wrong. 

- **`4`** The Bowmore Royale, an illegal demolition derby where competitors deliberately try to destroy each other’s vehicles in a large arena, until only one is left standing. 

- **`5`** A powerful figure just found out their rakish lover has been brazenly cheating on them. The former is furious and wants revenge, so the scoundrel is trying to hightail it out of the city. 

- **`6`** A self-driving autopod powered by a sparkmind intelligence has gone rogue. Nobody has managed to catch it. 

131 

**Crew Type FIVE of SIX** 

**COVERT SPECIALISTS, EXPERTS IN HEISTS AND ESPIONAGE** 

## SHADOWS 

**When you play a Shadows, you earn xp when you execute a successful surveillance, heist, subterfuge, or sabotage score.** _Do you steal to line your own pockets, or do you have a larger project? Do you have any allegiances, or do you work for the highest bidder?_ 

132 

## **Starting Upgrades** 

- **Lair: Hidden** 

- **Cohort: Gang (Infiltrators)** 

## **Hunting Grounds** 

Choose a favored operation type. _This will color what kind of Shadows you are_ — _smooth operators who pull off daring heists, or shady professionals who specialize in espionage intelligence?_ When you gain turf, you unlock new preferred operations. 

- **Surveillance.** Gather intelligence for a client through stakeouts, wiretapping, planting bugs, or following a target. 

- **Heists.** The theft of valuables, whether the target is art and jewelery, bank vaults, private collections, or casinos. 

- **Subterfuge.** Covert infiltration, compromising secure facilities, conducting clandestine meetings, and other acts of espionage. 

- **Cleanup.** Rogue agents, cover-ups gone wrong, failed ops; there’s good money in being the ones who tidy up loose ends, hide the evidence, and extract compromised assets. 

## **Contacts** 

- **Malloy** , a Ministry clerk. _Perhaps a good source for tip-offs about potential scores?_ 

133 

- **Caldwell** , an art forger. _Perhaps a useful tool in your toolbox?_ 

- **Bloom** , a collector. _Perhaps a potential patron for your crew?_ 

- **Vera** , a switchboard operator. _Perhaps someone who knows what the powerful talk about on closed lines?_ 

- **Catton** , a hotel concierge. _Perhaps a good source of news and gossip?_ 

- **Tarnish** , an information broker. _Perhaps a well-connected figure in the espionage world, known for their neutrality?_ 

## **Shadows Upgrades** 

- **Secret maps, and various keys and passcards:** You have easy passage through the city’s shadow routes—underground canals, service tunnels, and basement access hatches. 

- **Elite Infiltrators:** All your cohorts with the Infiltrators type get +1d to Quality rolls for Infiltrator-related actions. 

- **Elite Hustlers:** All your cohorts with the Hustlers type get +1d to Quality rolls for Hustler-related actions. 

- **Multifaceted:** Each PC gets +1 key/deadlock box, meaning they can each take another key (which can become another deadlock). This costs three upgrades to unlock, not just one. _This may bring a PC with four deadlocks back into play if you wish._ 

## **Shadows Claims**

This crew has five special claims on the claim map, including two **one-off opportunities** . The “claim” is itself a lucrative score (with bonus rewards). If they have the connection on the claim map, the crew can attempt the one-off score at any time of their choosing. It doesn’t expire. 

**Checkmate:** This claim is a one-off special score against a **Tier 5 target** , which yields **30 stacks** as payout, and completes any clock of the crew’s choice. Consider the fiction when choosing the clock—the idea is that by completing this score, the crew finishes something important like stopping a ticking timebomb, exposing a conspiracy, compromising a high-Tier faction, etc. _This is a very dangerous opportunity with a big reward. It’s probably the end of a season, or even the campaign._ 

**Cover Identities:** You get **+1d** to the **engagement roll** for **deception** and **social** approaches. _False identities help confuse the opposition._ 

**Cover Story:** Unlocking this claim means you get **+2d** to the **engagement roll** for the **Checkmate score** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Covert Fixer:** You get **+2 stacks** payout for **surveillance** or **sabotage** scores. 

**Critical Move:** This claim is a one-off special score against a **Tier 4 target** , which yields a **15 stack** payout and puts +4 ticks on any clock of the crew’s choice. Consider the fiction when choosing the clock—the idea is that by completing this score, the crew works toward something important like stopping a ticking timebomb, exposing a conspiracy, compromising a high-Tier faction, etc. 

**Dispensary:** You get **+1d** to **healing treatment rolls** . _Easy access to all the best drugs and medicines._ 

**High Stakes Game:** Any time during personal business, roll dice equal to your Tier. You earn **stacks** equal to the highest result, minus your **Heat** . 

**Inside Mark:** Unlocking this claim means that the target for the **Checkmate** counts as **-1 Tier** for that score. The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Informants:** You get **+1d** to gather information for a score. _Your eyes and ears on the streets are always on the lookout for new targets._ 

**Interested Party:** Unlocking this claim means that the **Checkmate score** now includes **+10 stacks** in its **payout** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Lounge Bar:** Any time during personal business, roll dice equal to your Tier. You earn **stacks** equal to the highest result, minus your **Heat** . 

**Luxury Venue: +1d** to **Command** and **Sway** on-site. 

**Paid-Off Bluecoats:** You take **-2** Heat per score. 

**Secret Pathways:** You get **+1d** to the **engagement** roll for **stealth** plans. You might have access to long-forgotten underground canals, rooftop walkways, or some other route of your choosing. 

**Slush Fund:** You get **+1d** to **Acquire Asset rolls** . _You have access to a secret, off-the-books account. Who owns it, and why have they given you access?_ 

**Specialist Fence:** You get **+2 stacks** payout for **heists** or **subterfuge** scores. 

135 

## **Shadows Special Abilities** 

## **SYNCHRONIZED WATCHES** 

You may use **assists** or **setup actions** with any crew member, regardless of the distance separating you. When you perform a **group action** , you may count multiple 6s from different rolls as a critical success. 

_The first part of this ability only works with assists or setup actions, not group actions. The second part of this ability works with group actions._ 

## **THIEVES WITH A CODE** 

When you complete a score with no deaths having occurred, gain **+1 faction status** with the local citizenry. 

## **SLEEPY TIME** 

Everyone on the crew adds **tranquilizer rounds** (0 load, compatible with any firearm) to their playbook items. 

_Each character gets one use of these tranq rounds—so if you use them in your silenced shooter, they won’t be available for your handcannon. The GM may use the crew Tier as a fortune roll to see how long the effect lasts, sometimes._ 

## **DON’T FORGET THE DUFFEL BAG** 

Once per score, the crew can flashback to an **Acquire Asset** roll with **+2d** . Both the flashback and the downtime activity are free. 

_You may still wish to spend stacks to increase the result level of the Acquire Asset roll._ 

## **BENEFACTOR** 

When you take this ability, the crew immediately receives **4 stacks** . Whenever you advance your **Tier** , it costs **half the stacks** it normally would. 

_Who’s backing you? Why do they help you?_ 

## **ECHO SAFEHOUSE** 

The crew has access to a safehouse in the resonance field. It can be accessed once per score, from anywhere. The door always returns to the same place it was entered from. Use it as a hiding place, to reequip, repair, or just take a breather. Any PCs who enter gain **+1 load** . One PC may clear all **level 1 harm** via emergency medical supplies there. Note that time still passes in the outside world. 

136 

## **BLACK BAG OPERATIONS** 

When you execute a clandestine infiltration, you get **+1d** to the **engagement roll** . You may attempt to install surveillance equipment during a score on any faction’s turf. So long as the wire remains in place, take **+1d** on any future **gather information** rolls related to that faction. The GM may make a fortune roll using the target faction’s Tier to see if they notice the bug and remove it during any personal business phase. 

## **Shadows Questions** 

After character questions, your group can run through crew questions together. Each PC picks one from the following list that applies to you (or make up your own) and gives a few details about how you came to that role. You don’t have to go too in-depth—this is just to give a general sense of the shape of the crew as you begin. 

- Which of you first suggested forming a crew? 

- Which of you has the most experience with heists? 

- Which of you was recruited for your particular skill set? 

- Which of you handles the homework—making the maps, charts, and diagrams before a heist? 

- Which of you looks after fencing the goods, and maintains the books? 

- Which of you knows the streets best? 

137 

## **Shadows Opportunities** 

During the planning meeting (page 180), each player (as well as the GM) will present an opportunity for a possible score that the crew might take. If anyone feels stuck, look at the following list and consider a Surveillance, Heist, Subterfuge, or Sabotage approach for any of them. 

- **`1`** A private art dealer has acquired something they shouldn’t have. 

- **`2`** A new nightclub is rumored to be a front for an intelligence agency. 

- **`3`** A courier has gotten sloppy and uses the same canal route to carry sensitive documents from Charterhall, every Home Day. 

- **`4`** The consulate gala will feature high-profile guests, loose lips, and lax security. **`5`** A defecting scientist wants extraction—but they’re under constant watch. **`6`** An informant is ready to talk, but only to someone off the books. 

- **`1`** The target of a political assassination has resurfaced as a resonance echo. Finish the job, permanently. 

- **`2`** A casino is hosting the biggest high-roller tournament of the year. The prize pool is eye-watering. 

- **`3`** There’s a train leaving Gaddoc Station with a suspected intelligence handoff to occur during the journey. 

- **`4`** You know the time and location of an infamous, clandestine underworld auction, held once every three years. 

- **`5`** An assassination attempt failed—the target wants to know who ordered it, and they want payback. 

- **`6`** An airship belonging to a millionaire recluse will be docked at Penderyn Air Terminal, for just one night. 

138 

139 

**A NEW AGE CULT DEDICATED TO  NEW AGE CULT DEDICATED TO DEDICATED TO AN UNSETTLING VISION OF THE FUTUREVISION OF THE FUTUREOF THE FUTUREFUTURE** 

**Crew Type A NEW AGE CULT DEDICATED TO  NEW AGE CULT DEDICATED TO DEDICATED TO SIX of SIX AN UNSETTLING VISION OF THE FUTUREVISION OF THE FUTUREOF THE FUTUREFUTURE** UTOPIANS 

**When you play Utopians, you earn xp when you advance the realization of your Utopian Vision.** While you might start off with good (utopian) intentions, make no mistake that this crew is on a dark path. This is a cult, and there are forgotten gods just waiting for believers like you. _Are your characters fully aware of the dark path they walk, or are they earnest optimists who will learn the truth of the world the hard way?_ 

140 

## **Starting Upgrades** 

- **Training: Resolve** 

- **Cohort: Gang (Eggheads)** 

## **Utopian Vision** 

Core to the Utopian crew is their Utopian Vision. During crew creation, choose two truths of the Utopian Vision: _Free—Egalitarian—Abundant—Beautiful— Serene—Radiant—Natural._ 

To begin with, the Utopian Vision is somewhat vague. You do not know if it is the future or the past, or another plane of existence entirely. Importantly, **you believe that it is a real place or state of being that you can actually attain** . 

It may help to decide how you collectively learned of this Utopian Vision. _Was it a literal vision experienced by one or more of the PCs? Was it something you read about it in an ancient forbidden book? Was it something hinted at in the results of a fringe scientific experiment, or seen on the printouts from a huge and mysterious computer?_ 

141 

## **Utopians, Ward Bosses, and the Underworld** 

Utopians have a ward boss as usual (see page 89), and also earn Heat and Wanted Levels. It’s important to remember that the Imperium is under Reality Constancy Law, strictly enforced by Section 6. Paranormal experiments and intentionally interacting with anomalies and/or Utopian Visions are as highly illegal as murder or dealing contraband. When you undertake this sort of criminal activity in a given district, the local ward boss will expect a cut of your profits, just like they would any other crew. 

## **Anomalies** 

Instead of hunting grounds, paranormal **anomalies** are key to manifesting your utopia. An anomaly is a localized tear in the fabric of reality, where paranormal power is amplified and anything is possible. There are three types of scores involving anomalies: 

- **Discovery.** Find new anomalies before they’re claimed by another faction, or secured and sealed by Section 6. 

- **Stabilization.** Anomalies are highly unstable by nature, but they can be harnessed through occult ritual or scientific apparatus. 

- **Experimentation.** The possible use cases for the immense power of an anomaly are infinite. Trial and error is the only way to know more. 

Unlike other crew types who choose just one favored operation to begin with, Utopians get +1d to gather information rolls and a free downtime activity for operations that involve **any** of these operations. 

**What is the purpose of anomalies?** That depends on the nature of the crew and your Utopian Vision. Anomalies break the rules of reality in a fundamental way (see page 332). They can be stabilized, harnessed, and controlled (through the three types of scores or through a long-term project), for possible effects that might include: 

- **Harvesting alluvium.** Rare, unstable, and very expensive on the black market, alluvium breaks the laws of reality by its very presence, and most advanced paranormal experiments require some measure of alluvium as a catalyst. Anomalies can be used as a source of alluvium. 

- **Communicating with, and possibly binding, resonance entities.** 

- **Changing the past, or the future.** 

- **Changing the world.** Since anomalies variously effect everything from gravity, to plant growth, to temperature, to time itself (page 332), the possibilities are endless. You might change the world to match your Utopian Vision (freeing prisoners from captivity, painting the sky in beautiful and terrifying colors, causing abundant plant growth, etc.). _For example, some anomalies create an anti-gravity effect in their vicinity; this anomalous effect could be harnessed to create flying autopods._ 

142 

## **Circles** 

Unlike other crew types, Utopian claims and special abilities are gated behind certain thresholds. These are arranged in four Circles of descending order. The crew starts in the First Circle, and can attempt to grab any of the First Circle claims in any order, and can take any of the First Circle special abilities. 

Note that the Circles represent _increasing darkness_ , not necessarily increasing power level. Descending to lower Circles is a story beat about the crew doing ever-darker deeds and learning ever-darker truths. It’s not as simple as “advancement”; it’s about corruption. 

**First Circle.** The crew learns the first two truths of their Utopian Vision (perhaps: _Free—Egalitarian—Abundant—Beautiful—Serene—Radiant— Natural_ ). 

**Second Circle.** Requires unlocking the **Threshold of Gold** : when the crew has earned a **total of 20 stacks** (track this from the start). The crew gets a slightly clearer Utopian Vision, and learns an unsettling new truth (perhaps: _Shifting— Sweltering—Lustful—Unsettling—Future—Past—Alien_ ). 

**Third Circle.** Requires unlocking the Second Circle and the **Threshold of Blood** : when the crew has **ended at least 10 lives** (track this from the start of the campaign, not from when they achieve the Second Circle). The crew gets a slightly clearer Utopian Vision, and learns a dark new truth (perhaps: _Psychedelic—Inhuman—Violent—Future—Past—Tempestuous_ ). 

**Final Circle.** Requires unlocking the Third Circle and the **Threshold of Power** : the crew must be at least **Tier 3** , and have created a **major anomaly** . The Utopian Vision becomes clear, and the crew learns a final, terrible truth (perhaps: _Fiery—Frozen—Terrifying—Cruel—Monstrous—Capricious— Inhuman_ ). 

Circles must be completed in descending order, even if their prerequisites are met early. 

Only First Circle abilities may be taken as versatile advances by other crew types. If another crew type discovers their own Utopian Vision, they may switch to the Utopian crew sheet and proceed from there. 

143 

## **Contacts** 

- **Evangeline** , a spiritual sage. _Perhaps a charismatic cult leader of their own who can offer wise advice?_ 

- **Friswell** , an aristocrat. _Perhaps bored, wealthy, and looking for deeper meaning—their money and connections could be very useful..._ 

- **Netherley** , a psychedelic artist. _Perhaps their art can offer deeper insights into your Utopian Vision?_ 

- **Tarn** , a paranormal experimentalist. _Perhaps a fringe scientist with their own utopian aspirations?_ 

- **Lockmore Wend** , a celebrity. _Perhaps an actor or musician seeking spiritual fulfillment—could their fame be used as a beacon to spread the light of the Utopian Vision?_ 

- **Om** , a deathlands dropout. _They rejected mainstream society to live in the deathlands. The revelations they’ve experienced there might be critical to your project._ 

## **Utopian Upgrades** 

- **Utopian Rigging:** You get 2 free load worth of documents or paranormal implements. _For example, you could carry a ream of printouts from a cursed terminal, as well as an echo containment unit and safety gloves, all for zero load._ 

- **Elite Eggheads:** All your cohorts with the Eggheads type get +1d to Quality rolls for Egghead-related actions. 

- **Elite Muscle:** All your cohorts with the Muscle type get +1d to Quality rolls for Muscle-related actions. 

- **Awakened** : Each PC gets +1 key/deadlock box, meaning they can each take another key (which can become another deadlock). This costs three upgrades to unlock, not just one. _This may bring a PC with four deadlocks back into play if you wish._ 

144 

## **FIRST CIRCLE CLAIMS** 

**Luxury Retreat:** Your Egghead cohorts get **+1 scale** . _A luxury retreat is a great way to recruit new followers._ 

**Turf:** Unlocking turf simply reduces the Rep cost to develop by one (Utopians start with all three favored operations). 

**Wellness Class:** Any time during personal business, roll dice equal to your Tier. You earn **stacks** equal to the highest result, minus your **Heat** . 

## **SECOND CIRCLE CLAIMS** 

**Donations:** You get **+2 stacks** payout for **paranormal** scores. _What kind of pyramid scheme have you set up?_ 

**Natural Healer:** You get **+1d** to **healing treatment rolls.** _What form of healing do they practice?_ 

**Temple: +1d** to **Command** and **Sway** on-site. 

## **THIRD CIRCLE CLAIMS** 

**Abandoned Lab:** You get **+1d** to any **Attune** rolls on-site; both action rolls, as well downtime activities such as long-term projects. _Where is this lab? What was its original purpose?_ 

**Ancient Altar:** You get **+1d** to the **engagement roll** for paranormal approaches. _Who, or what, is it an altar to?_ 

**Ancient Gate:** Safe passage out of the Bubble. _Usually travel in and out of the Bubble is strictly controlled by the Ministry of Stability. This gate provides a safe and secret path, just for you._ 

**Ancient Tower:** You get **+1d** to **Consort** with resonance entities on-site. _Where is this tower? Does it even exist in our reality? Is it from the ancient past, or the ancient future?_ 

**Reality Shift:** This claim is a one-off score against a **Tier 4 target** , and if successful, it creates a **new major anomaly** . The anomaly will be under 

your control, and stabilized. _What is the nature of the anomaly, and where is it? How is the target faction gate-keeping this possible anomaly? What will the catalyst to its creation be?_ 

## **FINAL CIRCLE CLAIMS** 

**Ancient Tomes:** Unlocking this claim means you get **+2d** to the **engagement roll** for the **Reality Tear one-off opportunity** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Figurehead:** You convince a patsy to become the figurehead leader of your cult. At any time, have them take the fall and go to Ironhook (or worse) to **remove 3 Wanted Levels** from the crew. They are in too deep to seek retribution, and you will suffer no blowback. 

**Interested Party:** Unlocking this claim means that the **Reality Tear one-off opportunity** now includes **+6 stacks** in its **payout** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. 

**Notable Skeptic:** Unlocking this claim means that the **Reality Tear one-off opportunity** now yields **+4 Rep** . The score to unlock this claim should also carry a standard payout as usual. _Who is this skeptic? Unlocking this claim means convincing them to pay attention and take you seriously._ 

**Reality Tear:** This claim is a one-off opportunity against a **Tier 5 target** , and if successful, it creates a **new mega anomaly** . A mega anomaly is a tear in reality the size of an entire district, or even multiple districts. _This is a very dangerous score with a high-impact result. It’s probably the end of a season, or even the campaign. What is the nature of the anomaly, and where will it appear? How is the target faction gatekeeping this possible anomaly? What will the catalyst to its creation be?_ 

145

This crew has six special claims on the claim map, including two **one-off opportunities** . The “claim” is itself a special score with bonus rewards. 

## **Utopian Special Abilities** 

## **FIRST CIRCLE ABILITIES** 

## **ENLIGHTENED** 

You get **+1d** to **resistance** rolls against paranormal threats and consequences. You get **+1d** to **healing** rolls when you have paranormal harm. 

## **COMMUNE** 

You may use **teamwork** with any crew member, regardless of the distance separating you. By taking 1 Stress, your projected thoughts are heard by every crew member as telepathic communication. 

_How does this ability work for your crew? Is it through uncanny invention, or spiritual technique? How are new crew members given this ability?_ 

146 

## **BEST INTENTIONS** 

If every PC vows not to kill anyone before a score, take **+1d** to the engagement roll. The first time each PC takes an action that might kill someone if it’s successful (whether intentional by the PC or not), they take **+1d** and **potency** . If you all keep the vow, the crew marks **1 xp** . 

_This ability is win-win—either you keep the vow and everyone marks xp, or you break the vow and get a decent boost to one action roll. Either way, it’s the thought that counts, isn’t it? Accidents happen._ 

## **ZEAL** 

Every PC gets **+1d** and **potency** when they evangelize about the Utopian Vision. 

_The evangelizing (whether that’s Consort, Sway, Command, or whatever) must be the point of the action—this ability doesn’t apply if you happen to be evangelizing while you do something unrelated._ 

## **SECOND CIRCLE ABILITIES** 

## **TRUE BELIEVERS** 

Your **cohorts** will undertake any service, no matter how dangerous or strange. They gain **+1d** to rolls against enemies of the Utopian Vision. 

## **ALTERED STATES** 

Each PC gains an additional **vice** : _Ritual Hedonism_ . When you indulge this vice, you don’t overindulge if you clear excess Stress. In addition, your ecstatic visions of the future mean you can perform one **flashback** for free. 

## **THIRD CIRCLE ABILITIES** 

## **FOR THE GREATER GOOD** 

A human sacrifice removes the Stress cost for any paranormal experiment you perform, and such sacrifices performed in your base do not trigger the Death Radar or generate Heat. 

_For details on paranormal experiments, see page 167._ 

## **THIS IS FINE** 

If every PC works together (group action), you can summon a denizen of your Utopian Vision into this reality; a Class V Resonance Entity. 

_This non-human entity (a horror or aberration) counts as Tier 5 for the purposes of fortune rolls. Note that it does not automatically obey your commands (but you may still attempt to have it do so). It does not automatically return to the resonance field._ 

147 

## **FINAL CIRCLE ABILITIES** 

## **REMEMBER THE FORGOTTEN** 

You can now communicate with the entity that created your Utopian Vision (a “god”?). Tread carefully. 

## **PARADISE MANIFEST** 

When you take this advance, your base and the area around transforms into a small fragment of your utopia, manifest in this reality. Take +2d to the engagement roll for any raids. All crew members gain **potency** when acting in the base and its surrounds, and all downtime actions conducted in the base get **+1 result level** . This will attract significant attention from Section 6 and other high-Tier factions. 

## **WE NO LONGER PLAY BY YOUR RULES** 

When you take this advance, immediately pick two more advances. 

## **Utopian Questions** 

After character questions, your group can run through crew questions together. Each PC picks one from the following list that applies to you (or make up your own) and gives a few details about how you came to that role. You don’t have to go too in-depth—this is just to give a general sense of the shape of the crew as you begin. 

- Which of you first had a vision of the utopia? 

- Which of you suggested forming a crew? 

- Which of you is the most devout believer? 

- Which of you is the most naive? 

- Which of you is the most cynical? 

- Which of you handles recruitment? 

## **Utopian Opportunities** 

During the planning meeting (page 180), each player (as well as the GM) will present an opportunity for a possible score that the crew might take. If anyone feels stuck, look at the list on the next page. 

**How do Utopians get paid?** They might sell a paranormal byproduct, such as alluvium, to a third-party client. A client might pay them to accomplish some other task in the course of their paranormal activities, such as reaching out to a dead loved one through an anomaly. A paranormal faction might pay them to do a paranormal score in exchange for sharing the data from the “experiment.” Utopians may also perform regular crimes like heists or intelligence espionage, in order to fund their more important work of realizing their Utopian Vision. 

148 

- **`1`** An apartment block is suffering under the effects of an uncontrolled anomaly in the building. They’re trying to keep it secret from Section 6, to avoid a heavy-handed crackdown. 

- **`2`** A wealthy businessperson will pay anything to hear from their dead lover. 

- **`3`** Lady Risbury is holding a gallery showing of pre-cataclysm artifacts. One of them is the real deal. 

- **`4`** A computer terminal in the depths of the Ministry of Discovery started spewing hundreds of yards of printout, all of it about your exact Utopian Vision. What else could it tell you? 

- **`5`** A rival cult is assimilating smaller rivals, and killing those who refuse. Your crew may be next. 

- **`6`** A local street gang is plagued by the echoes of their victims. They’re desperate for help. 

- **`1`** You saw a sparkmind construct in your Utopian Vision. You don’t know why, but you know you must free the huge machine, and have it join your crew. 

- **`2`** Sirens outside. Section 6 are in the district _now_ , on their way to a newly discovered anomaly. Can you misdirect them, and claim it for yourselves? 

- **`3`** Captain Blanchet says that when he takes his submarine to a particular spot 15 fathoms deep, something weird happens. Could be an anomaly down there. 

- **`4`** A research group at the university has successfully created an anomaly in lab conditions. A lot of people might want those findings, and the equipment. 

- **`5`** Section 6 has set up a temporary field office to deal with a local paranormal outbreak. Although heavily guarded, it contains top secret intel on all the reported anomalies in the district... 

- **`6`** There’s a student society engaging in all sorts of hedonistic, psychedelic experimentation, and they’re ripe for recruitment to one paranormal cult or another. Get there first, and demonstrate your Utopian Vision.
