## **The Hull Directive Page 280** 

## **The Model Worker Initiative Page 284** 

## **Minutes to Midnight Page 288** 

## **Invasion from Another World Page 296** 

The Ministry of Discovery is pouring money into the top-secret Blueraker Project, an experimental rocket ship. If it launches, everything will change. 

The Lusk Reform Technique turns a criminal into one of the Reformed and produces a hull to boot; is it a clever, efficient form of managing the criminal population, or is it a horrific crime against humanity? 

Satisfied with the success of their trials in Coalridge, the Ministry of Stability and several corporations plan to roll the initiative out to other districts. Total worker efficiency through surveillance, propaganda, and brainwashing. Where will it end? Can it be stopped? 

Tensions between Blackthorn Park and the Palace are rapidly escalating, threatening to tip the Imperium and United Skov Covenant into open warfare—Unity War IV. Both factions are being secretly manipulated by a third party with their own agenda, hoping to capitalize on the chaos of global conflict. 

The resonance field is connected to another living world, one which Section 6 believes is antithetical to our own. Reality Wardens have made a concerted effort to prevent traffic between the worlds. With more and more factions meddling with the resonance field, however, the rift between worlds threatens to tear wide open, leading to a full-scale invasion. 

273 

## Blueraker Is Go 

The Ministry of Discovery is pouring money into the top-secret Blueraker Project, a series of experimental rocket ships intended to explore the far reaches of the Blue and uncover its secrets. The first four Bluerakers have been catastrophic failures, but Blueraker 5 has passed all checks and looks to be clear for ignition. 

If it launches, everything will change—one way or another. 

## **Inciting Incident** 

A briefcase containing the blueprints and mission parameters of the Blueraker 5 launch has gone missing. Add the _Patrols_ ongoing trouble to the table, as the Ministry of Discovery puts pressure on the Bluecoats to find the missing intel without delay. 

## **Questions for the Players** 

- Who do you know who was recently shook down by Bluecoats looking for the briefcase? _The Bluecoats let slip what they’re looking for, and now the PCs know too._ 

- What’s something fundamental about this world that you wish you could change somehow? _The eternal night or the deathlands? That you can’t leave the city? That a dead person’s psychic echo rises as a vengeful ghost?_ 

- Who’s someone you’re fond of that works as a test pilot for the Ministry of Discovery? _Your character doesn’t know it, but that person has assigned to the Blueraker 5 launch, as an elite Blue Explorer._ 

- Who do you know who’s recently fallen in with the countercultural protest group known as the Youth Action Movement, or “Yammies”? 

## **Key NPCs** 

**Strathmill** , Director-General of the **Ministry of Discovery** . An energetic and eccentric visionary who sees the Blueraker Project as nothing less than the future of humanity. Strathmill believes in the Blueraker Project in its purest form—discovering what lies beyond the Shattered Isles as we know them. 

**Linford Hycrest** , Supreme Director of Guidance within **New Dawn** . DirectorGeneral Strathmill is a loyal member, and divulges intimate secrets to Hycrest during their private wellness sessions. Hycrest believes that the Blueraker rocket ship could lead them to the last of the “void keys,” allowing New Dawn to free the Red Queen from her bondage at last. 

274 

**Ms. Asta** , controller of **Blackthorn Park** in Doskvol. Only recently learned of the existence of Blueraker 5, and is now under urgent orders to find it and rig it to explode on its maiden voyage (both to destroy the ship, and to publicly humiliate the Imperium). 

**River** , a daredevil member of the **Youth Action Movement (the Yammies)** . The Yammies know about the Blueraker project, and they want to hijack it for their most audacious spectacle yet. They’ll fill the rocket ship with flowers and have it explode above the city, showering Doskvol with petals. 

**Lord Scurlock** , an enigmatic recluse, as well as a secret patron of the Yammies. Scurlock is bound to a Class VI Metadimensional Entity called Setarra, currently bound in a crystal prison by the Strelai and due to be transported to their high-security containment vault in the deathlands. If Scurlock fails to free Setarra before she is taken beyond the Bubble, his backup plan is to use the Yammies to crash Blueraker 5 into the Strelai containment vault, blowing it to smithereens. This would free a catastrophic number of powerful resonance entities. The head of the Blueraker engineering team is already under Scurlock’s hypnotic control. 

**Major Fellows** , Imperial Military. A tough, capable officer, and fanatically loyal to the Imperium. The military is providing the Blueraker Project with funds and specialist personnel, and Fellows is in charge of the liaison. Unbeknownst to the Ministry of Discovery, the military intends to turn the Blueraker into a weapon of mass destruction. 

**Doctor Morcroft** , Director of the **Lusk Reform Clinic** . Terrifyingly cheerful. The pilots of Blueraker 5 (the Blue Explorers) will undergo the Lusk Reform Technique immediately before launch, a fact they have not been informed of. Their echoes will be placed in waiting hulls, and both their hollowed bodies and the on-program hulls will be launched together. The hollows are to test the effects of such rocket ship travel on the human body, while the hulls can continue the scientific mission regardless of how lethal it may be. 

**Vestige** , Reality Warden with **Section 6** . Section 6 is aware of the Blueraker Project, and they believe it to be a reality-warping disaster waiting to happen. If they crack down on the project too early, there’s a risk the ministry will carry on under more secrecy. The Reality Warden known as Vestige is in command of a squad with orders to commandeer the ship just before launch. 

**The Hart** , fixer for the **Unseen** . Section 6 are pawns being used by the Unseen for their own grand plans—the senior Reality Warden in charge of the Blueraker infiltration is a member of the Unseen, and reports to the Hart. The Hart may try to manipulate the PC crew toward the same goal, through bribery, blackmail, or trickery. This might be direct, or it might be through various intermediaries (friends, allies, enemies) who secretly work for the Unseen, knowingly or unknowingly. 

275 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0286-01.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
10 1<br>9 2<br>8 3<br>7 4<br>6 5<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


## **The Countdown** 

Use a 10-segment clock to track this timebomb. Tick it when you update faction clocks as part of the Trouble Engine, or based on a fortune roll, or your narrative instincts, or any fictional events you deem relevant. 

As the clock fills, the following escalations happen. 

- **2 ticks.** Blackthorn Park places an agent within the Blueraker team. 

- **4 ticks.** The Yammies blow the whistle on the project through their underground newsletter. The Ministry of Discovery rushes out a press release publicly announcing the launch, in order to “own the narrative.” The launch will now be broadcast live across the Imperium. 

- **6 ticks.** The Ministry installs a fake rocket at the underground hangar for the public launch, and shift the real launch location to another hidden facility—perhaps under the Vreen Autodrome in Nightmarket, or under the Monitory Peak Coronagraph in Bowmore Fields, or within the mysterious Dunslough Incident Site. 

- **7 ticks.** The Palace officially begins investigating the Blueraker Project. All scores related to it gain +2 Heat going forward. 

- **9 ticks.** Director-General Strathmill is found dead. The launch will go ahead as planned. 

- **10 ticks.** Blueraker 5 launches. 

As the main clock advances, also track the progress of the various factions involved toward their own goals, such as hijacking the rocket ship. You do not have to track all the listed NPCs and factions, just choose the ones that seem most compelling to you, or are the most relevant and connected to the PC crew. You could track their progress with clocks, or simply jot down a note between sessions as they make progress (or suffer setbacks). 

When the Blueraker 5 launches, consider which factions and NPCs are in place to make their move. This is worth playing out as a score, assuming the PC crew have their own goals related to the launch. The outcome of the launch will depend on which faction (if any) is successful in hijacking the rocket ship. 

276 

If launched into the Blue, other possible outcomes might include: 

- The Bubble is punctured, leading to a sudden and catastrophic influx of resonance entities into the city. 

- A world-destroying entity, its magnitude off the charts, becomes aware of the Shattered Isles. 

- A second cataclysm occurs. The sun is already destroyed—what happens this time? 

- The explorers discover that the Shattered Isles are not alone, and that they are one of several worlds circling a small, cold star. What discoveries might the other worlds hold? 

## **Questions for the GM** 

- How does the Ministry of Stability feel about the Blueraker Project? Does it threaten their own remit of security and stability? 

- The Palace has been left out of the loop on this. What will they do once they find out? 

- What do the Unseen intend to do with Blueraker 5? How does it further their goal of world domination? 

- The Blueraker 5 may have world-changing consequences. Will a time traveler from the future appear, to prevent catastrophe? 

## **Opportunities by Crew Type** 

**Dealers:** The Ministry of Discovery is moving a lot of product, which might either be competition for the crew or a ripe target. This could include alluvium, ultraplasm, echo-sensing arrays, gravitic inverters, a cocktail of drugs for the Blue Explorers, as well as a large stockpile of supplies for the trip, including a capsule of representative Shattered Isles culture, music, and art. 

**Hit Squad:** Many factions have their own goals for the Blueraker Project, and a Hit Squad could find themselves working for all sides in this chaotic conflict. 

**Militants:** Is the Enemy of the Cause involved? Which outcome for Blueraker 5 works best for your cause? Who will you work with? 

**Racers:** The Blueraker Project requires materials that are technically illegal, and so smugglers will be required. There is also scope for hijacking shipments of parts or plans. Finally, highly skilled drivers may find themselves headhunted as potential rocket ship pilots by any of the factions involved. 

**Shadows:** A crew of Shadows should find themselves easily drawn in—there are lots of parts, intel, and expensive technology to steal here, or to sabotage. All the spy agencies are very interested in the Blueraker Project. 

**Utopians:** Blueraker 5 promises to change the world, one way or the other—a crew of Utopians could use this as a golden opportunity to realize their Vision. 

277 

## **Hooks** 

- **The Alluvium Affair.** The crew have two mysterious items in the backseat— the canister of alluvium as normal, but also a briefcase containing the blueprints and mission parameters of the Blueraker 5 launch. Will they sell the information to the highest bidder? 

- **A Thousand Feet Above Doskvol.** Faction 2 is the Ministry of Discovery, or working for them. The airship utilized highly classified (and stolen) Blueraker technology, and so it had to be destroyed. Having seen this technology in action, now the PCs know too much. 

- **The Frame-Up.** The go-between was helping Section 6 infiltrate the Blueraker Project, and learned of the existence and involvement of the Unseen. Their death was to tidy up a loose end, and the PC crew were patsies to take the blame. The spy agency was just a pawn used by the Unseen to do this dirty work. 

- **Escaping the Mind’s Eye.** Add “location of the hidden launch facility for the Blueraker Project” to the list of secrets the PCs might know. One player must select it. Are the captors tying up loose ends to protect the Blueraker launch? Or are they trying to hijack the launch themselves, and need this information to further their goals? 

278 

279 

## The Hull Directive 

The Lusk Reform Technique turns a criminal into one of the Reformed and produces a hull to boot; is it a clever, efficient form of managing the criminal population, or a horrific crime against humanity? 

Reformed or not, hulls are used for more jobs around the city every day, putting more and more people out of work. Already the Rail Jacks and the Gondoliers have been made redundant, and rumor is the Bluecoats are next. 

## **Inciting Incident** 

**Lord Daros** , an influential member of the nobility and a prominent critic of the use of the hulls, has been found dead in the street. The death is a mystery, and the only witness was **GRD-9** , a street-sweeping hull that’s since gone missing. The tabloids blame GRD-9 for the murder, and angry citizens are rioting in the streets, demanding justice. 

## **Questions for the Players** 

- How has the life of someone you care about been negatively affected by hulls? 

- When did a hull do you a kindness that you still remember? 

- Who is someone you care about that got sent to the Lusk Reform Clinic? Where is their reformed, hollowed body now? 

## **Key NPCs** 

## **Anti-Hull:** 

- **Captain Gant** , riotcoat commander, **Bluecoats** . Gant has orders to quell the protests and riots, but would love nothing more than to stoke antihull sentiment. 

- **Kagney** , boss of the **Blackjacks** . Former Rail Jack put out of work by rail hulls, now gang boss. Will take any opportunity to smash hulls. 

- **Judith Sweetland** , warden of **Ironhook Prison** . Ironhook is the source of all Sweetland’s power and respectability, and she’ll do anything to stop the Lusk Reform Clinic from taking that away. 

- **Professor Kole** , spokesperson for the Burn Corps, a group of political radicals. The Burn Corps are involved in many of the protests. Kole is adamant that hulls have personhood, but that they should not be made in the first place; that they are a crime against humanity. Also staunchly anti-Bluecoat. 

280 

## **Pro-Hull:** 

- **Superintendent Clermont** , civilian head of the patrol hull division of the **Bluecoats** (also reports to the **Ministry of Stability** ). Their entire career depends on the continued proliferation of patrol hulls. 

- **Doctor Morcroft** , Director of the **Lusk Reform Clinic** . Terrifyingly cheerful. A fervent believer in the Lusk Reform Technique, totally committed to its success. 

- **Lord Dunvil** , Chief of Operations for the **Ministry of Stability** . Another hull proponent; he already rolled out hulls for rail security, and now has much bigger plans. Would love to take over the Lusk Reform Clinic and absorb it into the Ministry under his command. 

- **Croc** , sparktech for the **Golden Hand** . Croc sees hulls as the future, but not as tools—as the future for all humanity, living forever, never aging, never dying. 

- **Delta-986** and the **Dirt Barons** . Delta-986 is an awakened hull, and the Dirt Barons are very sympathetic to the hull cause. Their role as freelance intelligence operatives, however, makes them reluctant to attract attention. 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0291-07.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
10 1<br>9 2<br>8 3<br>7 4<br>6 5<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


## **The Countdown** 

Use a 10-segment clock to track this timebomb. Tick it when you update faction clocks as part of the Trouble Engine, or based on a fortune roll, or your narrative instincts, or any fictional events you deem relevant. 

As the clock fills, the following escalations happen: 

- **2 ticks.** Anti-hull protests (add the _Protests_ ongoing trouble). 

- **4 ticks.** Anti-hull riots (add the _Riots_ ongoing trouble). 

- **6 ticks.** Counterprotests and reactionary violence. 

- **7 ticks.** Hull victim caught in the middle of both sides. 

- **8 ticks.** A brutal crackdown by patrol hulls. 

- **9 ticks.** Backlash against riots fuels fast-tracking of the Lusk Reform Technique legislation, and it passes the vote. 

- **10 ticks.** The Lusk Reform Clinic is massively expanded, ushering in a new era of criminal reform and hull creation. 

281 

## **Questions for the GM** 

- Who killed Lord Daros, and why? What secret did Daros know? 

- What does GRD-9 know? Did they commit the murder, or were they framed? 

- Who benefits from this unrest? 

- Will one of the Lusk Reform Clinic’s rivals take them down? Perhaps the Ministry of Stability commandeers the clinic, or perhaps Ironhook Prison manages to discredit them. 

- The Dirt Barons are rumored to have intel on where GRD-9 is hiding. What push do the Barons need to get involved? 

## **Opportunities by Crew Type** 

**Dealers:** Is there a contraband product that the conflict makes valuable overnight—high-grade plasomoleum, hull capacitors, or a peculiar vice that hulls enjoy? How does the conflict impact business; a welcome distraction from the Bluecoats, or excessive chaos that’s bad for the bottom line? 

**Hit Squad:** Jobs against key targets on both sides of the conflict. Dealing with GRD-9; does the client want an accident, disappearance, murder, or ransom? Perhaps a rival faction starts using a hit squad of hulls; how does the crew deal with being replaced by machines themselves? 

**Militants:** Will you stand up for regular folks put out of work, or for the hulls themselves (caught in the middle of this ideological conflict)? Which side of the conflict is the Enemy of the Cause on? 

**Racers:** Smuggling hulls around the city, or out of the city. Hijacking a shipment of new hulls before they’re rolled out. Hot pursuit of an escaped hull. A mysterious hot-shot race-winning driver is revealed to be a hull. 

**Shadows:** Jobs stealing intel from both sides of the conflict (example intel: _plans to roll out more hulls, shocking secrets of the Lusk Reform Technique, evidence of hull crimes, evidence of hull humanity, evidence of treachery amongst allied factions_ ). Using the chaos of the conflict as cover for jewelry heists, art heists, etc. Perhaps a rival faction starts using a heist team of hulls; how does the crew deal with being replaced by machines themselves? 

**Utopians:** How do hulls figure into the utopian dream? Can the crew use the distraction of this conflict to advance their own agenda? How will riots and patrol hulls complicate their plans? If you need alluvium for your experiments, the Lusk Reform Clinic uses a lot of it; helping to shut them down might make more alluvium available, or maybe they’ll share some willingly in exchange for your help... 

282 

## **Hooks** 

- **The Alluvium Affair.** The crew have two mysterious items in the backseat— the canister of alluvium as normal, but also a cocktail napkin scrawled with the date and time for a rendezvous, in a few days, with GRD-9 (the missing suspect). Will they sell the information to the highest bidder? Will they go to the rendezvous themselves? Will GRD-9 be there, or is it a trap? 

- **A Thousand Feet Above Doskvol.** GRD-9 is on the airship, confused and afraid, and they beg for the crew to save them. They don’t have money, but they know things that would be worth money to the right people. Will they save GRD-9? What will they do with them after that? 

- **The Frame-Up.** The go-between was a witness to Lord Daros’s murder— perhaps they were even the assassin themself. Their death was to tidy up a loose end, and the PC crew were patsies to take the blame. The spy agency was just a pawn, used by the political heavyweight behind the killing of Lord Daros. The PCs were meant to be killed or arrested, and now the culprits will be coming for them next. 

- **Escaping the Mind’s Eye.** GRD-9’s soul is trapped in the resonance field as well. They appear as a human who has amnesia, doesn’t know their name, and hardly knows what’s going on. The captors are trying to find out what GRD-9 knows as well. Will the PCs help GRD-9 escape with them? Will they offer them as bait for the captors? Can they attune to realize GRD-9’s memories are locked behind a barrier—that could be broken? 

283 

## The Model Worker Initiative 

Satisfied with the success of their trials in Coalridge, the Ministry of Stability and several corporations plan to roll the initiative out to other districts. Total worker efficiency through surveillance, propaganda, and brainwashing. Where will it end? Can it be stopped? 

## **Inciting Incident** 

Xantara Pharm send an Assaying Unit to lay groundwork in the crew’s local district. Add the _Sharks in the Water_ ongoing trouble to the table. Ministry of Stability propaganda posters start appearing everywhere. 

This is just the beginning. 

## **Questions for the Players** 

- Who is someone you care about that lives and works in Coalridge? How have they been affected by the Model Worker Initiative experiments there? 

- What work did you do in Coalridge, for a time? Why did you quit? How did you escape? 

- What secrets do you have that could be exposed under a surveillance state? 

- Who is someone you care about that was a staunch critic of the initiative, until they were converted into a fanatical advocate? How do you suspect they were converted? 

## **Key NPCs** 

**Hatcher** , head of a private security firm employed by the **Ministry of Stability** . A true believer in the Model Worker Initiative, and a key part of its implementation in Coalridge. 

**Canden Xantara** , the heir of **Xantara Pharm** . Erratic and narcissistic, Canden has been put in charge of the roll-out in this district to keep them out of the way of other, more important business. Ambitious and impulsive. Wants a big success here to prove their worth to Yugo Xantara. 

**Coldwell** , Director of Success within **New Dawn** . A high-ranking member of the cult, beaming with energy. Sees the Model Worker Initiative as an important channel to bring new converts to New Dawn, but would rather cut out the other factions involved entirely. 

**Lady Bowmore** , executive officer in charge of the **Ministry of Stability’s** affairs in Doskvol. A focused and terrifyingly effective person, although this particular roll-out is only one project out of many under her oversight. 

**“Horror” Horriston** , infamous fixer for **Strangford-Michter Financial** . Seen snooping around the local district in recent weeks. Strangford-Michter 

284 

Financial would love nothing more than to humiliate Xantara Pharm with a public failure... 

**Shapcott** , legendary reporter for the **Inklane Tabloids** . There are some heavyhitters involved in the Model Worker Initiative, and it would be very dangerous to upset them with an exposé—but that would never stop a tough old hack like Shapcott. 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0295-03.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
10 1<br>9 2<br>8 3<br>7 4<br>6 5<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


## **The Countdown** 

Use a 10-segment clock to track this timebomb. Tick it when you update faction clocks as part of the Trouble Engine, or based on a fortune roll, or your narrative instincts, or any fictional events you deem relevant. 

As the clock fills, the following escalations happen: 

- **2 ticks.** Security cameras are installed on every street corner. Any scores in this district take **+1 Heat** from now on. 

- **4 ticks.** Xantara Pharm vending dispensaries appear across the district, with prescriptions filled for each employee based on their personal productivity assessment. One of the crew’s contacts becomes dazed by their mandated pill regimen, and is useless until they’re helped off it. 

- **6 ticks.** New Dawn sends in recruiters and starts broadcasting regular wellness parables through loudspeakers. Which of your friends or contacts becomes an initiate? 

- **7 ticks.** Crowd Surveyors are installed. Each is a mechanical red eye that scans the streets and records worker movements. All scores in this district generate +2 Heat ( **+3 Heat total** ) from now on. 

- **8 ticks.** The local citizens push back. Add the _Rioting_ ongoing trouble. Will the crew help? 

- **9 ticks.** A contact or friend disappears, taken by enforcers of the Model Worker Initiative. Add the _Disappearance_ ongoing trouble. 

- **10 ticks.** The Model Worker Initiative is instituted in full in the crew’s local district, a totalitarian system of worker control. All scores in this district generate +3 Heat ( **+6 Heat total** ) from now on. 

285 

## **Questions for the GM** 

- Why did they choose this district? Is there something they want here, or something they want to suppress? 

- Can the efforts be redirected to another district, either by making it too difficult here, or more enticing elsewhere? 

- What grassroots groups oppose the initiative? Can they be organized into an effective resistance? 

- Is there any tension between the Model Worker Initiative’s factions; the Ministry of Stability, Xantara Pharm, and New Dawn? How can this tension be heightened and exploited? 

- How do the spy agencies feel about the initiative? They require shadows to operate in, and total surveillance would work against them. Do they have a hand to play here? 

## **Opportunities by Crew Type** 

**Dealers:** This situation is going to be bad for business, no doubt about that. How will the crew balance the priorities of getting their enterprise up and running vs. stopping this encroaching totalitarianism? 

**Hit Squad:** Jobs against key targets, either members of the resistance or those working for the initiative. Internecine conflict between members of the initiative, working for one corporation against another. 

**Militants:** Is the Enemy of the Cause involved? Will you put aside your wider cause to help with this one? 

**Racers:** Smuggling contraband into the district, or smuggling fleeing workers out. Hijacking a shipment of initiative equipment before it’s installed. Racing is banned in the district under the Model Worker Initiative; how will the crew respond? 

**Shadows:** Plenty of opportunities to steal intel from those behind the initiative. In all other respects, this situation will be bad for heist opportunities. Will the team take time off heists to put a stop to all this? 

**Utopians:** Whatever future they’re building with the initiative, it is not your Utopian Vision. How will you advance your own agenda under the boot of total surveillance? Can you subvert the initiative to your own ends? 

286 

## **Hooks** 

- **The Alluvium Affair.** The crew get a second glimpse of the future, before they hand over the alluvium toward the end of the score. In this vision, they see themselves in beige jumpsuits at an assembly line with hundreds of other glassy-eyed workers, with an ominous mechanical red eye watching over from above. This vision is a warning of a potential future; can they stop it coming to pass? 

Ask each player what their character looks like in this glimpse of the future, under the total control of corporate overlords. 

- **A Thousand Feet Above Doskvol.** Faction 2 is either one of the initiative’s main factions (Xantara Pharm, New Dawn, the Ministry of Stability), or working for them. Taking out this vice-smuggling operation is part of laying the groundwork for the Model Worker Initiative. Now that the PCs are witnesses, they’ll either have to be converted to the cause or taken out of action. 

- **The Frame-Up.** The go-between knew a secret about the Model Worker Initiative that could cause a scandal, maybe even cause the Initiative to be shut down. Their death was to tidy up a loose end, and the PC crew were patsies to take the blame. The spy agency was just a pawn used by one of the Initiative factions (Ministry of Stability, New Dawn, or Xantara Pharm). The PCs were meant to be killed or arrested, and now the culprits will be coming for them next. 

- **Escaping the Mind’s Eye.** Add these options to the list of secrets the PCs might know. Ask at least one player to select one of them. 

- Location of the formula Xantara Pharm uses for the worker subjugation program. 

- A mole inside the Ministry of Stability. 

Are the captors shoring up vulnerabilities to ensure the rollout does not encounter any unforeseen complications? Or are they trying to sabotage the Initiative and need the PCs’ knowledge to foil them? 

287 

## Minutes to Midnight 

Tensions between Blackthorn Park and the Palace are rapidly escalating, threatening to tip the Imperium and United Skov Covenant into open warfare—Unity War IV. Both factions are being secretly manipulated by a third party with their own agenda, hoping to capitalize on the chaos of global conflict. 

## **Inciting Incident** 

Brigadier Colwick, a high-ranking Imperial Military officer visiting the city on official business, is killed. The Palace believes that Blackthorn Park is behind the assassination, and the Crown demands immediate retaliation. 

## **Questions for the Players** 

- Who is someone you care about who has done clerical work for the Palace? 

- What sympathies do you have toward the United Skov Covenant? Is it because of friends, family, ideology, or paranormal experience? 

- Who is someone you care about who has been an informant for Blackthorn Park? 

- Why does the Palace consider you a dependable and patriotic citizen? 

## **Next Steps** 

The early stages of this ticking timebomb should focus on pulling the PCs into the middle of the escalating conflict between Blackthorn Park and the Palace, with the crew used as a disposable pawn by both sides. The PCs might find themselves putting out fires to slow the countdown toward world war—exposing double agents, extracting hostages or defectors, sabotaging or destroying key sites, and so on. 

As the campaign progresses, they start to sense the Spider’s web around them. Now they’re still fighting fires of the main countdown, but they’re also investigating the truth of Project Midnight. Installing bugs, following key targets, stealing intel, and so on. 

## **Key NPCs** 

**Silk** , a mysterious and legendary thief. It’s a coincidence that the top secret project is called the Silk Protocol; Silk the thief is a red herring. If Silk learns of all this, though, they will be keen to get involved and might be a useful ally to the PCs. They will perform an ostentatious theft at the worst possible time. 

**Khuran** , surveillance officer with the **Anixis Field Unit** . Has collected extensive intelligence on Brigadier Colwick’s death and crime scene. The Anixis Field Unit does not want to see Unity War IV happen, but they also don’t want to draw too much Heat from either Blackthorn Park or the Palace. 

288 

**The Dirt Barons** , freelance information brokers. Can act as a fence to arrange payment for intel. They may also have some early information on the Spider’s web, such as what the Silk Protocol really is. 

**Ms. Asta** , controller for **Blackthorn Park** . Suspects that they’re being played, but this is a deadly game and she can’t risk letting Palace aggression go unchecked. 

**Prichard** , handler for the **Palace** . Suspects they’re being played, but Prichard understands their priorities—beat Blackthorn Park first, anything else comes a distant second. 

**Baine** , the best spy working for the **Palace** . Baine is secretly a double agent in deep cover, working for Blackthorn Park. This is currently only known by Ms. Asta. If it is revealed, can Baine ever be trusted? Perhaps they’re a triple agent, with their true loyalty remaining with the Crown. Whatever the case, they have a wider perspective on the espionage war than almost anybody. 

**Kessarin** , agent for the **Strelai** . The mysterious order known as the Strelai typically stay out of mundane espionage activities, but Project Midnight threatens the stability of reality itself. Kessarin is on the case, though prefers to work alone. 

**The Milliner** , an unassuming hat-maker who works from a small backroom amidst the busy tailors of Charterhall. A well-respected, truly neutral information broker. If anyone knows some of the deeper particulars of the Spider’s web, it would be them. 

**Silver** . The pianist at Paddles, an exclusive private members club frequented by the most powerful politicians and bureaucrats in the city. Long-standing informant working for Blackthorn Park. Likely to become compromised (burned) as the timebomb advances, and Blackthorn Park may want to tie up loose ends. Silver suspects they know who the Spider is, but hasn’t told anyone. 

**Halsey** . A virtuoso Skov cryptographer and mathematician. Worked on Project Midnight before becoming disillusioned by the project’s terrible nature and fleeing into hiding. 

**Hellyers** , City Councilor and weapon manufacturing magnate. A very wealthy and amoral individual with hawkish views, always advocating for more Akorosi aggression and escalation against the USC. Secretly helping to fund Project Midnight. Possibly an asset working for the Spider. 

**Murton** , manager of a factory in Coalridge that secretly works on key parts of Project Midnight. Knows more than they should. Likely to turn up dead. 

289 


![](Blades_Markdown_Reader/images/blades68_v0.9.5_textonly.pdf-0300-01.png)


**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
10 1<br>9 2<br>8 3<br>7 4<br>6 5<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>


## **The Countdown** 

Use a 10-segment clock to track this timebomb. Tick it when you update faction clocks as part of the Trouble Engine, or based on a fortune roll, or your narrative instincts, or any fictional events you deem relevant. 

As the clock fills, the following escalations happen: 

- **2 ticks.** Foreign consulates increase security. Extra espionage personnel are brought into the city by all spy agencies. 

- **3 ticks.** Consul-General Kalmark, head of the USC consulate in Doskvol, is found dead. 

- **4 ticks.** Remaining USC consulate staff are expelled from Akoros. Official diplomatic channels go silent. Covert channels heat up. Military presence at the North Hook camp is increased. 

- **5 ticks.** Student protests erupt, possibly funded or stoked by covert operators. Add the _Protests_ ongoing trouble. Known informants disappear. 

- **6 ticks.** Unmarked vans are a common sight in Doskvol. Many phone lines are bugged as routine surveillance. All scores generate **+1 Heat** . A diplomatic summit collapses publicly. 

- **7 ticks.** Foreign consulates are locked down, becoming fortified bunkers. A USC warship is anchored near Imperial waters. A contact or friend disappears, taken to a black site (add the _Disappearance_ ongoing trouble). 

- **8 ticks.** Military and Bluecoats are on high alert, with extra personnel brought into the city. Curfew declared. All scores generate **+3 Heat** (+4 Heat total). 

- **9 ticks.** Foreign consulates are evacuated. Martial law declared, with tanks and soldiers a common sight on the streets of Doskvol. 

- **10 ticks.** Unity War IV declared between the Imperium and the USC. Project Midnight is activated. 

290 

## **The Spider’s Web** 

While other ticking timebombs are an explosive but open-ended situation that escalates in the background of the campaign, _Minutes to Midnight_ is more complex. The following sequence of discoveries can be scattered in front of the players via scores, gather information rolls, long-term projects, NPCs, etc. The players should still drive the action, and what they do with this intel is up to them. 

As the ticking timebomb advances and tensions rise dangerously high, the players are untangling an increasingly dangerous knot. Can they unravel the conspiracy before the timebomb explodes? 

- **SILK.** A codeword so highly classified that anybody who learns it is likely to be killed. _Perhaps Brigadier Colwick was found clutching a napkin in his dead fingers, scrawled with this one word._ 

- **SILK refers to the Silk Protocol.** A codename for a codename. Very few know exactly what it means, but some know it’s a top secret Imperial initiative. _The “Hour of Silk” is midnight, by the Akorosi time-keeping system, and the Silk Protocol is a codename for Project Midnight._ 

- **Project Midnight is a dangerous proposal.** Only the highest echelons of the Imperial apparatus know the details of Project Midnight—the First Speaker, Section 6’s Overseer, the Director of the Imperial Intelligence Agency. They tell their direct reports, such as Prichard, that the project is theoretical—a contingency plan, an academic exercise. _The PCs learn that Project Midnight is a dangerous but theoretical threat._ 

- **Project Midnight is real.** The PCs find evidence that Project Midnight is not just a proposal—the project is underway, perhaps even right under their noses in Doskvol. Even worse, it’s almost ready. 

- **Project Midnight has a mole.** Evidence that this most top secret of top secret projects has been compromised by a third party, “the Spider”— neither Imperial nor Skov. The Spider has assets in place to take over Project Midnight after it is launched. 

- **Blackthorn Park and the Palace are being manipulated.** Evidence that everything from the death of Brigadier Colwick to the many escalations since have been the work of the Spider, stoking conflict to ensure that Project Midnight is finished and launched. 

- **Minutes to Midnight.** Now that the PCs know everything, they have to scramble before the ticking timebomb finishes. Can they find Project Midnight, figure out the activation protocol, convince both Blackthorn Park and the Palace that they are being manipulated, and finally stop the Spider before they bring about a second apocalypse? 

291 

## **What is Project Midnight?** 

Start with a loose idea for Project Midnight, and allow it become more concrete as the campaign progresses. This lets you adapt it to fit the PCs, their themes and relationships, and the factions they seem interested in. Your choice will also greatly influence the tone of your campaign, from the more plausible to the more outlandish. 

- **Weapon of Mass Destruction.** Something like a nuclear weapon, but with a paranormal element. Unity War III ended with the creation of the eerie Null Zone, wiping out part of Akoros and Iruvia. Perhaps this is a version of the same weapon, device, or ritual. 

- **Mega Hull, and/or Weaponized Leviathan.** Perhaps Project Midnight is a hull of colossal size, powered by an obscene number of echoes. Or maybe it’s an attempt to bring a leviathan back and harness it—a _Blades_ version of a kaiju. Perhaps the project is both an unleashed leviathan and a hull to counter it, or the combination of them in one form. 

- **The Red Queen Protocol.** Whether because of religious beliefs or out of ruthless brutality, Project Midnight might involve summoning a forgotten god into this world, in all their terrible glory. 

- **The Emperor Returned.** Perhaps the Immortal Emperor was killed a hundred years ago (see Sean Nittner’s _Broken Spire_ ), and the Crown has been empty ever since, leading to the Imperium’s steady decline. Project Midnight creates fractures in the resonance field that open to the world of a hundred years ago. They have an antique Imperial airship, the _Verdict_ , in a top secret hangar; Imperial scientists pulled it through a fracture. They want to bring the Immortal Emperor through too, along with his arsenal of war hulls, battleships, and experimental airships, to reassert the Imperium’s control over all the Shattered Isles once and for all. 

## **Who is the Spider?** 

As with the nature of Project Midnight, start with a loose idea for the Spider (the third party provoking Blackthorn Park and the Palace into a war). Adapt the truth to fit your PCs and your campaign, as it unfolds, for maximum dramatic impact. Some ideas are presented here. Each lists a foreshadowing clue that you could drop in at the start, with the death of Brigadier Colwick; perhaps sprinkle in a few clues, and some of them can end up as red herrings. 

- **The Tower** (#1), leader of **the Unseen** . The Unseen have achieved ultimate power in Doskvol, controlling the factions of the city like puppets, and the next step is global domination. _**Goal** : world domination._ _**Clue** : witnesses have unexplained gaps in their memory._ 

292 

- A member of **Rowan House** (see the Church faction description, page 354). Rowan House is a powerful secret society caught in an existential battle for its own supremacy across time and space. Project Midnight may be its key to victory. _**Goal** : world domination._ _**Clue** : a small plant growing in a pot, left at the scene of the crime_ — _a rowan sapling._ 

- **Eshala Ankhayat** , of the **Ankhayat Consortium** . Tired of trying to enlist the help of one power or another to restore her house to power in Iruvia, Eshala decides to take matters into her own hands. _**Goal** : destroy the other great powers, take over Iruvia, reign supreme._ _**Clue** : a casino chip from the Iruvian Sands casino._ 

- **Karstas** , Lead Experimentalist of **Mirror House** . This leads to further questions, of course—are Mirror House visitors from beyond the Blue, or are they the PCs from the future, or are they the current form of the Reconciled, the Path of Echoes, or the Dimmer Sisters? If you choose this faction, Karstas, when revealed as the Spider, should have a much higher Tier than Mirror House. _**Goal** : destroy the world to build something new._ _**Clue** : a mirror at the scene of the crime behaves strangely; living people don’t appear in it at all._ 

- **Castelle Fane** , CEO of **Strangford-Michter Financial** . Since SMF moved into their new HQ in Comber House, Castelle Fane has been acting increasingly erratically. _**Goal** : vast amounts of money from war-profiteering for Strangford-Michter Financial, and a more occult goal for Castelle Fane— perhaps a dreaming leviathan, or the Red Queen, or even the Immortal Emperor has been whispering in her ear._ _**Clue** : the real killer is a former employee of Ironclad Security, an outfit owned (through a series of multiple subsidiaries) by Strangford-Michter Financial._ 

- **Mahia Salang** , leader of the **Golden Hand** . Mahia came to Doskvol as a refugee from the Daggerite banyan of Biringan. She has built a successful criminal syndicate, but her real goal has always been nothing less than bringing down the great powers that have led to so much strife in her homeland. If you choose this faction, Mahia, when revealed as the Spider, should have a much higher Tier than the Golden Hand. _**Goal** : bring down the great powers, free the Dagger Isles._ _**Clue** : jasmine flowers, an important component of many Daggerite funerary rites._ 

- **Chago** , head of the **SCORPION Syndicate** . In his youth, Chago fought for a Severosi separatist group. They were crushed by the Imperium in the Sevrin Invasion. Chago has since built a very powerful smuggling operation, but his real goal is, and has always been, destroying the Imperium and freeing Severos. _**Goal** : bring down the great powers, free Severos._ _**Clue** : residue of a black resin under the fingernails_ — _black lotus._ 

293 

## **Opportunities by Crew Type** 

**Hit Squads** , **Militants** , **Racers** , and **Shadows** are all perfectly well-suited to this ticking timebomb, doing jobs for and against Blackthorn Park and the Palace before they realize the true stakes of the situation. 

**Utopians** may be interested in the outcome of Project Midnight, and they may want to co-opt it to their own ends and their Utopian Vision. 

While the core activity of **Dealers** may be less relevant, it’s highly likely that one or more PCs will have ties to the Palace and/or Blackthorn Park, which could enmesh the whole crew. The real world is full of examples of intelligence agencies using illegal dealers for their own ends. 

Whatever the crew type, give them space to pursue their own goals and claims outside of this ticking timebomb. The PCs should still drive the narrative through their actions. It’s your job, as GM, to weave Project Midnight and the espionage cold war through the scores and events, whatever they may be. 

## **Hooks** 

- **The Alluvium Affair:** The PCs have both the canister of alluvium and the dead body of Brigadier Colwick in the back seat of their autopod. Now the Palace believes that they are assassins working for Blackthorn Park. Can they clear their name? Who is Brigadier Colwick, and why are they dead? Scatter some potential clues that might foreshadow the Spider’s identity (to be revealed much later in the campaign). 

- **A Thousand Feet Above Doskvol:** An irregularity in the product on display in the airship; there’s a message hidden inside—“SILK.” Since the message has been read, the airship and its occupants must be destroyed. Later, the PCs learn about the death of Brigadier Colwick, and the word “SILK” clutched in his hand. What does it all mean? 

- **The Frame-Up:** The go-between was saying something about “SILK” when the safe exploded. Later, the PCs learn about the death of Brigadier Colwick, and the word “SILK” clutched in his hand. The spy agency involved is being manipulated by the Spider, and the PCs are just pawns in the game. Scatter some potential clues that might foreshadow the Spider’s identity (to be revealed much later in the campaign). 

- **Escaping the Mind’s Eye:** The PCs encounter the fading echo of Brigadier Colwick inside the resonance field. He introduces himself and tells them one word, “SILK,” before he vanishes. Now they know too much, and the Spider will be coming for them. 

294 

295 

## Invasion from Another World 

Reality Wardens are terrifying and inscrutable. Their technological marvels make them alert to any deviations from Reality Constancy Law. They seem to be everywhere at once, ever-vigilant and always watching, impossible to deceive or evade. What only a few know is, they are only holding on to our reality by a thread. 

The resonance field is connected to another living world, one which Section 6 believes is antithetical to our own. Reality Wardens have made a concerted effort to prevent traffic between the worlds. Over the last few years, however, more and more factions are meddling with the resonance field, conducting increasingly dangerous experiments. Now, the rift between worlds threatens to tear wide open, leading to a full-scale invasion. 

## **Inciting Incident** 

Professor **Dorresti Yal** , a visiting Tycherosi scholar, was giving a guest lecture at Charterhall University on the nature of void spaces when they disintegrated in front of a hall of 300 students. They took with them two students who had volunteered to partake in the demonstration: Weston Strangford and Anya Hellyers. 

The real Professor Yal was found tied up in their apartment later that day. The presentation, and what might have been a kidnapping, was done by a doppelganger. Add the _Paranormal Activity_ ongoing trouble to the table. 

## **Questions for the Players** 

- One of you has a doppelganger from the other world. What efforts has it made to replace you? 

- Who is someone you care about that you’ve lost? How far would you go to get them back? 

- What’s the name of the student you know who saw the whole thing? What obvious lies were they told to explain the anomaly? 

## **Key NPCs** 

- **Dr. Blackburn** , a brilliant scientist with the **Tomorrow Program** . Though her methods are controversial, she believes in studying the harmonic resonance differences between people from this world and the next. She may be able to find a way to open portals to new worlds entirely. 

296 

- **Ixis-9** , the sparkmind construct that provides **Mirror House** analytical and computing capabilities. Has been studying the resonance echoes of patrons of the Blue Baths (page 406). Though the members of Mirror House, including its leader Karstas, use the baths to gather secrets from unsuspecting echoes, Ixis-9 has been covertly using the technology to send messages to its counterpart in the other world. 

- **Veil** , Reality Warden with **Section 6** . Leader of the RCL (Reality Constancy Law) division, they have been granted visions (some say directly from the Crown) of key individuals who cannot cross the threshold, as their presence would create a conduit to the other world. Among them are Lynthia Rowan and Roslyn Dimmer. 

- **Thistle** , an assassin working for the **Palace** . Tasked with eliminating any “strangers” found in Doskvol. Has been equipped with an experimental resonance scanner that can supposedly identify creatures from other worlds at short range, though its accuracy is unknown. 

- **Dorji Kon** , fixer for the SCORPION Syndicate. Has made a deal with **Castelle Fane** , CEO of **Strangford-Michter Financial** , to provide a cheap and expendable labor force by smuggling people from the other world. Dorji doesn’t know the details, only that Castelle keeps bringing people from Comber House who are eager to stay below the radar, and will work for next to nothing. 

- **Estelle Rowan** , matriarch of **Rowan House** . Operates from the other side of a time anomaly, in old Doskvol. She has found the means to reach forward in time to 968 and retroactively instantiate her house as a major player in the City Council. 

- **Sergeant Vran** , a recalcitrant Bluecoat, has been given a list of arrests to make with no explanation as to why, or what crimes they are guilty of. A constant thorn in the side of his superiors; he knows this is punishment. 

- **Manston** , the Security Operations Director for the **Ministry of Stability** . As if worker rights and people’s riots weren’t troubling enough, Manston has just learned about many unauthorized individuals on Imperium soil who aren’t paying taxes.

## **The Countdown** 

Use a 10-segment clock to track this timebomb. Tick it when you update faction clocks as part of the Trouble Engine, or based on a fortune roll, or your narrative instincts, or any fictional events you deem relevant. 

As the clock fills, the following escalations happen: 

- **2 ticks.** Strangers wearing archaic clothing spotted in Six Towers. They catch the attention of the Evening Whisper, one of the Ink Lane Tabloids. 

- **4 ticks.** Portions of Six Towers and Brightstone are cordoned off by Section 6. Add the _No-Go Zone_ ongoing trouble. 

- **6 ticks.** Widespread arrest warrants are issued, and the Bluecoats are granted clemency on any extreme measures required carrying them out. All scores generate **+1 Heat** . 

- **7 ticks.** Rowan House (Tier 5) has retroactively weaved a web of worldwide control, including occupying two seats on the City Council (replacing Clelland and Tyrconnell). See the Church (page 354) for more details. 

- **8 ticks.** Ink Lane Tabloids and credible sources alike feature “Alien Invasion” on front pages. Panic ensues. Add the _Rioting_ ongoing trouble. 

- **9 ticks.** Open fighting breaks out in the City Council. Major Fellows of the Imperial Military shuts down Gaddoc Station and places Doskvol under martial law. All scores generate a further **+1 Heat** (+2 Heat total). 

- **10 ticks.** A leviathan from the past breaches through the rift and topples the Bellweather Electroplasmic Fusion Station. Darkness falls. 

## **Questions for the GM** 

- Is there just one other world, or are there many? Are they time-locked with Doskvol, or do the portals lead to many different times and places? 

- Which of the existing anomalies (the Null Zone, the Mire, and others) are portals to other worlds? Who or what controls when they open? 

- Do the other worlds truly seek invasion? Or are they fleeing from somewhere even worse than the Shattered Isles? 

- Which of the PCs have doppelgangers? What do they want from them? 

298 

- _Blades in the Dark: Deep Cuts_ contains a catalyst called “The Other Living World” that could be used to explore the other side of this invasion. You could play one side as a prequel campaign to the other, or alternate games until they cross over and collide in an explosive fashion; ’68 characters in old Doskvol, Blades characters in ’68, and finally everyone all together. 

## **Opportunities by Crew Type** 

**Dealers:** There are new markets for your products. How will you capture them before others do? What might be brought from the other side of the rift that you could corner the market on if you get to it first? 

**Hit Squad:** As the countdown increases, the desperation to eliminate or capture strangers will increase. Conversely, some of the doppelgangers will need important people removed so they can take their place. Neither side is likely to reveal their motives. 

**Militants:** Is the Enemy of the Cause involved? Will you put aside your wider cause to help with this one? Does the world from the other side represent freedom from tyranny, or even worse subjugation? 

**Racers:** Smuggling people in and out of restricted zones has never been more lucrative. 

**Shadows:** Alluvium is in higher demand than ever. There are stockpiles all throughout the city that are fiercely guarded, but with the demand as high as it is, it might be worth the risk. There’s also the question of who is really who, and you might be the best people to figure it out—for the right buyer. 

**Utopians:** What calls to you from the other side of the void? How do the dark visions you’ve received affect your Utopian Vision? Who from the other side might be the missing link? 

## **Hooks** 

- **The Alluvium Affair:** The authorities chasing the PCs are Section 6, and they suspect that the anomaly was a portal to the other world. Are the PCs really the PCs, or are they their own doppelgangers? 

- **A Thousand Feet Above Doskvol:** The airship is smuggling a person wearing archaic clothing from 100 years ago. Section 6 blows it up. 

- **The Frame-Up:** The go-between was a doppelganger, and the spy agency was just a pawn used by Section 6. 

- **Escaping the Mind’s Eye:** Inside the resonance field, the PCs encounter the echo of Professor Yal’s doppelganger ushering the echoes of Weston Strangford and Anya Hellyers through a portal. The hostages plead for rescue from the PCs, before they disappear from this world. 

299 

## ART PLACEHOLDER 

300 

## A Brief History 

oskvol is a city at the crossroads. In the Unity Era, it was one of the most important cities in the Imperium, the home of the lucrative D leviathan hunter fleets. That industry has vanished, but the vast wealth it generated means that Doskvol is still one of the great cities of the world. Money attracts money, which attracts people. Several global corporations have their headquarters here, and tourists flock to the city. 

Officially, Imperial ministries still use the Unity Era Calendar (counting years since the first Unity War ended), but everyone else in Akoros and the rest of the world have settled on a simple system of Pre-Cataclysm (PC) and AfterCataclysm (AC). The confusing dates on ministry documents and forms are seen as a classic example of confounding governmental bureaucracy. The current year is 968 AC.

302 

## Bluetime 

In the heart of Doskvol is the Bellweather Electroplasmic Fusion Station. This station powers the city and generates the Bubble, a field of invisible energy that surrounds the city, protecting it from the reality-warping terrors of the deathlands beyond. This electroplasmic force field is much more effective than the lightning barriers of old, and unsanctioned intrusions are very rare. The city has been drenched in paranormal activity for centuries, however, and there is plenty of latent supernatural phenomena to keep Section 6 busy, even though the Bubble keeps new horrors out. 

The Bubble is mostly invisible, except when it crackles with electroplasm as it vaporizes some unnatural entity from beyond. Transit in or out of the Bubble is only possible through one of a few gates; circular steel apertures sized to allow trains, airships, and sea vessels. Smaller human-sized gates are rumored to exist, but access is highly classified and controlled. 

Attached to the Fusion Station is the B.L.U.E. Array, an apparatus of sleek, curving metal that soars into the sky overhead. This experimental device “tunes” the Bubble, causing its invisible surface to ripple with psychedelic colors before settling into a cerulean blue. In the sky is a bright, white orb—the sun. This state is known as “bluetime.” 

Although weather intrudes and rainy days are possible, make no mistake— bluetime is real daylight. Plants that struggled to survive on the old shards of the sun or unsettling radiant energy now bloom and thrive under beaming warm sunlight. Tourists get tans, and even sunburn. 

The exact mechanics of bluetime are a closely guarded secret, and may not even be known to the scientists who invented it. Does it simply focus the shards of the sun like a magnifying glass, or is it projecting a very advanced form of radiant energy? Some say it opens a portal to another dimension, or another time. 

## **Bluetime and the Paranormal** 

Scientists have noted that paranormal effects become somewhat muted during bluetime—there are fewer paranormal sightings reported, and lab experiments have shown that anomaly effects are dampened. 

When the B.L.U.E. Array is switched off, however, it’s like unstopping a cork—paranormal energy floods back in. The psychedelic twilight hours when bluetime is powering up or down are particularly erratic and paranormally charged. 

303 

## Life in ’68 

Doskvol in ’68 is a place of contrasts. On the one hand, it’s the Swinging Sixties and this city is the cultural epicenter. Fashion, music, art, and politics are being radically challenged and reshaped in exciting new ways. Walk down Apple Lane in Crowfoot and you’ll experience a kaleidoscope of advertising, jangling pop music, velvet jackets, geometric prints, and young people everywhere dancing, talking, and laughing under a bright blue sky. 

But the present is built on the bones of the past, and those bones are made up of narrow alleys, crumbling brick tenement buildings, and a thick haze of exhaust smog. Behind the colorful billboards, Old Duskwall is still there, grim and brooding. Those shadows are where the game of espionage is played, and life in Doskvol is shot through with an undercurrent of paranoia and fear. 

The Age of Consensus has been one of safety and stability for those in the Imperium, but also one of conformity and control. That status quo is being challenged; through protests, riots, music, and art. The question at the heart of it all is this: _what comes next?_ Is there a better world being born, or is this the high-water mark? The forces of the establishment have started to understand the groundswell of change—will they lower the boot and snuff it out, or have they left it too late? 

## **Travel** 

Thanks to high-speed trains, airships, and wireless communication, the Bubble-cities of Akoros are more connected than they’ve ever been. Free communication and travel remain privileges of the wealthy, however; the Ministry of Stability is responsible for border security and transportation between cities and takes this task very seriously. All communication is monitored, and censored where necessary, and inter-city travel requires a variety of paperwork and expensive permits. 

There are a variety of public transportation options inside Doskvol, including gondolas on the many canals (whether human-piloted or automated), monorail lines, old rail lines, and buses. 

## **Autopods** 

Steam cars were first invented during the Unity Era, but they struggled to gain widespread traction; the old, narrow streets were not built for large vehicles. Autocycles, a two-wheeled vehicle powered by a plasmic turbine engine, proved to be much more popular and successful. New models were introduced, some with three wheels, then four, and then with enclosed cockpits. This led to the evolution of the autopod as we know it—a small but robust pod-like vehicle that can navigate even the maze-like alleys of Doskvol. 

304 

As the autopod gained popularity, Doskvol has been gradually revamped with freeways and overpasses, leading to more and bigger autopods. 

Perhaps in another world without a cataclysm, people would not be so drawn to an unsafe and inefficient mode of transport that relies on a volatile fuel source distilled from the death of living things. Alas, this is the world of the Shattered Isles, and everyone loves their autopod. 

## **Airships** 

Airships are a common sight in the skies above Doskvol. The searchlights on Bluecoat patrol ships cut through the darkness of the poorer districts. Large warships, bristling with cannons and coilguns, come to refuel at the military camp near Dunslough. Luxury passenger airships dock at Penderyn Air Terminal in Brightstone. Cargo ships unload at Gaddoc Station. 

The North Hook Military Camp also houses a few squadrons of turbofighters, which can deploy from the larger warships. A turbofighter is one big plasmic turbine engine with wings, built for air superiority—outmaneuvering cumbersome airships and intercepting enemy turbofighters. 

305 

## **Technology** 

The world is full of exciting new inventions—telephones, huge computing machines, color plasmovision, portable radios, not to mention the astounding experiments showcased by the Ministry of Discovery, like flying autopods and jetpacks. 

This progress is not widely distributed, however. Offices still rely entirely on mountains of paperwork; office life is marked by the clatter of typewriters and the sharp smell of toner and ink. Mimeograph machines and dot matrix printers spew yet more paper, filling endless ledger books and filing cabinets. Telephones have a rotary dial and are not portable in any way, requiring switchboard operators and manual exchanges. Technology is still, in many ways, clunky and manual. 

As a general rule, if any piece of technology existed in the late ’60s or early ’70s in the real world, it probably exists in Doskvol ’68 in some form. 

## **Media** 

Radio, plasmovision, film, and music are a huge part of modern life. The Ministry of Stability monitors and censors all broadcasts, but artists and pirates are always pushing the boundaries of what is acceptable. 

## **Bands** 

- _The Silver Echoes_ , pop music 

- _The Electroplasmic Caravan_ , psychedelia 

- _The Rivingtons_ , crooners 

- Sylvia Carrow, folk singer 

## **Radio Shows** 

- _Gavel_ , Bluecoat procedural drama 

- _Hour of Flame_ , hard-hitting interviews 

- _Radio Tangletown_ , a pirate radio station 

## **Plasmovision Shows** 

- _Citadel 9_ , dystopian sci-fi drama 

- _The Laughing Crown_ , soft political satire 

- _Lightning Hook_ , historical drama about a whisper who investigates crimes
